## 6. Bhesajjakkhandhako

6.The Chapter on Medicines

### 160. Pañcabhesajjakathā ^1

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv6-brahmali-pali#^1|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch5|BMC Chapter 5]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-MV6.1" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


160.The Discourse on the Five Medicines

260. Tena samayena buddho bhagavā sāvatthiyaṃ viharati jetavane anāthapiṇḍikassa ārāme. Tena kho pana samayena bhikkhūnaṃ sāradikena ābādhena phuṭṭhānaṃ yāgupi pītā uggacchati, bhattampi bhuttaṃ uggacchati. Te tena kisā honti, lūkhā, dubbaṇṇā, uppaṇḍuppaṇḍukajātā, dhamanisanthatagattā. Addasā kho bhagavā te bhikkhū kise lūkhe dubbaṇṇe uppaṇḍuppaṇḍukajāte dhamanisanthatagatte, disvāna āyasmantaṃ ānandaṃ āmantesi – ‘‘kiṃ nu kho, ānanda, etarahi bhikkhū kisā, lūkhā, dubbaṇṇā, uppaṇḍuppaṇḍukajātā, dhamanisanthatagattā’’ti? ‘‘Etarahi, bhante, bhikkhūnaṃ sāradikena ābādhena phuṭṭhānaṃ yāgupi pītā uggacchati, bhattampi bhuttaṃ uggacchati. Te tena kisā honti, lūkhā, dubbaṇṇā, uppaṇḍuppaṇḍukajātā, dhamanisanthatagattā’’ti. Atha kho bhagavato rahogatassa paṭisallīnassa evaṃ cetaso parivitakko udapādi – ‘‘etarahi kho bhikkhūnaṃ sāradikena ābādhena phuṭṭhānaṃ yāgupi pītā uggacchati, bhattampi bhuttaṃ uggacchati. Te tena kisā honti, lūkhā, dubbaṇṇā, uppaṇḍuppaṇḍukajātā, dhamanisanthatagattā. Kiṃ nu kho ahaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ bhesajjaṃ anujāneyyaṃ, yaṃ bhesajjañceva assa bhesajjasammatañca lokassa, āhāratthañca phareyya, na ca oḷāriko āhāro paññāyeyyā’’ti? Atha kho bhagavato etadahosi – ‘‘imāni kho pañca bhesajjāni, seyyathidaṃ – sappi, navanītaṃ, telaṃ, madhu, phāṇitaṃ; bhesajjāni ceva bhesajjasammatāni ca lokassa, āhāratthañca pharanti, na ca oḷāriko āhāro paññāyati. Yaṃnūnāhaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ imāni pañca bhesajjāni anujāneyyaṃ, kāle paṭiggahetvā kāle paribhuñjitu’’nti. Atha kho bhagavā sāyanhasamayaṃ paṭisallānā vuṭṭhito etasmiṃ nidāne etasmiṃ pakaraṇe dhammiṃ kathaṃ katvā bhikkhū āmantesi – ‘‘idha mayhaṃ, bhikkhave, rahogatassa paṭisallīnassa evaṃ cetaso parivitakko udapādi – ‘etarahi kho bhikkhūnaṃ sāradikena ābādhena phuṭṭhānaṃ yāgupi pītā uggacchati, bhattampi bhuttaṃ uggacchati. Te tena kisā honti, lūkhā, dubbaṇṇā, uppaṇḍuppaṇḍukajātā, dhamanisanthatagattā. Kiṃ nu kho ahaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ bhesajjaṃ anujāneyyaṃ, yaṃ bhesajjañceva assa bhesajjasammatañca lokassa, āhāratthañca phareyya, na ca oḷāriko āhāro paññāyeyyā’ti. Tassa mayhaṃ, bhikkhave, etadahosi ‘imāni kho pañca bhesajjāni, seyyathidaṃ – sappi, navanītaṃ, telaṃ, madhu, phāṇitaṃ; bhesajjāni ceva bhesajjasammatāni ca lokassa, āhāratthañca pharanti, na ca oḷāriko āhāro paññāyati. Yaṃnūnāhaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ imāni pañca bhesajjāni anujāneyyaṃ, kāle paṭiggahetvā kāle paribhuñjitu’nti. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, tāni pañca bhesajjāni kāle paṭiggahetvā kāle paribhuñjitu’’nti.

260.At that time the Blessed One was dwelling at Savatthi, in Jeta Grove, Anāthapiṇḍika’s Monastery. Now at that time the monks, afflicted with a seasonal illness, found that even the gruel they drank was vomited, and the food they ate was vomited. They became thin, haggard, ill-favored, pale and yellowish, with veins spread over their bodies. The Blessed One saw those monks thin, haggard, ill-favored, pale and yellowish, with veins spread over their bodies. Having seen them, he addressed the Venerable Ānanda: “Ānanda, why are the monks now so thin, haggard, ill-favored, pale and yellowish, with veins spread over their bodies?” “Venerable sir, nowadays the monks are afflicted with a seasonal illness. Even the gruel they drink is vomited, and the food they eat is vomited. That is why they are thin, haggard, ill-favored, pale and yellowish, with veins spread over their bodies.” Then, as the Blessed One was alone in retreat, this thought arose in his mind: “Nowadays the monks are afflicted with a seasonal illness. Even the gruel they drink is vomited, and the food they eat is vomited. They have become thin, haggard, ill-favored, pale and yellowish, with veins spread over their bodies. What medicine should I allow the monks, that would be medicine and considered medicine by the world, be conducive to nourishment, and not appear as coarse food?” Then it occurred to the Blessed One: “These five medicines—ghee, fresh butter, oil, honey, and molasses—are medicines and are considered medicines by the world, are conducive to nourishment, and do not appear as coarse food. Why don’t I allow the monks these five medicines, to be received at the proper time and consumed at the proper time?” Then, in the evening, the Blessed One emerged from retreat and, on this occasion, in connection with this matter, delivered a Dhamma talk and addressed the monks: “Here, monks, as I was alone in retreat, this thought arose in my mind: ‘Nowadays the monks are afflicted with a seasonal illness. Even the gruel they drink is vomited, and the food they eat is vomited. They have become thin, haggard, ill-favored, pale and yellowish, with veins spread over their bodies. What medicine should I allow the monks, that would be medicine and considered medicine by the world, be conducive to nourishment, and not appear as coarse food?’ Then it occurred to me: ‘These five medicines—ghee, fresh butter, oil, honey, and molasses—are medicines and are considered medicines by the world, are conducive to nourishment, and do not appear as coarse food. Why don’t I allow the monks these five medicines, to be received at the proper time and consumed at the proper time?’ Monks, I allow these five medicines to be received at the proper time and consumed at the proper time.”

261. Tena kho pana samayena bhikkhū tāni pañca bhesajjāni kāle paṭiggahetvā kāle paribhuñjanti. Tesaṃ yānipi tāni pākatikāni lūkhāni bhojanāni tānipi nacchādenti, pageva senesitāni [senesikāni (sī. syā.), senehikāni (yojanā)]. Te tena ceva sāradikena ābādhena phuṭṭhā, iminā ca bhattācchādakena [bhattācchannakena (ka.)], tadubhayena bhiyyosomattāya kisā honti, lūkhā, dubbaṇṇā, uppaṇḍuppaṇḍukajātā, dhamanisanthatagattā. Addasā kho bhagavā te bhikkhū bhiyyosomattāya kise lūkhe dubbaṇṇe uppaṇḍuppaṇḍukajāte dhamanisanthatagatte, disvāna āyasmantaṃ ānandaṃ āmantesi – ‘‘kiṃ nu kho, ānanda, etarahi bhikkhū bhiyyosomattāya kisā, lūkhā, dubbaṇṇā, uppaṇḍuppaṇḍukajātā, dhamanisanthatagattā’’ti? ‘‘Etarahi, bhante, bhikkhū tāni ca pañca bhesajjāni kāle paṭiggahetvā kāle paribhuñjanti. Tesaṃ yānipi tāni pākatikāni lūkhāni bhojanāni tānipi nacchādenti, pageva senesikāni. Te tena ceva sāradikena ābādhena phuṭṭhā, iminā ca bhattācchādakena, tadubhayena bhiyyosomattāya kisā, lūkhā, dubbaṇṇā, uppaṇḍuppaṇḍukajātā, dhamanisanthatagattā’’ti. Atha kho bhagavā etasmiṃ nidāne etasmiṃ pakaraṇe dhammiṃ kathaṃ katvā bhikkhū āmantesi – ‘‘anujānāmi, bhikkhave, tāni pañca bhesajjāni paṭiggahetvā kālepi vikālepi paribhuñjitu’’nti.

261.At that time, the monks, having received the five medicines at the proper time, consumed them at the proper time. Even the coarse, natural foods they did not digest, let alone the rich ones. Afflicted by that seasonal illness and this lack of appetite for food, they became excessively thin, haggard, ill-favored, pale and yellowish, with veins spread over their bodies. The Blessed One saw those monks who were excessively thin, haggard, ill-favored, pale and yellowish, with veins spread over their bodies. Having seen them, he addressed the Venerable Ānanda: “Ānanda, why are the monks now so excessively thin, haggard, ill-favored, pale and yellowish, with veins spread over their bodies?” “Venerable sir, nowadays the monks, having received the five medicines at the proper time, consume them at the proper time. Even the coarse, natural foods they do not digest, let alone the rich ones. Afflicted by that seasonal illness and this lack of appetite for food, they have become excessively thin, haggard, ill-favored, pale and yellowish, with veins spread over their bodies.” Then the Blessed One, on this occasion, in connection with this matter, delivered a Dhamma talk and addressed the monks: “Monks, I allow these five medicines to be received and consumed both at the proper time and at the improper time.”

262. Tena kho pana samayena gilānānaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ vasehi bhesajjehi attho hoti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, vasāni bhesajjāni – acchavasaṃ, macchavasaṃ, susukāvasaṃ, sūkaravasaṃ, gadrabhavasaṃ – kāle paṭiggahitaṃ kāle nippakkaṃ [nipakkaṃ (ka.)] kāle saṃsaṭṭhaṃ telaparibhogena paribhuñjituṃ. Vikāle ce, bhikkhave, paṭiggahitaṃ vikāle nippakkaṃ vikāle saṃsaṭṭhaṃ, taṃ ce paribhuñjeyya, āpatti tiṇṇaṃ dukkaṭānaṃ. Kāle ce, bhikkhave, paṭiggahitaṃ vikāle nippakkaṃ vikāle saṃsaṭṭhaṃ, taṃ ce paribhuñjeyya, āpatti dvinnaṃ dukkaṭānaṃ. Kāle ce, bhikkhave, paṭiggahitaṃ kāle nippakkaṃ vikāle saṃsaṭṭhaṃ, taṃ ce paribhuñjeyya, āpatti dukkaṭassa. Kāle ce, bhikkhave, paṭiggahitaṃ kāle nippakkaṃ kāle saṃsaṭṭhaṃ, taṃ ce paribhuñjeyya, anāpattīti.

262.Now at that time sick monks had need of medicines made with animal fat. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, I allow these animal fats as medicines—rendered fat from bear, rendered fat from fish, rendered fat from crocodile, rendered fat from pig, and rendered fat from donkey—if received at the proper time, cooked at the proper time, and mixed at the proper time, to be consumed with oil. If, monks, it is received at the wrong time, cooked at the wrong time, or mixed at the wrong time, if he consumes it, there is an offense of three dukkaṭas. If, monks, it is received at the proper time but cooked at the wrong time or mixed at the wrong time, if he consumes it, there is an offense of two dukkaṭas. If, monks, it is received at the proper time and cooked at the proper time but mixed at the wrong time, if he consumes it, there is an offense of a dukkaṭa. If, monks, it is received at the proper time, cooked at the proper time, and mixed at the proper time, if he consumes it, there is no offense.”

Pañcabhesajjakathā niṭṭhitā.

The Discourse on the Five Medicines is concluded.

### 161. Mūlādibhesajjakathā ^2

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv6-brahmali-pali#^2|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch5|BMC Chapter 5]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-MV6.2" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


161.The Discussion on Medicines Consisting of Roots, and So Forth

263. Tena kho pana samayena gilānānaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ mūlehi bhesajjehi attho hoti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, mūlāni bhesajjāni – haliddiṃ, siṅgiveraṃ, vacaṃ, vacatthaṃ [vacatthaṃ (sī. syā.)], ativisaṃ, kaṭukarohiṇiṃ, usīraṃ, bhaddamuttakaṃ, yāni vā panaññānipi atthi mūlāni bhesajjāni, neva khādanīye khādanīyatthaṃ pharanti, na bhojanīye bhojanīyatthaṃ pharanti, tāni – paṭiggahetvā yāvajīvaṃ pariharituṃ; sati paccaye paribhuñjituṃ. Asati paccaye paribhuñjantassa āpatti dukkaṭassāti.

263.At that time, sick monks needed medicines made from roots. They informed the Blessed One about this matter. “Monks, I allow root medicines—turmeric, ginger, orris root, sweet flag, ativisa, kaṭukarohiṇī, usīra, bhaddamuttaka, or any other root medicines that do not serve as food for eating nor as food for consuming—to be received and kept for as long as one lives. They may be used when there is a reason. If one uses them without a reason, there is an offense of wrong-doing.”

Tena kho pana samayena gilānānaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ mūlehi bhesajjehi piṭṭhehi attho hoti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, nisadaṃ nisadapotakanti.

At that time, sick monks needed medicines made from roots and flour. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, I allow a grinding stone and a grinding pot.”

Tena kho pana samayena gilānānaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ kasāvehi bhesajjehi attho hoti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, kasāvāni [kasāvabhesajjāni (ka.)] bhesajjāni – nimbakasāvaṃ, kuṭajakasāvaṃ, paṭolakasāvaṃ, phaggavakasāvaṃ, nattamālakasāvaṃ, yāni vā panaññānipi atthi kasāvāni bhesajjāni neva khādanīye khādanīyatthaṃ pharanti, na bhojanīye bhojanīyatthaṃ pharanti, tāni – paṭiggahetvā yāvajīvaṃ pariharituṃ; sati paccaye paribhuñjituṃ. Asati paccaye paribhuñjantassa āpatti dukkaṭassāti.

At that time, sick monks needed medicines of astringent flavors. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, I allow astringent medicines—neem astringent, kuṭaja astringent, paṭola astringent, phaggava astringent, nattamāla astringent, or any other astringent medicines that do not serve as food for eating nor as food for consuming—to be received and kept for as long as one lives. They may be used when there is a reason. If one uses them without a reason, there is an offense of wrong-doing.”

Tena kho pana samayena gilānānaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ paṇṇehi bhesajjehi attho hoti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, paṇṇāni bhesajjāni – nimbapaṇṇaṃ, kuṭajapaṇṇaṃ, paṭolapaṇṇaṃ, sulasipaṇṇaṃ, kappāsapaṇṇaṃ, yāni vā panaññānipi atthi paṇṇāni bhesajjāni, neva khādanīye khādanīyatthaṃ pharanti, na bhojanīye bhojanīyatthaṃ pharanti…pe….

At that time, sick monks needed medicines made from leaves. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, I allow leaves as medicine—neem leaves, kuṭaja leaves, paṭola leaves, tulasi leaves, cotton leaves, or any other leaves that are medicine, that do not serve as food for eating nor as food for consuming….”

Tena kho pana samayena gilānānaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ phalehi bhesajjehi attho hoti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, phalāni bhesajjāni – bilaṅgaṃ, pippaliṃ, maricaṃ, harītakaṃ, vibhītakaṃ, āmalakaṃ, goṭṭhaphalaṃ [goṭhaphalaṃ (syā.), koṭṭhaphalaṃ (ka.)], yāni vā panaññānipi atthi phalāni bhesajjāni, neva khādanīye khādanīyatthaṃ pharanti, na bhojanīye bhojanīyatthaṃ pharanti…pe….

At that time, sick monks needed medicines consisting of fruits. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, I allow fruits as medicine—bilaṅga, long pepper, black pepper, harītaka, vibhītaka, āmalaka, goṭṭhaphala, or any other fruits that are medicine, that do not serve as food for eating nor as food for consuming….”

Tena kho pana samayena gilānānaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ jatūhi bhesajjehi attho hoti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, jatūni bhesajjāni – hiṅguṃ, hiṅgujatuṃ, hiṅgusipāṭikaṃ, takaṃ, takapattiṃ, takapaṇṇiṃ, sajjulasaṃ, yāni vā panaññānipi atthi jatūni bhesajjāni, neva khādanīye khādanīyatthaṃ pharanti…pe….

At that time, sick monks needed resins as medicine. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, I allow resins as medicine—asafoetida, hiṅgujatu, hiṅgusipāṭikā, taka, takapatti, takapaṇṇī, sajjulasa, or any other resins that are medicine, that do not serve as food for eating….”

Tena kho pana samayena gilānānaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ loṇehi bhesajjehi attho hoti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, loṇāni bhesajjāni – sāmuddaṃ, kāḷaloṇaṃ, sindhavaṃ, ubbhidaṃ [ubbhiraṃ (ka.)], bilaṃ [biḷālaṃ (sī.)], yāni vā panaññānipi atthi loṇāni bhesajjāni, neva khādanīye khādanīyatthaṃ pharanti, na bhojanīye bhojanīyatthaṃ pharanti, tāni – paṭiggahetvā yāvajīvaṃ pariharituṃ; sati paccaye paribhuñjituṃ. Asati paccaye paribhuñjantassa āpatti dukkaṭassāti.

At that time, sick monks needed salts as medicine. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, I allow medicinal salts—sea salt, black salt, rock salt, ubbhida salt, bila salt, or any other medicinal salts that do not serve as food for eating nor as food for consuming—to be received and kept for as long as one lives. They may be used when there is a reason. If one uses them without a reason, there is an offense of wrong-doing.”

264. Tena kho pana samayena āyasmato ānandassa upajjhāyassa āyasmato belaṭṭhasīsassa thullakacchābādho hoti. Tassa lasikāya cīvarāni kāye lagganti, tāni bhikkhū udakena temetvā temetvā apakaḍḍhanti. Addasā kho bhagavā senāsanacārikaṃ āhiṇḍanto te bhikkhū tāni cīvarāni udakena temetvā temetvā apakaḍḍhante, disvāna yena te bhikkhū tenupasaṅkami, upasaṅkamitvā te bhikkhū etadavoca – ‘‘kiṃ imassa, bhikkhave, bhikkhuno ābādho’’ti? ‘‘Imassa, bhante, āyasmato thullakacchābādho, lasikāya cīvarāni kāye lagganti, tāni mayaṃ udakena temetvā temetvā apakaḍḍhāmā’’ti. Atha kho bhagavā etasmiṃ nidāne etasmiṃ pakaraṇe dhammiṃ kathaṃ katvā bhikkhū āmantesi – ‘‘anujānāmi, bhikkhave, yassa kaṇḍu vā, piḷakā vā, assāvo vā, thullakacchu vā ābādho, kāyo vā duggandho, cuṇṇāni bhesajjāni; agilānassa chakaṇaṃ mattikaṃ rajananippakkaṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, udukkhalaṃ musala’’nti.

264.At that time, Venerable Ānanda’s preceptor, Venerable Belaṭṭhasīsa, was suffering from a severe skin disease. His robes were sticking to his body due to the pus, and the monks were repeatedly soaking them in water and pulling them off. The Blessed One, while walking around the lodgings, saw those monks repeatedly soaking the robes in water and pulling them off. Seeing this, he approached them and asked, “Monks, what is the illness of this monk?” “Venerable sir, this venerable one has a severe skin disease. His robes are sticking to his body due to the pus, so we are repeatedly soaking them in water and pulling them off.” Then, on this occasion, the Blessed One gave a Dhamma talk and addressed the monks: “Monks, I allow medicinal powders for one who has itching, boils, discharges, severe skin disease, or a foul-smelling body. For one who is not ill, I allow cow dung, clay, or dye refuse. Monks, I allow a mortar and a pestle.”

Tena kho pana samayena gilānānaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ cuṇṇehi bhesajjehi cālitehi attho hoti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, cuṇṇacālininti. Saṇhehi attho hoti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, dussacālininti.

At that time, sick monks needed medicinal powders sifted with a sieve. They informed the Blessed One of this matter. “Monks, I allow a powder sieve.” They needed something for sifting fine materials. They informed the Blessed One of this matter. “Monks, I allow a cloth sieve.”

Tena kho pana samayena aññatarassa bhikkhuno amanussikābādho hoti. Taṃ ācariyupajjhāyā upaṭṭhahantā nāsakkhiṃsu arogaṃ kātuṃ. So sūkarasūnaṃ gantvā āmakamaṃsaṃ khādi, āmakalohitaṃ pivi. Tassa so amanussikābādho paṭippassambhi. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, amanussikābādhe āmakamaṃsaṃ āmakalohitanti.

At that time, a certain monk had a disease caused by non-human beings. His teachers and preceptors, attending to him, were unable to make him well. He went to a pig slaughterer, ate raw meat, and drank raw blood. That disease caused by non-human beings subsided for him. They informed the Blessed One of this matter. “Monks, I allow raw meat and raw blood for a disease caused by non-human beings.”

265. Tena kho pana samayena aññatarassa bhikkhuno cakkhurogābādho hoti. Taṃ bhikkhū pariggahetvā uccārampi passāvampi nikkhāmenti. Addasā kho bhagavā senāsanacārikaṃ āhiṇḍanto te bhikkhū taṃ bhikkhuṃ pariggahetvā uccārampi passāvampi nikkhāmente, disvāna yena te bhikkhū tenupasaṅkami, upasaṅkamitvā te bhikkhū etadavoca – ‘‘kiṃ imassa, bhikkhave, bhikkhuno ābādho’’ti? ‘‘Imassa, bhante, āyasmato cakkhurogābādho. Imaṃ mayaṃ pariggahetvā uccārampi passāvampi nikkhāmemā’’ti. Atha kho bhagavā etasmiṃ nidāne etasmiṃ pakaraṇe dhammiṃ kathaṃ katvā bhikkhū āmantesi – ‘‘anujānāmi, bhikkhave, añjanaṃ – kāḷañjanaṃ, rasañjanaṃ, sotañjanaṃ, gerukaṃ, kapalla’’nti. Añjanūpapisanehi attho hoti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, candanaṃ, tagaraṃ, kāḷānusāriyaṃ, tālīsaṃ, bhaddamuttakanti. Tena kho pana samayena bhikkhū piṭṭhāni añjanāni carukesupi [thālakesupi (sī. syā.)] sarāvakesupi nikkhipanti; tiṇacuṇṇehipi paṃsukehipi okiriyanti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, añjaninti.

265.At that time, a certain monk was suffering from an eye disease. The monks attended to him and helped him relieve himself, both feces and urine. The Blessed One, while walking around the lodgings, saw those monks attending to that monk as he relieved himself, both feces and urine. Having seen them, he approached those monks and asked, “Monks, what is the ailment of this monk?” “Venerable sir, this venerable one has an eye disease. We are attending to him as he relieves himself, both feces and urine.” Then the Blessed One, on this occasion, having given a Dhamma talk, addressed the monks: “Monks, I allow eye ointments—black ointment, compound ointment, antimony ointment, red ochre, and soot.” There was a need for things to be ground together with the ointment. They informed the Blessed One of this matter. “Monks, I allow sandalwood, tagara, black collyrium, tālīsa, and bhaddamuttaka.” At that time, monks placed ground ointments in small bowls or on trays. They were scattered by grass dust or dirt. They informed the Blessed One of this matter. “Monks, I allow an ointment container.”

Tena kho pana samayena chabbaggiyā bhikkhū uccāvacā añjaniyo dhārenti – sovaṇṇamayaṃ, rūpiyamayaṃ. Manussā ujjhāyanti khiyyanti vipācenti – ‘‘seyyathāpi gihī kāmabhogino’’ti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Na, bhikkhave, uccāvacā añjanī dhāretabbā. Yo dhāreyya, āpatti dukkaṭassa. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, aṭṭhimayaṃ, dantamayaṃ, visāṇamayaṃ, naḷamayaṃ, veḷumayaṃ, kaṭṭhamayaṃ, jatumayaṃ, phalamayaṃ, lohamayaṃ, saṅkhanābhimayanti.

At that time, the monks of the group of six were carrying various kinds of ointment containers—made of gold, made of silver. People complained, criticized, and spread it about: “Just like householders indulging in sensual pleasures.” They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, various kinds of ointment containers should not be carried. Whoever carries one incurs an offense of wrong-doing. Monks, I allow those made of bone, ivory, horn, reed, bamboo, wood, resin, fruit, metal, or shell.”

Tena kho pana samayena añjaniyo apārutā honti, tiṇacuṇṇehipi paṃsukehipi okiriyanti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, apidhānanti. Apidhānaṃ nipatati. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, suttakena bandhitvā añjaniyā bandhitunti. Añjanī phalati [nipatati (ka.)]. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, suttakena sibbetunti.

At that time, the ointment pots were open and got scattered with grass dust and dirt. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, I allow a cover.” The cover fell off. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, I allow tying it with a thread to the ointment pot.” The ointment pot broke. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, I allow sewing it with a thread.”

Tena kho pana samayena bhikkhū aṅguliyā añjanti, akkhīni dukkhāni honti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, añjanisalākanti.

At that time, monks were applying ointment with their fingers, and their eyes became sore. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, I allow an ointment applicator.”

Tena kho pana samayena chabbaggiyā bhikkhū uccāvacā añjanisalākāyo dhārenti – sovaṇṇamayaṃ rūpiyamayaṃ. Manussā ujjhāyanti khiyyanti vipācenti, ‘‘seyyathāpi gihī kāmabhogino’’ti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Na, bhikkhave, uccāvacā añjanisalākā dhāretabbā. Yo dhāreyya, āpatti dukkaṭassa. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, aṭṭhimayaṃ…pe… saṅkhanābhimayanti.

At that time, the monks of the group of six were carrying various kinds of ointment applicators—made of gold, made of silver. People complained, criticized, and spread it about: “Just like householders enjoying sensual pleasures.” They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, various kinds of ointment applicators should not be carried. Whoever carries one incurs an offense of wrong-doing. Monks, I allow those made of bone…of shell.”

Tena kho pana samayena añjanisalākā bhūmiyaṃ patitā pharusā hoti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, salākaṭhāniyanti [salākodhāniyanti (sī. syā.)].

At that time, an ointment applicator, having fallen on the ground, became rough. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, I allow an applicator holder.”

Tena kho pana samayena bhikkhū añjanimpi añjanisalākampi hatthena pariharanti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, añjanitthavikanti. Aṃsabaddhako na hoti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, aṃsabaddhakaṃ bandhanasuttakanti.

At that time, monks carried both ointment and an ointment applicator in their hands. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, I allow an ointment bag.” There was no shoulder strap. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, I allow a shoulder strap and a tying string.”

266. Tena kho pana samayena āyasmato pilindavacchassa sīsābhitāpo hoti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, muddhani telakanti. Nakkhamaniyo hoti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, natthukammanti. Natthu galati. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, natthukaraṇinti.

266.At that time, Venerable Pilindavaccha was suffering from a headache. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, I allow oil for the head.” It was not effective. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, I allow nasal treatment.” The nasal medication was dripping out. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, I allow a nasal tube.”

Tena kho pana samayena chabbaggiyā bhikkhū uccāvacā natthukaraṇiyo dhārenti – sovaṇṇamayaṃ rūpiyamayaṃ. Manussā ujjhāyanti khiyyanti vipācenti, ‘‘seyyathāpi gihī kāmabhogino’’ti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Na, bhikkhave, uccāvacā natthukaraṇī dhāretabbā. Yo dhāreyya, āpatti dukkaṭassa. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, aṭṭhimayaṃ…pe… saṅkhanābhimayanti. Natthuṃ visamaṃ āsiñcanti [natthu visamaṃ āsiñciyati (sī. syā.)]. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, yamakanatthukaraṇinti. Nakkhamaniyo hoti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, dhūmaṃ pātunti. Taññeva vaṭṭiṃ ālimpetvā pivanti, kaṇṭho dahati. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, dhūmanettanti.

At that time, the monks of the group of six were wearing various kinds of nasal tubes—some made of gold, some made of silver. People complained, criticized, and spread it about, saying, “Just like householders enjoying sensual pleasures!” They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, various kinds of nasal tubes should not be worn. Whoever wears one commits an offense of wrong-doing. Monks, I allow those made of bone… …or made of conch shell.” They sprinkled the nasal medication unevenly. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, I allow a double nasal tube.” It was not effective. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, I allow inhaling smoke.” They lit the same wick and inhaled it, burning their throats. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, I allow a smoke pipe.”

Tena kho pana samayena chabbaggiyā bhikkhū uccāvacāni dhūmanettāni dhārenti – sovaṇṇamayaṃ rūpiyamayaṃ. Manussā ujjhāyanti khiyyanti vipācenti – seyyathāpi gihī kāmabhoginoti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Na, bhikkhave, uccāvacāni dhūmanettāni dhāretabbāni. Yo dhāreyya, āpatti dukkaṭassa. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, aṭṭhimayaṃ…pe… saṅkhanābhimayanti.

At that time, the monks of the group of six were wearing various kinds of smoke pipes—some made of gold, some made of silver. People complained, criticized, and spread it about, saying, “Just like householders enjoying sensual pleasures!” They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, various kinds of smoke pipes should not be worn. Whoever wears one commits an offense of wrong-doing. Monks, I allow those made of bone… …or made of conch shell.”

Tena kho pana samayena dhūmanettāni apārutāni honti, pāṇakā pavisanti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, apidhānanti.

At that time, the smoke pipes were left open, and insects entered. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, I allow a lid.”

Tena kho pana samayena bhikkhū dhūmanettāni hatthena pariharanti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, dhūmanettathavikanti. Ekato ghaṃsiyanti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, yamakathavikanti. Aṃsabaddhako na hoti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, aṃsabaddhakaṃ bandhanasuttakanti.

At that time, monks carried smoke pipes in their hands. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, I allow a smoke-pipe bag.” They were abraded at one place. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, I allow a double bag.” There was no shoulder strap. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, I allow a shoulder strap and a fastening cord.”

267. Tena kho pana samayena āyasmato pilindavacchassa vātābādho hoti. Vejjā evamāhaṃsu – ‘‘telaṃ pacitabba’’nti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, telapākanti. Tasmiṃ kho pana telapāke majjaṃ pakkhipitabbaṃ hoti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, telapāke majjaṃ pakkhipitunti.

267.At that time, Venerable Pilindavaccha was suffering from a wind disorder. The physicians said, “Oil should be cooked.” They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, I allow the cooking of oil.” In that cooking of oil, intoxicant needed to be added. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, I allow the adding of intoxicant to the cooking of oil.”

Tena kho pana samayena chabbaggiyā bhikkhū atipakkhittamajjāni [atikhittamajjāni (ka.)] telāni pacanti, tāni pivitvā majjanti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Na, bhikkhave, atipakkhittamajjaṃ telaṃ pātabbaṃ. Yo piveyya, yathādhammo kāretabbo. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, yasmiṃ telapāke majjassa na vaṇṇo na gandho na raso paññāyati, evarūpaṃ majjapakkhittaṃ telaṃ pātunti.

At that time, the monks of the group of six were cooking oils with excessive intoxicants and drinking them, becoming intoxicated. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, oil cooked with excessive intoxicants should not be drunk. Whoever drinks it should be dealt with according to the rule. Monks, I allow oil cooked with intoxicants in which the color, smell, or taste of intoxicants is not discernible—such oil cooked with intoxicants may be drunk.”

Tena kho pana samayena bhikkhūnaṃ bahuṃ atipakkhittamajjaṃ telaṃ pakkaṃ hoti. Atha kho bhikkhūnaṃ etadahosi – ‘‘kathaṃ nu kho atipakkhittamajje tele paṭipajjitabba’’nti? Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, abbhañjanaṃ adhiṭṭhātunti.

At that time, the monks had a large quantity of oil cooked with excessive intoxicants. Then the monks thought, “How should we deal with this oil cooked with excessive intoxicants?” They reported the matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, I allow it to be designated as oil for anointing.”

Tena kho pana samayena āyasmato pilindavacchassa bahutaraṃ telaṃ pakkaṃ hoti, telabhājanaṃ na vijjati. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, tīṇi tumbāni – lohatumbaṃ, kaṭṭhatumbaṃ, phalatumbanti.

At that time, Venerable Pilindavaccha had a large quantity of oil cooked, but there was no oil vessel. They reported the matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, I allow three gourd containers: a metal gourd container, a wooden gourd container, and a fruit gourd container.”

Tena kho pana samayena āyasmato pilindavacchassa aṅgavāto hoti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, sedakammanti. Nakkhamaniyo hoti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, sambhārasedanti. Nakkhamaniyo hoti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, mahāsedanti. Nakkhamaniyo hoti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, bhaṅgodakanti. Nakkhamaniyo hoti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, udakakoṭṭhakanti.

At that time, Venerable Pilindavaccha had a wind disorder in the limbs. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, I allow sweat treatment.” It was not effective. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, I allow sweat treatment with various ingredients.” It was not effective. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, I allow extensive sweat treatment.” It was not effective. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, I allow water boiled with various leaves.” It was not effective. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, I allow a water chamber.”

Tena kho pana samayena āyasmato pilindavacchassa pabbavāto hoti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, lohitaṃ mocetunti. Nakkhamaniyo hoti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, lohitaṃ mocetvā visāṇena gāhetunti [gahetunti (sī. syā.)].

At that time, Venerable Pilindavaccha had a wind disorder in the joints. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, I allow bloodletting.” It was not effective. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, I allow bloodletting and then drawing it with a horn.”

Tena kho pana samayena āyasmato pilindavacchassa pādā phalitā [phālitā (ka.)] honti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, pādabbhañjananti. Nakkhamaniyo hoti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, pajjaṃ abhisaṅkharitunti.

At that time, the feet of Venerable Pilindavaccha were cracked. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, I allow foot anointing.” It was not effective. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, I allow preparing a foot remedy.”

Tena kho pana samayena aññatarassa bhikkhuno gaṇḍābādho hoti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, satthakammanti. Kasāvodakena attho hoti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, kasāvodakanti. Tilakakkena attho hoti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, tilakakkanti. Kabaḷikāya attho hoti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, kabaḷikanti. Vaṇabandhanacoḷena attho hoti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, vaṇabandhanacoḷanti. Vaṇo kaṇḍuvati. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, sāsapakuṭṭena [sāsapakuḍḍena (sī. syā.)] phositunti. Vaṇo kilijjittha. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, dhūmaṃ kātunti. Vaḍḍhamaṃsaṃ vuṭṭhāti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, loṇasakkharikāya chinditunti. Vaṇo na ruhati. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, vaṇatelanti. Telaṃ galati. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, vikāsikaṃ sabbaṃ vaṇapaṭikammanti.

At that time, a certain monk had a boil. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, I allow surgical treatment.” There was a need for astringent water. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, I allow astringent water.” There was a need for sesame cake. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, I allow sesame cake.” There was a need for a compress. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, I allow a compress.” There was a need for a wound-binding cloth. They reported the matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, I allow a wound-binding cloth.” The wound itched. They reported the matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, I allow sprinkling with mustard powder.” The wound became putrid. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, I allow applying smoke treatment.” Excess flesh grew. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, I allow cutting it with salt crystal.” The wound did not heal. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, I allow wound oil.” The oil dripped. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, I allow a bandage and all kinds of wound treatment.”

268. Tena kho pana samayena aññataro bhikkhu ahinā daṭṭho hoti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, cattāri mahāvikaṭāni dātuṃ – gūthaṃ, muttaṃ, chārikaṃ, mattikanti. Atha kho bhikkhūnaṃ etadahosi – ‘‘appaṭiggahitāni nu kho udāhu paṭiggahetabbānī’’ti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, sati kappiyakārake paṭiggahāpetuṃ, asati kappiyakārake sāmaṃ gahetvā paribhuñjitunti.

268.At that time, a certain monk was bitten by a snake. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, I allow the giving of four great medicaments—dung, urine, ashes, and clay.” Then the monks thought, “Should these be received or not?” They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, I allow that if there is a suitable person, it should be received by them; if there is no suitable person, one may take it oneself and use it.”

Tena kho pana samayena aññatarena bhikkhunā visaṃ pītaṃ hoti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi bhikkhave gūthaṃ pāyetunti. Atha kho bhikkhūnaṃ etadahosi – ‘‘appaṭiggahitaṃ nu kho udāhu paṭiggahetabbo’’ti? Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, yaṃ karonto paṭiggaṇhāti, sveva paṭiggaho kato, na puna [kato pana (?)] paṭiggahetabboti.

At that time, a certain monk had drunk poison. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, I allow dung to be drunk.” Then the monks thought, “Should this be received or not?” They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, I allow that by whatever action one receives it, by that the receiving is done; it need not be received again.”

269. Tena kho pana samayena aññatarassa bhikkhuno gharadinnakābādho hoti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, sītāloḷiṃ pāyetunti.

269.At that time, a certain monk had an illness caused by a charm. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, I allow cold gruel to be drunk.”

Tena kho pana samayena aññataro bhikkhu duṭṭhagahaṇiko hoti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, āmisakhāraṃ pāyetunti.

At that time, a certain monk suffered from a bad stomach. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, I allow alkaline water from burnt rice to be drunk.”

Tena kho pana samayena aññatarassa bhikkhuno paṇḍurogābādho hoti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, muttaharītakaṃ pāyetunti.

At that time, a certain monk was afflicted with jaundice. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, I allow harītaka soaked in cow urine to be drunk.”

Tena kho pana samayena aññatarassa bhikkhuno chavidosābādho hoti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, gandhālepaṃ kātunti.

At that time, a certain monk had a skin disease. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, I allow the application of scented ointment.”

Tena kho pana samayena aññataro bhikkhu abhisannakāyo hoti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, virecanaṃ pātunti. Acchakañjiyā attho hoti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, acchakañjinti. Akaṭayūsena attho hoti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, akaṭayūsanti. Kaṭākaṭena attho hoti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, kaṭākaṭanti. Paṭicchādanīyena attho hoti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, paṭicchādanīyanti.

At that time a certain monk had a body with excessive humors. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “I allow, monks, the taking of a purgative.” He needed rice-water gruel. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “I allow, monks, rice-water gruel.” He needed un-oiled mung bean broth. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “I allow, monks, un-oiled mung bean broth.” He needed oiled mung bean broth. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “I allow, monks, oiled mung bean broth.” He needed meat broth. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “I allow, monks, meat broth.”

Mūlādibhesajjakathā niṭṭhitā.

The discussion of root-based medicines, etc., is concluded.

### 162. Pilindavacchavatthu ^3

162.The Story of Pilindavaccha

270. [idaṃ vatthu pārā. 618 ādayo] Tena kho pana samayena āyasmā pilindavaccho rājagahe pabbhāraṃ sodhāpeti leṇaṃ kattukāmo. Atha kho rājā māgadho seniyo bimbisāro yenāyasmā pilindavaccho tenupasaṅkami, upasaṅkamitvā āyasmantaṃ pilindavacchaṃ abhivādetvā ekamantaṃ nisīdi. Ekamantaṃ nisinno kho rājā māgadho seniyo bimbisāro āyasmantaṃ pilindavacchaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘kiṃ, bhante, thero kārāpetī’’ti? ‘‘Pabbhāraṃ, mahārāja, sodhāpemi, leṇaṃ kattukāmo’’ti. ‘‘Attho, bhante, ayyassa ārāmikenā’’ti? ‘‘Na kho, mahārāja, bhagavatā ārāmiko anuññāto’’ti. ‘‘Tena hi, bhante, bhagavantaṃ paṭipucchitvā mama āroceyyāthā’’ti. ‘Evaṃ, mahārājā’ti kho āyasmā pilindavaccho rañño māgadhassa seniyassa bimbisārassa paccassosi. Atha kho āyasmā pilindavaccho rājānaṃ māgadhaṃ seniyaṃ bimbisāraṃ dhammiyā kathāya sandassesi, samādapesi, samuttejesi, sampahaṃsesi. Atha kho rājā māgadho seniyo bimbisāro āyasmatā pilindavacchena dhammiyā kathāya sandassito samādapito samuttejito sampahaṃsito uṭṭhāyāsanā āyasmantaṃ pilindavacchaṃ abhivādetvā padakkhiṇaṃ katvā pakkāmi.

270.Now at that time the Venerable Pilindavaccha was having a slope cleared at Rājagaha, wanting to make a dwelling. Then King Seniya Bimbisāra of Magadha approached the Venerable Pilindavaccha, paid homage to him, and sat down to one side. Sitting to one side, King Seniya Bimbisāra of Magadha said to the Venerable Pilindavaccha: “What is the elder having done, venerable sir?” “Great king, I am having a slope cleared, wanting to make a dwelling.” “Does the venerable one need a monastery worker, venerable sir?” “Great king, a monastery worker has not been allowed by the Blessed One.” “Then, venerable sir, please ask the Blessed One and inform me.” “Yes, great king,” the Venerable Pilindavaccha replied to King Seniya Bimbisāra of Magadha. Then the Venerable Pilindavaccha instructed, urged, inspired, and gladdened King Seniya Bimbisāra of Magadha with a Dhamma talk. Then King Seniya Bimbisāra of Magadha, having been instructed, urged, inspired, and gladdened by the Venerable Pilindavaccha with a Dhamma talk, rose from his seat, paid homage to the Venerable Pilindavaccha, circumambulated him, and departed.

Atha kho āyasmā pilindavaccho bhagavato santike dūtaṃ pāhesi – ‘‘rājā, bhante, māgadho seniyo bimbisāro ārāmikaṃ dātukāmo. Kathaṃ nu kho, bhante, mayā paṭipajjitabba’’nti? Atha kho bhagavā etasmiṃ nidāne etasmiṃ pakaraṇe dhammiṃ kathaṃ katvā bhikkhū āmantesi – ‘‘anujānāmi, bhikkhave, ārāmika’’nti. Dutiyampi kho rājā māgadho seniyo bimbisāro yenāyasmā pilindavaccho tenupasaṅkami; upasaṅkamitvā āyasmantaṃ pilindavacchaṃ abhivādetvā ekamantaṃ nisīdi. Ekamantaṃ nisinno kho rājā māgadho seniyo bimbisāro āyasmantaṃ pilindavacchaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘anuññāto, bhante, bhagavatā ārāmiko’’ti? ‘‘Evaṃ, mahārājā’’ti. ‘‘Tena hi, bhante, ayyassa ārāmikaṃ dammī’’ti. Atha kho rājā māgadho seniyo bimbisāro āyasmato pilindavacchassa ārāmikaṃ paṭissutvā, vissaritvā, cirena satiṃ paṭilabhitvā, aññataraṃ sabbatthakaṃ mahāmattaṃ āmantesi – ‘‘yo mayā, bhaṇe, ayyassa ārāmiko paṭissuto, dinno so ārāmiko’’ti? ‘‘Na kho, deva, ayyassa ārāmiko dinno’’ti. ‘‘Kīva ciraṃ nu kho, bhaṇe, ito [ito ratti (syā.)] hi taṃ hotī’’ti? Atha kho so mahāmatto rattiyo gaṇetvā [vigaṇetvā (sī.)] rājānaṃ māgadhaṃ seniyaṃ bimbisāraṃ etadavoca – ‘‘pañca, deva, rattisatānī’’ti. Tena hi, bhaṇe, ayyassa pañca ārāmikasatāni dehīti. ‘‘Evaṃ, devā’’ti kho so mahāmatto rañño māgadhassa seniyassa bimbisārassa paṭissutvā āyasmato pilindavacchassa pañca ārāmikasatāni pādāsi, pāṭiyekko gāmo nivisi. ‘Ārāmikagāmakoti’pi naṃ āhaṃsu, ‘pilindagāmako’tipi naṃ āhaṃsu.

Then Venerable Pilindavaccha sent a messenger to the Blessed One: “Venerable sir, King Seniya Bimbisāra of Magadha wishes to give a monastery attendant. How should I proceed, venerable sir?” Then the Blessed One, having given a Dhamma talk on this occasion and in connection with this matter, addressed the monks: “I allow, monks, a monastery attendant.” A second time, King Seniya Bimbisāra of Magadha approached Venerable Pilindavaccha; having approached, he paid homage to Venerable Pilindavaccha and sat down to one side. Sitting to one side, King Seniya Bimbisāra of Magadha said to Venerable Pilindavaccha, “Has a monastery attendant been permitted by the Blessed One, venerable sir?” “Yes, great king.” “Then, venerable sir, I will give a monastery attendant to the venerable one.” Then King Seniya Bimbisāra of Magadha, having promised a monastery attendant to Venerable Pilindavaccha, forgot about it and only remembered after a long time. He then addressed a certain general official: “Good man, was the monastery attendant I promised to the venerable one given?” “No, sire, the monastery attendant was not given to the venerable one.” “How long has it been, good man, since that happened?” Then that official counted the nights and said to King Seniya Bimbisāra of Magadha, “Five hundred nights, sire.” “Then, good man, give the venerable one five hundred monastery attendants.” “Yes, sire,” the official replied to King Seniya Bimbisāra of Magadha and gave Venerable Pilindavaccha five hundred monastery attendants. A separate village was established for each one. They called it ‘Ārāmikagāmaka’ (Monastery Attendant Village) and also ‘Pilindagāmaka’ (Pilinda’s Village).

271. Tena kho pana samayena āyasmā pilindavaccho tasmiṃ gāmake kulūpako hoti. Atha kho āyasmā pilindavaccho pubbaṇhasamayaṃ nivāsetvā pattacīvaramādāya pilindagāmaṃ piṇḍāya pāvisi. Tena kho pana samayena tasmiṃ gāmake ussavo hoti. Dārakā alaṅkatā mālākitā kīḷanti. Atha kho āyasmā pilindavaccho pilindagāmake sapadānaṃ piṇḍāya caramāno yena aññatarassa ārāmikassa nivesanaṃ tenupasaṅkami, upasaṅkamitvā paññatte āsane nisīdi. Tena kho pana samayena tassā ārāmikiniyā dhītā aññe dārake alaṅkate mālākite passitvā rodati – ‘mālaṃ me detha, alaṅkāraṃ me dethā’ti. Atha kho āyasmā pilindavaccho taṃ ārāmikiniṃ etadavoca – ‘‘kissāyaṃ dārikā rodatī’’ti? ‘‘Ayaṃ, bhante, dārikā aññe dārake alaṅkate mālākite passitvā rodati – ‘mālaṃ me detha, alaṅkāraṃ me dethā’ti. Kuto amhākaṃ duggatānaṃ mālā, kuto alaṅkāro’’ti? Atha kho āyasmā pilindavaccho aññataraṃ tiṇaṇḍupakaṃ gahetvā taṃ ārāmikiniṃ etadavoca – ‘‘handimaṃ tiṇaṇḍupakaṃ tassā dārikāya sīse paṭimuñcā’’ti. Atha kho sā ārāmikinī taṃ tiṇaṇḍupakaṃ gahetvā tassā dārikāya sīse paṭimuñci. Sā ahosi suvaṇṇamālā abhirūpā, dassanīyā, pāsādikā; natthi tādisā raññopi antepure suvaṇṇamālā. Manussā rañño māgadhassa seniyassa bimbisārassa ārocesuṃ – ‘‘amukassa, deva, ārāmikassa ghare suvaṇṇamālā abhirūpā, dassanīyā, pāsādikā; natthi tādisā devassapi antepure suvaṇṇamālā; kuto tassa duggatassa? Nissaṃsayaṃ corikāya ābhatā’’ti.

271.Now at that time, Venerable Pilindavaccha was a frequent guest in that village. Then, Venerable Pilindavaccha, having dressed in the morning, took his bowl and robe and entered Pilindavillage for alms. Now at that time, there was a festival in that village. Children, adorned and garlanded, were playing. Then, Venerable Pilindavaccha, walking for alms from house to house in Pilindavillage, approached the dwelling of a certain groundskeeper and sat down on the prepared seat. Now at that time, the daughter of that groundskeeper, seeing other children adorned and garlanded, cried: “Give me a garland! Give me ornaments!” Then, Venerable Pilindavaccha said to that groundskeeper: “Why is this girl crying?” “Venerable sir, this girl sees other children adorned and garlanded and cries: ‘Give me a garland! Give me ornaments!’ But where would we poor people get garlands or ornaments?” Then, Venerable Pilindavaccha took a small bunch of grass and said to that groundskeeper: “Here, place this small bunch of grass on the girl’s head.” Then, that groundskeeper took the small bunch of grass and placed it on the girl’s head. It became a golden garland—beautiful, lovely, and pleasing. There was no such golden garland even in King Bimbisāra’s inner palace. People informed King Seniya Bimbisāra of Magadha: “Sire, in the house of such-and-such a groundskeeper, there is a golden garland—beautiful, lovely, and pleasing. There is no such golden garland even in your inner palace. How could such a poor person have it? Surely, it must have been obtained by theft!”

Atha kho rājā māgadho seniyo bimbisāro taṃ ārāmikakulaṃ bandhāpesi. Dutiyampi kho āyasmā pilindavaccho pubbaṇhasamayaṃ nivāsetvā pattacīvaramādāya pilindagāmaṃ piṇḍāya pāvisi. Pilindagāmake sapadānaṃ piṇḍāya caramāno yena tassa ārāmikassa nivesanaṃ tenupasaṅkami, upasaṅkamitvā paṭivissake pucchi – ‘‘kahaṃ imaṃ ārāmikakulaṃ gata’’nti? ‘‘Etissā, bhante, suvaṇṇamālāya kāraṇā raññā bandhāpita’’nti. Atha kho āyasmā pilindavaccho yena rañño māgadhassa seniyassa bimbisārassa nivesanaṃ tenupasaṅkami, upasaṅkamitvā paññatte āsane nisīdi. Atha kho rājā māgadho seniyo bimbisāro yenāyasmā pilindavaccho tenupasaṅkami, upasaṅkamitvā āyasmantaṃ pilindavacchaṃ abhivādetvā ekamantaṃ nisīdi. Ekamantaṃ nisinnaṃ kho rājānaṃ māgadhaṃ seniyaṃ bimbisāraṃ āyasmā pilindavaccho etadavoca – ‘‘kissa, mahārāja, ārāmikakulaṃ bandhāpita’’nti? ‘‘Tassa, bhante, ārāmikassa ghare suvaṇṇamālā abhirūpā, dassanīyā, pāsādikā; natthi tādisā amhākampi antepure suvaṇṇamālā; kuto tassa duggatassa? Nissaṃsayaṃ corikāya ābhatā’’ti. Atha kho āyasmā pilindavaccho rañño māgadhassa seniyassa bimbisārassa pāsādaṃ suvaṇṇanti adhimucci; so ahosi sabbasovaṇṇamayo. ‘‘Idaṃ pana te, mahārāja, tāva bahuṃ suvaṇṇaṃ kuto’’ti? ‘Aññātaṃ, bhante, ayyasseveso iddhānubhāvo’ti taṃ ārāmikakulaṃ muñcāpesi.

Then King Seniya Bimbisāra of Magadha had that groundskeeper’s family arrested. A second time, Venerable Pilindavaccha, having dressed in the morning and taken his bowl and robe, entered Pilindagāma for alms. Wandering for alms from house to house in Pilindagāma, he approached the dwelling of that groundskeeper. Having approached, he asked the neighbors, “Where has this groundskeeper’s family gone?” “Because of that golden garland, venerable sir, the king had them arrested.” Then Venerable Pilindavaccha approached the dwelling of King Seniya Bimbisāra of Magadha. Having approached, he sat down on the prepared seat. Then King Seniya Bimbisāra of Magadha approached Venerable Pilindavaccha; having approached, he paid homage to Venerable Pilindavaccha and sat down to one side. Sitting to one side, King Seniya Bimbisāra was addressed by Venerable Pilindavaccha: “Great king, why was the groundskeeper’s family arrested?” “Venerable sir, in that groundskeeper’s house was a golden garland—beautiful, lovely, splendid. There is no such golden garland even in our inner palace; how much less for that poor man? Surely it was brought by theft.” Then Venerable Pilindavaccha willed King Seniya Bimbisāra’s palace to be golden; it was entirely golden. “But great king, where did this much gold of yours come from?” “It is unknown, venerable sir. This is the venerable one’s psychic power.” And he had that groundskeeper’s family released.

Manussā ‘‘ayyena kira pilindavacchena sarājikāya parisāya uttarimanussadhammaṃ iddhipāṭihāriyaṃ dassita’’nti attamanā abhippasannā āyasmato pilindavacchassa pañca bhesajjāni abhihariṃsu, seyyathidaṃ – sappiṃ, navanītaṃ, telaṃ, madhuṃ [sappi navanītaṃ telaṃ madhu (ka.)], phāṇitaṃ. Pakatiyāpi ca āyasmā pilindavaccho lābhī hoti pañcannaṃ bhesajjānaṃ; laddhaṃ laddhaṃ parisāya vissajjeti. Parisā cassa hoti bāhullikā; laddhaṃ laddhaṃ kolambepi [koḷumbepi (ka.)], ghaṭepi, pūretvā paṭisāmeti; parissāvanānipi, thavikāyopi, pūretvā vātapānesu laggeti. Tāni olīnavilīnāni tiṭṭhanti. Undūrehipi vihārā okiṇṇavikiṇṇā honti. Manussā vihāracārikaṃ āhiṇḍantā passitvā ujjhāyanti khiyyanti vipācenti – ‘‘antokoṭṭhāgārikā ime samaṇā sakyaputtiyā, seyyathāpi rājā māgadho seniyo bimbisāro’’ti. Assosuṃ kho bhikkhū tesaṃ manussānaṃ ujjhāyantānaṃ khiyyantānaṃ vipācentānaṃ. Ye te bhikkhū appicchā, te ujjhāyanti khiyyanti vipācenti – ‘‘kathañhi nāma bhikkhū evarūpāya bāhullāya cetessantī’’ti. Atha kho te bhikkhū te anekapariyāyena vigarahitvā bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ…pe… ‘‘saccaṃ kira, bhikkhave, bhikkhū evarūpāya bāhullāya cetentī’’ti? ‘‘Saccaṃ bhagavāti…pe… vigarahitvā dhammiṃ kathaṃ katvā bhikkhū āmantesi – ‘‘yāni kho pana tāni gilānānaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ paṭisāyanīyāni bhesajjāni, seyyathidaṃ – sappi, navanītaṃ, telaṃ, madhu, phāṇitaṃ, tāni paṭiggahetvā sattāhaparamaṃ sannidhikārakaṃ paribhuñjitabbāni. Taṃ atikkāmayato yathādhammo kāretabbo’’ti.

The people, delighted and full of faith, [thinking,] 'It seems the venerable Pilindavaccha has displayed a superhuman state, a miracle of psychic power, before the royal assembly,' offered five kinds of medicine to Venerable Pilindavaccha: namely, ghee, fresh butter, oil, honey, and molasses. By nature, Venerable Pilindavaccha was accustomed to receiving these five medicines. Whatever he received, he distributed to his retinue. His retinue was numerous; whatever they received, they stored in pots and jars, filling them up and putting them aside. They even filled strainers and bags, hanging them in the windows. These items remained sticky and melted. Even the dwellings became scattered and strewn about by rats. People wandering around the monastery saw this and complained, grumbled, and criticized, 'These Sakyan ascetics are like householders who store up provisions, just like King Seniya Bimbisāra of Magadha!' The monks heard these people complaining, grumbling, and criticizing. Those monks who were of few desires complained, grumbled, and criticized, 'How can the monks be intent on such abundance?' Then those monks, after rebuking them in many ways, reported the matter to the Blessed One… 'Is it true, monks, that the monks are intent on such abundance?' 'It is true, Blessed One.' … After rebuking them and giving a Dhamma talk, the Blessed One addressed the monks: 'Medicines to be taken by sick monks—namely, ghee, fresh butter, oil, honey, and molasses—may be accepted and consumed as a store for a maximum of seven days. Anyone who exceeds this limit is to be dealt with according to the rule.'

Pilindavacchavatthu niṭṭhitaṃ.

The story of Pilindavaccha is concluded.

Bhesajjānuññātabhāṇavāro niṭṭhito paṭhamo.

The first section on permitted medicines is concluded.

### 163. Guḷādianujānanā ^4

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv6-brahmali-pali#^4|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch5|BMC Chapter 5]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-MV6.4" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


163.Permission for Molasses, etc.

272. Atha kho bhagavā sāvatthiyaṃ yathābhirantaṃ viharitvā yena rājagahaṃ tena cārikaṃ pakkāmi. Addasā kho āyasmā kaṅkhārevato antarāmagge guḷakaraṇaṃ, okkamitvā guḷe piṭṭhampi chārikampi pakkhipante, disvāna ‘‘akappiyo guḷo sāmiso, na kappati guḷo vikāle paribhuñjitu’’nti kukkuccāyanto sapariso guḷaṃ na paribhuñjati. Yepissa sotabbaṃ maññanti, tepi guḷaṃ na paribhuñjanti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Kimatthāya [kimatthiyā (ka.)], bhikkhave, guḷe piṭṭhampi chārikampi pakkhipantīti? Thaddhatthāya [bandhanatthāya (sī. syā.)] bhagavāti. Sace, bhikkhave, thaddhatthāya guḷe piṭṭhampi chārikampi pakkhipanti, so ca guḷotveva saṅkhaṃ gacchati. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, yathāsukhaṃ guḷaṃ paribhuñjitunti.

272.Then the Blessed One, having stayed at Sāvatthī as long as he pleased, set out on a journey toward Rājagaha. On the way, Venerable Kaṅkhārevata saw them making molasses and observed them adding flour and ash to the molasses. Seeing this, he thought, 'This molasses is impure; it is not permissible to consume molasses at the wrong time,' and, being scrupulous, he and his group did not consume the molasses. Those who thought they should listen to him also did not consume the molasses. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. 'For what purpose, bhikkhus, do they add flour and ash to the molasses?' 'For firmness, Blessed One.' 'If, bhikkhus, they add flour and ash to the molasses for firmness, and it is still reckoned as molasses, I allow you, bhikkhus, to consume molasses as you please.'

Addasā kho āyasmā kaṅkhārevato antarāmagge vacce muggaṃ jātaṃ, passitvā ‘‘akappiyā muggā; pakkāpi muggā jāyantīti’’ kukkuccāyanto sapariso muggaṃ na paribhuñjati. Yepissa sotabbaṃ maññanti, tepi muggaṃ na paribhuñjanti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Sace [sacepi (?)], bhikkhave, pakkāpi muggā jāyanti, anujānāmi, bhikkhave, yathāsukhaṃ muggaṃ paribhuñjitunti.

The Venerable Kaṅkhārevata saw mung beans growing in excrement by the roadside. Upon seeing it, he thought, 'These mung beans are unallowable; even ripe mung beans sprout,' and, being scrupulous, he and his group did not consume the mung beans. Those who thought they should listen to him also did not consume the mung beans. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. 'If, monks, even ripe mung beans sprout, I allow you, monks, to consume the mung beans as you please.'

273. Tena kho pana samayena aññatarassa bhikkhuno udaravātābādho hoti. So loṇasovīrakaṃ apāyi. Tassa so udaravātābādho paṭippassambhi. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, gilānassa loṇasovīrakaṃ; agilānassa udakasambhinnaṃ pānaparibhogena paribhuñjitunti.

273.Now at that time a certain monk had an abdominal wind ailment. He drank salt-sour gruel. That abdominal wind ailment subsided for him. They reported the matter to the Blessed One. 'I allow, monks, salt-sour gruel for the sick; for the healthy, it may be consumed as a drink mixed with water.'

Guḷādianujānanā niṭṭhitā.

The allowance for molasses, etc., is concluded.

### 164. Antovuṭṭhādipaṭikkhepakathā ^5

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv6-brahmali-pali#^5|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch5|BMC Chapter 5]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-MV6.5" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


164.The Discussion on the Prohibition of What is Husked Inside, and So Forth

274. Atha kho bhagavā anupubbena cārikaṃ caramāno yena rājagahaṃ tadavasari. Tatra sudaṃ bhagavā rājagahe viharati veḷuvane kalandakanivāpe. Tena kho pana samayena bhagavato udaravātābādho hoti. Atha kho āyasmā ānando – ‘pubbepi bhagavato udaravātābādho tekaṭulayāguyā phāsu hotī’ti – sāmaṃ tilampi, taṇḍulampi, muggampi viññāpetvā, anto vāsetvā, anto sāmaṃ pacitvā bhagavato upanāmesi – ‘‘pivatu bhagavā tekaṭulayāgu’’nti. Jānantāpi tathāgatā pucchanti, jānantāpi na pucchanti; kālaṃ viditvā pucchanti, kālaṃ viditvā na pucchanti; atthasaṃhitaṃ tathāgatā pucchanti, no anatthasaṃhitaṃ. Anatthasaṃhite setughāto tathāgatānaṃ. Dvīhi ākārehi buddhā bhagavanto bhikkhū paṭipucchanti – dhammaṃ vā desessāma, sāvakānaṃ vā sikkhāpadaṃ paññapessāmāti. Atha kho bhagavā āyasmantaṃ ānandaṃ āmantesi – ‘‘kutāyaṃ, ānanda, yāgū’’ti? Atha kho āyasmā ānando bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesi. Vigarahi buddho bhagavā – ‘ananucchavikaṃ, ānanda, ananulomikaṃ, appatirūpaṃ, assāmaṇakaṃ, akappiyaṃ, akaraṇīyaṃ. Kathañhi nāma tvaṃ, ānanda, evarūpāya bāhullāya cetessasi. Yadapi, ānanda, anto vuṭṭhaṃ [vutthaṃ (sī. syā. ka.)] tadapi akappiyaṃ; yadapi anto pakkaṃ tadapi akappiyaṃ; yadapi sāmaṃ pakkaṃ, tadapi akappiyaṃ. Netaṃ, ānanda, appasannānaṃ vā pasādāya…pe… vigarahitvā dhammiṃ kathaṃ katvā bhikkhū āmantesi – ‘‘na, bhikkhave, anto vuṭṭhaṃ, anto pakkaṃ, sāmaṃ pakkaṃ paribhuñjitabbaṃ. Yo paribhuñjeya, āpatti dukkaṭassa. Anto ce, bhikkhave, vuṭṭhaṃ, anto pakkaṃ, sāmaṃ pakkaṃ tañce paribhuñjeyya, āpatti tiṇṇaṃ dukkaṭānaṃ. Anto ce, bhikkhave, vuṭṭhaṃ, anto pakkaṃ, aññehi pakkaṃ, tañce paribhuñjeyya, āpatti dvinnaṃ dukkaṭānaṃ. Anto ce, bhikkhave, vuṭṭhaṃ, bahi pakkaṃ, sāmaṃ pakkaṃ, tañce paribhuñjeyya, āpatti dvinnaṃ dukkaṭānaṃ. Bahi ce, bhikkhave, vuṭṭhaṃ, anto pakkaṃ, sāmaṃ pakkaṃ, tañce paribhuñjeyya, āpatti dvinnaṃ dukkaṭānaṃ. Anto ce, bhikkhave, vuṭṭhaṃ, bahi pakkaṃ, aññehi pakkaṃ, tañce paribhuñjeyya, āpatti dukkaṭassa. Bahi ce, bhikkhave, vuṭṭhaṃ, anto pakkaṃ, aññehi pakkaṃ, tañce paribhuñjeyya, āpatti dukkaṭassa. Bahi ce, bhikkhave, vuṭṭhaṃ, bahi pakkaṃ, sāmaṃ pakkaṃ, tañce paribhuñjeyya, āpatti dukkaṭassa. Bahi ce, bhikkhave, vuṭṭhaṃ, bahi pakkaṃ, aññehi pakkaṃ, tañce paribhuñjeyya, anāpattī’’’ti.

274.Then the Blessed One, wandering by degrees, arrived at Rājagaha. There the Blessed One was dwelling at Rājagaha, in the Bamboo Grove, the Squirrels’ Feeding Ground. At that time, the Blessed One was suffering from a wind ailment in his stomach. Then Venerable Ānanda—thinking, 'Previously, the Blessed One’s wind ailment in his stomach was relieved by a three-ingredient gruel'—personally requested sesame, rice, and mung beans, had them husked inside, and cooked them himself inside, and offered them to the Blessed One, saying, 'May the Blessed One drink this three-ingredient gruel.' The Tathāgatas ask questions knowing, and they do not ask questions knowing; they ask at the right time, and they do not ask questions at the wrong time. The Tathāgatas ask questions that are meaningful, not meaningless. For the Tathāgatas, meaningless talk is a barrier. The Buddhas, the Blessed Ones, question the monks in two ways: either to teach the Dhamma or to establish a training rule for the disciples. Then the Blessed One addressed Venerable Ānanda: 'Ānanda, where did this gruel come from?' Then Venerable Ānanda explained the matter to the Blessed One. The Blessed One rebuked him: 'Ānanda, this is unbefitting, unsuitable, inappropriate, unworthy of a contemplative, unallowable, and not to be done. How could you, Ānanda, intend such a profusion? Whatever is husked inside is unallowable; whatever is cooked inside is unallowable; whatever is cooked by oneself is unallowable. This, Ānanda, does not lead to the confidence of the unconfident…' Having rebuked him, the Blessed One gave a Dhamma talk and addressed the monks: 'Monks, one should not consume what is husked inside, cooked inside, or cooked by oneself. Whoever does so commits an offense of wrongdoing. If, monks, something is husked inside, cooked inside, and cooked by oneself, and one consumes it, one commits three offenses of wrongdoing. If, monks, something is husked inside, cooked inside, and cooked by others, and one consumes it, one commits two offenses of wrongdoing. If, monks, something is husked inside, cooked outside, and cooked by oneself, and one consumes it, one commits two offenses of wrongdoing. If, monks, something is husked outside, cooked inside, and cooked by oneself, and one consumes it, one commits two offenses of wrongdoing. If, monks, something is husked inside, cooked outside, and cooked by others, and one consumes it, one commits an offense of wrongdoing. If, monks, something is husked outside, cooked inside, and cooked by others, and one consumes it, one commits an offense of wrongdoing. If, monks, something is husked outside, cooked outside, and cooked by oneself, and one consumes it, one commits an offense of wrongdoing. If, monks, something is husked outside, cooked outside, and cooked by others, and one consumes it, there is no offense.'

Tena kho pana samayena bhikkhū ‘‘bhagavatā sāmaṃpāko paṭikkhitto’’ti puna pāke kukkuccāyanti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, puna pākaṃ pacitunti.

At that time, the monks, thinking, 'The Blessed One has prohibited cooking by oneself,' felt scruples about cooking again. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. 'Monks, I allow cooking again.'

Tena kho pana samayena rājagahaṃ dubbhikkhaṃ hoti. Manussā loṇampi, telampi, taṇḍulampi, khādanīyampi ārāmaṃ āharanti. Tāni bhikkhū bahi vāsenti; ukkapiṇḍakāpi khādanti, corāpi haranti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, anto vāsetunti. Anto vāsetvā bahi pācenti. Damakā parivārenti. Bhikkhū avissaṭṭhā paribhuñjanti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, anto pacitunti. Dubbhikkhe kappiyakārakā bahutaraṃ haranti, appataraṃ bhikkhūnaṃ denti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, sāmaṃ pacituṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, anto vuṭṭhaṃ, anto pakkaṃ, sāmaṃ pakkanti.

At that time, there was a famine in Rājagaha. People brought salt, oil, rice, and other food items to the monastery. The monks stored them outside; lumps of food were eaten by animals, and thieves stole them. They reported the matter to the Blessed One. 'Monks, I allow storing them inside.' After storing them inside, they cooked outside. Scavengers surrounded them. The monks consumed without being able to distribute it. They reported the matter to the Blessed One. 'Monks, I allow cooking inside.' During the famine, the attendants took more and gave less to the monks. They reported the matter to the Blessed One. 'Monks, I allow cooking by oneself.' 'Monks, I allow what is husked inside, cooked inside, and cooked by oneself.'

Antovuṭṭhādipaṭikkhepakathā niṭṭhitā.

The Discussion on the Prohibition of What is Husked Inside, and So Forth, is concluded.

### 165. Uggahitapaṭiggahaṇā ^6

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv6-brahmali-pali#^6|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch5|BMC Chapter 5]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-MV6.6" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


165.Taking Up and Receiving

275. Tena kho pana samayena sambahulā bhikkhū kāsīsu vassaṃvuṭṭhā rājagahaṃ gacchantā bhagavantaṃ dassanāya antarāmagge na labhiṃsu lūkhassa vā paṇītassa vā bhojanassa yāvadatthaṃ pāripūriṃ; bahuñca phalakhādanīyaṃ ahosi; kappiyakārako ca na ahosi. Atha kho te bhikkhū kilantarūpā yena rājagahaṃ veḷuvanaṃ kalandakanivāpo, yena bhagavā tenupasaṅkamiṃsu, upasaṅkamitvā bhagavantaṃ abhivādetvā ekamantaṃ nisīdiṃsu. Āciṇṇaṃ kho panetaṃ buddhānaṃ bhagavantānaṃ āgantukehi bhikkhūhi saddhiṃ paṭisammodituṃ. Atha kho bhagavā te bhikkhū etadavoca – ‘‘kacci, bhikkhave, khamanīyaṃ, kacci yāpanīyaṃ, kaccittha appakilamathena addhānaṃ āgatā; kuto ca tumhe, bhikkhave, āgacchathā’’ti? ‘‘Khamanīyaṃ bhagavā, yāpanīyaṃ bhagavā. Idha mayaṃ, bhante, kāsīsu vassaṃvuṭṭhā rājagahaṃ āgacchantā bhagavantaṃ dassanāya antarāmagge na labhimhā lūkhassa vā paṇītassa vā bhojanassa yāvadatthaṃ pāripūriṃ; bahuñca phalakhādanīyaṃ ahosi; kappiyakārako ca na ahosi; tena mayaṃ kilantarūpā addhānaṃ āgatā’’ti. Atha kho bhagavā etasmiṃ nidāne etasmiṃ pakaraṇe dhammiṃ kathaṃ katvā bhikkhū āmantesi – ‘‘anujānāmi, bhikkhave, yattha phalakhādanīyaṃ passati, kappiyakārako ca na hoti, sāmaṃ gahetvā, haritvā, kappiyakārake passitvā, bhūmiyaṃ nikkhipitvā, paṭiggahāpetvā paribhuñjituṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, uggahitaṃ paṭiggahitu’’nti.

275.At that time, a number of monks who had spent the Rains in Kāsi were traveling to Rājagaha to see the Blessed One. Along the way, they could not obtain a sufficient supply of either coarse or fine food, and there was much fruit to eat, but there was no steward to make it allowable. Then those monks, weary, approached the Blessed One at Rājagaha, in the Bamboo Grove, the Squirrels’ Sanctuary. Having approached, they paid homage to the Blessed One and sat down to one side. Now it is the custom for the Buddhas, the Blessed Ones, to exchange greetings with newly arrived monks. Then the Blessed One said to those monks: “I hope, monks, you are keeping well, I hope you are comfortable, I hope you have come without too much fatigue on the journey. And from where, monks, have you come?” “We are keeping well, Blessed One, we are comfortable, Blessed One. Venerable sir, we spent the Rains in Kāsi and were traveling to Rājagaha to see the Blessed One. Along the way, we could not obtain a sufficient supply of either coarse or fine food, and there was much fruit to eat, but there was no steward to make it allowable. Thus we have come weary from the journey.” Then the Blessed One, on this occasion, on this ground, having given a Dhamma talk, addressed the monks: “I allow, monks, that where one sees fruit to eat and there is no steward, one may take it oneself, carry it away, and after seeing a steward, place it on the ground, have it formally received, and then consume it. I allow, monks, that what has been taken up may be formally received.”

276. Tena kho pana samayena aññatarassa brāhmaṇassa navā ca tilā navañca madhu uppannā honti. Atha kho tassa brāhmaṇassa etadahosi – ‘‘yaṃnūnāhaṃ nave ca tile navañca madhuṃ buddhappamukhassa bhikkhusaṅghassa dadeyya’’nti. Atha kho so brāhmaṇo yena bhagavā tenupasaṅkami, upasaṅkamitvā bhagavatā saddhiṃ paṭisammodi, sammodanīyaṃ kathaṃ sāraṇīyaṃ vītisāretvā ekamantaṃ aṭṭhāsi. Ekamantaṃ ṭhito kho so brāhmaṇo bhagavantaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘adhivāsetu me bhavaṃ gotamo svātanāya bhattaṃ, saddhiṃ bhikkhusaṅghenā’’ti. Adhivāsesi bhagavā tuṇhībhāvena. Atha kho so brāhmaṇo bhagavato adhivāsanaṃ viditvā pakkāmi. Atha kho so brāhmaṇo tassā rattiyā accayena paṇītaṃ khādanīyaṃ bhojanīyaṃ paṭiyādāpetvā bhagavato kālaṃ ārocāpesi – ‘‘kālo, bho gotama, niṭṭhitaṃ bhatta’’nti. Atha kho bhagavā pubbaṇhasamayaṃ nivāsetvā pattacīvaramādāya yena tassa brāhmaṇassa nivesanaṃ tenupasaṅkami, upasaṅkamitvā paññatte āsane nisīdi, saddhiṃ bhikkhusaṅghena. Atha kho so brāhmaṇo buddhappamukhaṃ bhikkhusaṅghaṃ paṇītena khādanīyena bhojanīyena sahatthā santappetvā sampavāretvā bhagavantaṃ bhuttāviṃ onītapattapāṇiṃ ekamantaṃ nisīdi. Ekamantaṃ nisinnaṃ kho taṃ brāhmaṇaṃ bhagavā dhammiyā kathāya sandassetvā, samādapetvā, samuttejetvā, sampahaṃsetvā uṭṭhāyāsanā pakkāmi.

276.Now at that time, a certain brahmin had new sesame and new honey come into his possession. Then it occurred to that brahmin: 'Suppose I were to give the new sesame and new honey to the Saṅgha of monks headed by the Buddha.' Then that brahmin approached the Blessed One, exchanged greetings with him, and after pleasant and courteous conversation, stood to one side. Standing to one side, that brahmin said to the Blessed One: 'May the Venerable Gotama accept my meal for tomorrow together with the Saṅgha of monks.' The Blessed One consented with silence. Then that brahmin, knowing the Blessed One's consent, departed. Then, at the end of that night, that brahmin had fine food, hard and soft, prepared and announced the time to the Blessed One: 'It is time, Venerable Gotama, the meal is ready.' Then the Blessed One, having dressed in the morning, taking his bowl and robe, went to the residence of that brahmin. Having arrived, he sat down on the prepared seat together with the Saṅgha of monks. Then that brahmin personally served and satisfied the Saṅgha of monks, headed by the Buddha, with fine food, hard and soft, and invited them to take their fill. When the Blessed One had eaten and had withdrawn his hand from the bowl, the brahmin sat down to one side. Sitting to one side, the Blessed One instructed, roused, inspired, and gladdened that brahmin with a Dhamma talk. Then he rose from his seat and departed.

Atha kho tassa brāhmaṇassa acirapakkantassa bhagavato etadahosi – ‘‘yesaṃ kho mayā atthāya buddhappamukho bhikkhusaṅgho nimantito, ‘nave ca tile navañca madhuṃ dassāmī’ti, te mayā pamuṭṭhā dātuṃ. Yaṃnūnāhaṃ nave ca tile navañca madhuṃ kolambehi ca ghaṭehi ca ārāmaṃ harāpeyya’’nti. Atha kho so brāhmaṇo nave ca tile navañca madhuṃ kolambehi ca ghaṭehi ca ārāmaṃ harāpetvā yena bhagavā tenupasaṅkami, upasaṅkamitvā ekamantaṃ aṭṭhāsi. Ekamantaṃ ṭhito kho so brāhmaṇo bhagavantaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘yesaṃ kho mayā, bho gotama, atthāya buddhappamukho bhikkhusaṅgho nimantito, ‘nave ca tile navañca madhuṃ dassāmī’ti, te mayā pamuṭṭhā dātuṃ. Paṭiggaṇhātu me bhavaṃ gotamo nave ca tile navañca madhu’’nti. Tena hi, brāhmaṇa, bhikkhūnaṃ dehīti. Tena kho pana samayena bhikkhū dubbhikkhe appamattakepi pavārenti, paṭisaṅkhāpi paṭikkhipanti, sabbo ca saṅgho pavārito hoti. Bhikkhū kukkuccāyantā na paṭiggaṇhanti. Paṭiggaṇhatha, bhikkhave, paribhuñjatha. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, tato nīhaṭaṃ bhuttāvinā pavāritena anatirittaṃ paribhuñjitunti.

Then, soon after the Blessed One had departed, it occurred to that brahmin: 'I invited the Saṅgha of monks with the Buddha at its head, intending to give new sesame and new honey, but I forgot to give them. Suppose I were to have the new sesame and new honey brought to the monastery in pails and jars.' Then that brahmin had new sesame and new honey brought to the monastery in pails and jars. He approached the Blessed One, stood to one side, and said: 'Venerable Gotama, I invited the Saṅgha of monks with the Buddha at its head, intending to give new sesame and new honey, but I forgot to give them. May the Venerable Gotama accept from me the new sesame and new honey.' 'Then, brahmin, give it to the monks.' Now at that time, during a famine, the monks were content with very little. They reflected and declined, and the entire Saṅgha had concluded their meal. The monks, being scrupulous, did not accept it. 'Accept it, monks, and consume it. I allow you, monks, to consume what is brought forth from that, even by one who has eaten and concluded the meal, provided it is not a surplus.'

Uggahitapaṭiggahaṇā niṭṭhitā.

The section on Taking Up and Receiving is concluded.

### 166. Paṭiggahitādianujānanā ^7

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv6-brahmali-pali#^7|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch5|BMC Chapter 5]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-MV6.7" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


166.Allowance concerning what has been received, and so forth

277. [pāci. 295] Tena kho pana samayena āyasmato upanandassa sakyaputtassa upaṭṭhākakulaṃ saṅghassatthāya khādanīyaṃ pāhesi – ayyassa upanandassa dassetvā saṅghassa dātabbanti. Tena kho pana samayena āyasmā upanando sakyaputto gāmaṃ piṇḍāya paviṭṭho hoti. Atha kho te manussā ārāmaṃ gantvā bhikkhū pucchiṃsu – ‘‘kahaṃ, bhante, ayyo upanando’’ti? ‘‘Esāvuso, āyasmā upanando sakyaputto gāmaṃ piṇḍāya paviṭṭho’’ti. ‘‘Idaṃ, bhante, khādanīyaṃ ayyassa upanandassa dassetvā saṅghassa dātabba’’nti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Tena hi, bhikkhave, paṭiggahetvā nikkhipatha yāva upanando āgacchatīti. Atha kho āyasmā upanando sakyaputto purebhattaṃ kulāni payirupāsitvā divā āgacchati. Tena kho pana samayena bhikkhū dubbhikkhe appamattakepi pavārenti, paṭisaṅkhāpi paṭikkhipanti, sabbo ca saṅgho pavārito hoti, bhikkhū kukkuccāyantā na paṭiggaṇhanti. Paṭiggaṇhatha, bhikkhave, paribhuñjatha. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, purebhattaṃ paṭiggahitaṃ bhuttāvinā pavāritena anatirittaṃ paribhuñjitunti.

277.At that time, a lay supporter family of the Venerable Upananda the Sakyan sent some edibles for the Saṅgha, saying, “After showing them to the Venerable Upananda, they are to be given to the Saṅgha.” At that time, the Venerable Upananda the Sakyan had entered a village for alms. Then those people went to the monastery and asked the bhikkhus, “Where, sirs, is the Venerable Upananda?” “Friends, the Venerable Upananda the Sakyan has entered a village for alms.” “Sirs, these edibles are to be given to the Saṅgha after showing them to the Venerable Upananda.” They reported the matter to the Blessed One. “Then, bhikkhus, receive it and put it aside until Upananda returns.” Then the Venerable Upananda the Sakyan, having visited families before the meal, returned during the day. At that time, during a famine, the bhikkhus would declare satisfaction even for small amounts, or decline after reflection, and the entire Saṅgha had made the declaration of satisfaction. The bhikkhus, being scrupulous, did not accept it. “Receive it, bhikkhus, and consume it. I allow, bhikkhus, that what was received before the meal may be consumed by one who has eaten and made the declaration of satisfaction, provided it is not leftover.”

278. Atha kho bhagavā rājagahe yathābhirantaṃ viharitvā yena sāvatthi tena cārikaṃ pakkāmi. Anupubbena cārikaṃ caramāno yena sāvatthi tadavasari. Tatra sudaṃ bhagavā sāvatthiyaṃ viharati jetavane anāthapiṇḍikassa ārāme. Tena kho pana samayena āyasmato sāriputtassa kāyaḍāhābādho hoti. Atha kho āyasmā mahāmoggallāno yenāyasmā sāriputto tenupasaṅkami, upasaṅkamitvā āyasmantaṃ sāriputtaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘pubbe te, āvuso sāriputta, kāyaḍāhābādho kena phāsu hotī’’ti? ‘‘Bhisehi ca me, āvuso, muḷālikāhi cā’’ti. Atha kho āyasmā mahāmoggallāno seyyathāpi nāma balavā puriso sammiñjitaṃ vā bāhaṃ pasāreyya, pasāritaṃ vā bāhaṃ samiñjeyya, evameva jetavane antarahito mandākiniyā pokkharaṇiyā tīre pāturahosi. Addasā kho aññataro nāgo āyasmantaṃ mahāmoggallānaṃ dūratova āgacchantaṃ, disvāna āyasmantaṃ mahāmoggallānaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘etu kho, bhante, ayyo mahāmoggallāno. Svāgataṃ, bhante, ayyassa mahāmoggallānassa. Kena, bhante, ayyassa attho; kiṃ dammī’’ti? ‘‘Bhisehi ca me, āvuso, attho, muḷālikāhi cā’’ti. Atha kho so nāgo aññataraṃ nāgaṃ āṇāpesi – ‘‘tena hi, bhaṇe, ayyassa bhise ca muḷālikāyo ca yāvadatthaṃ dehī’’ti. Atha kho so nāgo mandākiniṃ pokkharaṇiṃ ogāhetvā, soṇḍāya bhisañca muḷālikañca abbāhitvā, suvikkhālitaṃ vikkhāletvā, bhaṇḍikaṃ bandhitvā yenāyasmā mahāmoggallāno tenupasaṅkami. Atha kho āyasmā mahāmoggallāno – seyyathāpi nāma balavā puriso samiñjitaṃ vā bāhaṃ pasāreyya, pasāritaṃ vā bāhaṃ samiñjeyya, evameva – mandākiniyā pokkharaṇiyā tīre antarahito jetavane pāturahosi. Sopi kho nāgo mandākiniyā pokkharaṇiyā tīre antarahito jetavane pāturahosi. Atha kho so nāgo āyasmato mahāmoggallānassa bhise ca muḷālikāyo ca paṭiggahāpetvā jetavane antarahito mandākiniyā pokkharaṇiyā tīre pāturahosi. Atha kho āyasmā mahāmoggallāno āyasmato sāriputtassa bhise ca muḷālikāyo ca upanāmesi. Atha kho āyasmato sāriputtassa bhise ca muḷālikāyo ca bhuttassa kāyaḍāhābādho paṭippassambhi. Bahū bhisā ca muḷālikāyo ca avasiṭṭhā honti. Tena kho pana samayena bhikkhū dubbhikkhe appamattakepi pavārenti, paṭisaṅkhāpi paṭikkhipanti, sabbo ca saṅgho pavārito hoti. Bhikkhū kukkuccāyantā na paṭiggaṇhanti. Paṭiggaṇhatha, bhikkhave, paribhuñjatha. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, vanaṭṭhaṃ pokkharaṭṭhaṃ bhuttāvinā pavāritena anatirittaṃ paribhuñjitunti.

278.Then the Blessed One, having stayed in Rājagaha as long as he pleased, set out on a journey to Sāvatthī. Traveling in stages, he eventually arrived at Sāvatthī. There the Blessed One stayed in Jeta Grove, Anāthapiṇḍika’s Monastery. At that time, the Venerable Sāriputta was suffering from a bodily burning ailment. Then the Venerable Mahāmoggallāna approached the Venerable Sāriputta and said, “Friend Sāriputta, in the past, what brought you relief from this bodily burning ailment?” “Friend, lotus roots and stalks brought me relief.” Then the Venerable Mahāmoggallāna—just as a strong man might extend his bent arm or bend his extended arm—vanished from Jeta Grove and reappeared on the shore of the Mandākinī Pond. A certain nāga saw the Venerable Mahāmoggallāna approaching from afar and, having seen him, said to the Venerable Mahāmoggallāna, “Come, venerable sir, the Venerable Mahāmoggallāna! Welcome, venerable sir, the Venerable Mahāmoggallāna! What do you need, venerable sir? What shall I give?” “Friend, I need lotus roots and stalks.” Then that nāga instructed another nāga, “Well then, friend, give the Venerable as many lotus roots and stalks as he needs.” Then that nāga entered the Mandākinī Pond, scooped up lotus roots and stalks with his trunk, thoroughly washed them, tied them into a bundle, and approached the Venerable Mahāmoggallāna. Then the Venerable Mahāmoggallāna—just as a strong man might extend his bent arm or bend his extended arm—vanished from the shore of the Mandākinī Pond and reappeared in Jeta Grove. That nāga also vanished from the shore of the Mandākinī Pond and reappeared in Jeta Grove. Then that nāga, after the Venerable Mahāmoggallāna had received the lotus roots and stalks, vanished from Jeta Grove and reappeared on the shore of the Mandākinī Pond. Then the Venerable Mahāmoggallāna offered the lotus roots and stalks to the Venerable Sāriputta. After the Venerable Sāriputta had consumed the lotus roots and stalks, his bodily burning ailment subsided. Many lotus roots and stalks remained. At that time, during a famine, the bhikkhus would declare satisfaction even for small amounts, or decline after reflection, and the entire Saṅgha had made the declaration of satisfaction. The bhikkhus, being scrupulous, did not accept them. “Receive them, bhikkhus, and consume them. I allow, bhikkhus, to consume forest roots and lotus-pond roots by one who has eaten and made the declaration of satisfaction, provided they are not leftover.”

Tena kho pana samayena sāvatthiyaṃ bahuṃ phalakhādanīyaṃ uppannaṃ hoti, kappiyakārako ca na hoti. Bhikkhū kukkuccāyantā phalaṃ na paribhuñjanti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, abījaṃ nibbattabījaṃ [nibbaṭṭabījaṃ (sī.), nibbaṭabījaṃ (syā.), nippaṭṭabījaṃ (ka.)] akatakappaṃ phalaṃ paribhuñjitunti.

At that time, a great quantity of fruit edibles had arisen in Sāvatthī, but there was no one to make it allowable. The bhikkhus, being scrupulous, did not partake of the fruit. They reported the matter to the Blessed One. “I allow, bhikkhus, to consume fruit that is seedless, or with seeds removed, or that has not been made allowable.”

Paṭiggahitādi anujānanā niṭṭhitā.

The allowance concerning what has been received, and so forth, is concluded.

### 167. Satthakammapaṭikkhepakathā ^8
