> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv6-brahmali-pali#^8|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch5|BMC Chapter 5]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-MV6.8" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


167.The Discourse on the Prohibition of Surgical Operations.

279. Atha kho bhagavā sāvatthiyaṃ yathābhirantaṃ viharitvā yena rājagahaṃ tena cārikaṃ pakkāmi. Anupubbena cārikaṃ caramāno yena rājagahaṃ tadavasari. Tatra sudaṃ bhagavā rājagahe viharati veḷuvane kalandakanivāpe. Tena kho pana samayena aññatarassa bhikkhuno bhagandalābādho hoti. Ākāsagotto vejjo satthakammaṃ karoti. Atha kho bhagavā senāsanacārikaṃ āhiṇḍanto yena tassa bhikkhuno vihāro tenupasaṅkami. Addasā kho ākāsagotto vejjo bhagavantaṃ dūratova āgacchantaṃ, disvāna bhagavantaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘āgacchatu bhavaṃ gotamo, imassa bhikkhuno vaccamaggaṃ passatu, seyyathāpi godhāmukha’’nti. Atha kho bhagavā – ‘‘so maṃ khvāyaṃ moghapuriso uppaṇḍetī’’ti – tatova paṭinivattitvā, etasmiṃ nidāne etasmiṃ pakaraṇe bhikkhusaṅghaṃ sannipātāpetvā, bhikkhū paṭipucchi – ‘‘atthi kira, bhikkhave, amukasmiṃ vihāre bhikkhu gilāno’’ti? ‘‘Atthi bhagavā’’ti. ‘‘Kiṃ tassa, bhikkhave, bhikkhuno ābādho’’ti? ‘‘Tassa, bhante, āyasmato bhagandalābādho, ākāsagotto vejjo satthakammaṃ karotī’’ti. Vigarahi buddho bhagavā – ‘‘ananucchavikaṃ, bhikkhave, tassa moghapurisassa, ananulomikaṃ, appatirūpaṃ, assāmaṇakaṃ, akappiyaṃ, akaraṇīyaṃ. Kathañhi nāma so, bhikkhave, moghapuriso sambādhe satthakammaṃ kārāpessati. Sambādhe, bhikkhave, sukhumā chavi, duropayo vaṇo, dupparihāraṃ satthaṃ. Netaṃ, bhikkhave, appasannānaṃ vā pasādāya…pe… vigarahitvā…pe… dhammiṃ kathaṃ katvā bhikkhū āmantesi – ‘‘na, bhikkhave, sambādhe satthakammaṃ kārāpetabbaṃ. Yo kārāpeyya, āpatti thullaccayassā’’ti.

279.Then the Blessed One, having stayed at Sāvatthī as long as he pleased, set out on a journey toward Rājagaha. Traveling in stages, he eventually arrived at Rājagaha. There the Blessed One stayed in the Bamboo Grove, at the Squirrels’ Feeding Place. At that time, a certain monk was suffering from a fistula. The physician Ākāsagotta was performing surgery. Then the Blessed One, while walking around for lodgings, approached that monk’s residence. The physician Ākāsagotta saw the Blessed One coming from afar and, upon seeing him, said to the Blessed One: “Let the venerable Gotama come and see this monk’s anus, like the mouth of a monitor lizard.” Then the Blessed One thought, “This foolish man is mocking me,” and turned back right there. On this occasion, in this matter, he had the Sangha of monks assembled and questioned the monks: “Monks, is there a sick monk in such-and-such a dwelling?” “There is, Blessed One.” “What is the illness of that monk, monks?” “Venerable sir, that venerable one has a fistula. The physician Ākāsagotta is performing surgery.” The Buddha, the Blessed One, rebuked him: “It is inappropriate, monks, for that foolish man, unsuitable, improper, unworthy of a renunciate, impermissible, not to be done. How, monks, could that foolish man have surgery performed in a confined space? In a confined space, monks, the skin is delicate, the wound is difficult to heal, and the surgical instrument is difficult to handle. This, monks, will not inspire confidence in those who are without confidence…” Having rebuked him… he gave a Dhamma talk and addressed the monks: “Monks, surgery should not be performed in a confined space. Whoever does so commits a grave offense.”

Tena kho pana samayena chabbaggiyā bhikkhū – bhagavatā satthakammaṃ paṭikkhittanti – vatthikammaṃ kārāpenti. Ye te bhikkhū appicchā, te ujjhāyanti khiyyanti vipācenti – ‘‘kathañhi nāma chabbaggiyā bhikkhū vatthikammaṃ kārāpessantī’’ti. Atha kho te bhikkhū bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. ‘‘Saccaṃ kira, bhikkhave, chabbaggiyā bhikkhū vatthikammaṃ kārāpentī’’ti? ‘‘Saccaṃ bhagavā’’ti…pe… vigarahitvā dhammiṃ kathaṃ katvā bhikkhū āmantesi – ‘‘na, bhikkhave, sambādhassa sāmantā dvaṅgulā satthakammaṃ vā vatthikammaṃ vā kārāpetabbaṃ. Yo kārāpeyya, āpatti thullaccayassā’’ti.

At that time the monks of the group of six, thinking, "The Blessed One has prohibited surgery," had enemas performed. The monks who were modest complained, criticized, and protested: "How can the monks of the group of six have enemas performed?" Then those monks reported the matter to the Blessed One. "Is it true, monks, that the monks of the group of six are having enemas performed?" "It is true, Blessed One."… Having rebuked them… he gave a Dhamma talk and addressed the monks: "Monks, neither surgery nor an enema should be performed within two fingerbreadths of a confined space. Whoever does so commits a grave offense."

Satthakammapaṭikkhepakathā niṭṭhitā.

The Discourse on the Prohibition of Surgical Operations is concluded.

### 168. Manussamaṃsapaṭikkhepakathā ^9

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv6-brahmali-pali#^9|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch5|BMC Chapter 5]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-MV6.9" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


168.The Discourse on the Prohibition of Human Flesh.

280. Atha kho bhagavā rājagahe yathābhirantaṃ viharitvā yena bārāṇasī tena cārikaṃ pakkāmi. Anupubbena cārikaṃ caramāno yena bārāṇasī tadavasari. Tatra sudaṃ bhagavā bārāṇasiyaṃ viharati isipatane migadāye. Tena kho pana samayena bārāṇasiyaṃ suppiyo ca upāsako suppiyā ca upāsikā ubhatopasannā honti, dāyakā, kārakā, saṅghupaṭṭhākā. Atha kho suppiyā upāsikā ārāmaṃ gantvā vihārena vihāraṃ pariveṇena pariveṇaṃ upasaṅkamitvā bhikkhū pucchati – ‘‘ko, bhante, gilāno, kassa kiṃ āhariyatū’’ti? Tena kho pana samayena aññatarena bhikkhunā virecanaṃ pītaṃ hoti. Atha kho so bhikkhu suppiyaṃ upāsikaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘mayā kho, bhagini, virecanaṃ pītaṃ. Attho me paṭicchādanīyenā’’ti. ‘‘Suṭṭhu, ayya, āhariyissatī’’ti gharaṃ gantvā antevāsiṃ āṇāpesi – ‘‘gaccha, bhaṇe, pavattamaṃsaṃ jānāhī’’ti. Evaṃ, ayyeti kho so puriso suppiyāya upāsikāya paṭissuṇitvā kevalakappaṃ bārāṇasiṃ āhiṇḍanto na addasa pavattamaṃsaṃ. Atha kho so puriso yena suppiyā upāsikā tenupasaṅkami, upasaṅkamitvā suppiyaṃ upāsikaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘natthayye pavattamaṃsaṃ. Māghāto ajjā’’ti. Atha kho suppiyāya upāsikāya etadahosi – ‘‘tassa kho gilānassa bhikkhuno paṭicchādanīyaṃ alabhantassa ābādho vā abhivaḍḍhissati, kālaṅkiriyā vā bhavissati. Na kho metaṃ patirūpaṃ yāhaṃ paṭissuṇitvā na harāpeyya’’nti. Potthanikaṃ gahetvā ūrumaṃsaṃ ukkantitvā dāsiyā adāsi – ‘‘handa, je, imaṃ maṃsaṃ sampādetvā amukasmiṃ vihāre bhikkhu gilāno, tassa dajjāhi. Yo ca maṃ pucchati, ‘gilānā’ti paṭivedehī’’ti. Uttarāsaṅgena ūruṃ veṭhetvā ovarakaṃ pavisitvā mañcake nipajji. Atha kho suppiyo upāsako gharaṃ gantvā dāsiṃ pucchi – ‘‘kahaṃ suppiyā’’ti? ‘‘Esāyya ovarake nipannā’’ti. Atha kho suppiyo upāsako yena suppiyā upāsikā tenupasaṅkami, upasaṅkamitvā suppiyaṃ upāsikaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘kissa nipannāsī’’ti? ‘‘Gilānāmhī’’ti. ‘‘Kiṃ te ābādho’’ti? Atha kho suppiyā upāsikā suppiyassa upāsakassa etamatthaṃ ārocesi. Atha kho suppiyo upāsako – acchariyaṃ vata bho! Abbhutaṃ vata bho! Yāva saddhāyaṃ suppiyā pasannā, yatra hi nāma attanopi maṃsāni pariccattāni! Kimpimāya [kiṃ panimāya (sī. syā.)] aññaṃ kiñci adeyyaṃ bhavissatīti – haṭṭho udaggo yena bhagavā tenupasaṅkami, upasaṅkamitvā bhagavantaṃ abhivādetvā ekamantaṃ nisīdi. Ekamantaṃ nisinno kho suppiyo upāsako bhagavantaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘adhivāsetu me, bhante, bhagavā svātanāya bhattaṃ, saddhiṃ bhikkhusaṅghenā’’ti. Adhivāsesi bhagavā tuṇhībhāvena. Atha kho suppiyo upāsako bhagavato adhivāsanaṃ viditvā uṭṭhāyāsanā bhagavantaṃ abhivādetvā padakkhiṇaṃ katvā pakkāmi. Atha kho suppiyo upāsako tassā rattiyā accayena paṇītaṃ khādanīyaṃ bhojanīyaṃ paṭiyādāpetvā bhagavato kālaṃ ārocāpesi – ‘‘kālo, bhante, niṭṭhitaṃ bhatta’’nti. Atha kho bhagavā pubbaṇhasamayaṃ nivāsetvā pattacīvaramādāya yena suppiyassa upāsakassa nivesanaṃ tenupasaṅkami, upasaṅkamitvā paññatte āsane nisīdi, saddhiṃ bhikkhusaṅghena. Atha kho suppiyo upāsako yena bhagavā tenupasaṅkami, upasaṅkamitvā bhagavantaṃ abhivādetvā ekamantaṃ aṭṭhāsi. Ekamantaṃ ṭhitaṃ kho suppiyaṃ upāsakaṃ bhagavā etadavoca – ‘‘kahaṃ suppiyā’’ti? ‘‘Gilānā bhagavā’’ti. ‘‘Tena hi āgacchatū’’ti. ‘‘Na bhagavā ussahatī’’ti. ‘‘Tena hi pariggahetvāpi ānethā’’ti. Atha kho suppiyo upāsako suppiyaṃ upāsikaṃ pariggahetvā ānesi. Tassā, saha dassanena bhagavato, tāva mahāvaṇo ruḷaho ahosi, succhavilomajāto. Atha kho suppiyo ca upāsako suppiyā ca upāsikā – ‘‘acchariyaṃ vata bho! Abbhutaṃ vata bho! Tathāgatassa mahiddhikatā mahānubhāvatā, yatra hi nāma saha dassanena bhagavato tāva mahāvaṇo ruḷaho bhavissati, succhavilomajāto’’ti – haṭṭhā udaggā buddhappamukhaṃ bhikkhusaṅghaṃ paṇītena khādanīyena bhojanīyena sahatthā santappetvā sampavāretvā bhagavantaṃ bhuttāviṃ onītapattapāṇiṃ ekamantaṃ nisīdiṃsu. Atha kho bhagavā suppiyañca upāsakaṃ suppiyañca upāsikaṃ dhammiyā kathāya sandassetvā samādapetvā samuttejetvā sampahaṃsetvā uṭṭhāyāsanā pakkāmi.

280.Then the Blessed One, having stayed in Rājagaha as long as he pleased, set out on a journey to Bārāṇasī. Traveling in stages, he arrived at Bārāṇasī. There the Blessed One stayed in the Deer Park at Isipatana near Bārāṇasī.At that time in Bārāṇasī, there were two lay followers named Suppiya and Suppiyā, both devout, generous, helpful, and supporters of the Sangha. One day, Suppiyā the lay follower went to the monastery and went from dwelling to dwelling, from cell to cell, asking the monks: "Venerable sirs, who is sick? What should be brought for whom?"At that time, a certain monk had taken a purgative. That monk said to Suppiyā the lay follower: "Sister, I have taken a purgative. I need something restorative.""Very well, sir, it will be brought," she replied. She went home and instructed her servant: "Go, my dear, find some suitable meat.""Yes, madam," the servant replied. But after wandering all over Bārāṇasī, he could not find any suitable meat. Then the servant returned to Suppiyā the lay follower and said: "Madam, there is no suitable meat. Today is a day of non-killing."Then Suppiyā the lay follower thought: "If that sick monk does not get something restorative, his illness may worsen, or he may even die. It would not be proper for me to promise and then not deliver." Taking a sharp knife, she cut a piece of flesh from her thigh, gave it to a maid, and said: "Here, my dear, prepare this meat and give it to the sick monk in such-and-such dwelling. If anyone asks, say that the giver is sick." Then she wrapped her thigh with her upper robe, entered her chamber, and lay down on the bed.When Suppiya the lay follower returned home, he asked the maid: "Where is Suppiyā?" "Sir, she is lying down in the chamber." Then Suppiya the lay follower went to Suppiyā and asked: "Why are you lying down?" "I am sick." "What is your ailment?" Then Suppiyā the lay follower told him what had happened.Suppiya the lay follower was amazed and astonished: "How extraordinary! How wonderful! How deeply devoted Suppiyā is, that she would even give up her own flesh! What else would she not give?" Delighted and elated, he went to the Blessed One, paid homage, sat down to one side, and said: "Venerable sir, may the Blessed One accept tomorrow’s meal from me together with the Sangha of monks." The Blessed One consented by silence.Knowing the Blessed One had accepted, Suppiya rose from his seat, paid homage, circumambulated the Blessed One, and departed. When the night had passed, he had fine food prepared and announced the time to the Blessed One: "Venerable sir, it is time. The meal is ready."Then the Blessed One, having dressed in the morning, took his bowl and robe, and went to Suppiya’s residence, where he sat down on the prepared seat together with the Sangha of monks. Suppiya the lay follower approached the Blessed One, paid homage, and stood to one side. The Blessed One asked him: "Where is Suppiyā?" "She is sick, Blessed One." "Then let her come." "She is not able, Blessed One." "Then bring her here supporting her." So Suppiya the lay follower brought Suppiyā supporting her.As soon as she saw the Blessed One, the large wound on her thigh healed completely, with fine hair growing over it. Suppiya and Suppiyā the lay followers were amazed and astonished: "How extraordinary! How wonderful! The Tathāgata possesses such great power and might, that simply by seeing him, the large wound on her thigh healed completely, with fine hair growing over it!" Delighted and elated, they personally served the Sangha of monks headed by the Buddha with fine food. When the Blessed One had finished eating and had put away his bowl, they sat down to one side.Then the Blessed One instructed, encouraged, inspired, and gladdened Suppiya and Suppiyā the lay followers with a Dhamma talk. Having done so, he rose from his seat and departed.

Atha kho bhagavā etasmiṃ nidāne etasmiṃ pakaraṇe bhikkhusaṅghaṃ sannipātāpetvā bhikkhū

Then, on this occasion, in this matter, the Blessed One had the Sangha of monks assembled and questioned the monks:

Paṭipucchi – ‘‘ko, bhikkhave, suppiyaṃ upāsikaṃ maṃsaṃ viññāpesī’’ti? Evaṃ vutte so bhikkhu bhagavantaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘ahaṃ kho, bhante, suppiyaṃ upāsikaṃ maṃsaṃ viññāpesi’’nti. ‘‘Āhariyittha bhikkhū’’ti? ‘‘Āhariyittha bhagavā’’ti. ‘‘Paribhuñji tvaṃ bhikkhū’’ti? ‘‘Paribhuñjāmahaṃ bhagavā’’ti. ‘‘Paṭivekkhi tvaṃ bhikkhū’’ti? ‘‘Nāhaṃ bhagavā paṭivekkhi’’nti. Vigarahi buddho bhagavā…pe… kathañhi nāma tvaṃ, moghapurisa, appaṭivekkhitvā maṃsaṃ paribhuñjissasi. Manussamaṃsaṃ kho tayā, moghapurisa, paribhuttaṃ. Netaṃ, moghapurisa, appasannānaṃ vā pasādāya…pe… vigarahitvā dhammiṃ kathaṃ katvā bhikkhū āmantesi – ‘‘santi, bhikkhave, manussā saddhā pasannā, tehi attanopi maṃsāni pariccattāni. Na, bhikkhave, manussamaṃsaṃ paribhuñjitabbaṃ. Yo paribhuñjeyya, āpatti thullaccayassa. Na ca, bhikkhave, appaṭivekkhitvā maṃsaṃ paribhuñjitabbaṃ. Yo paribhuñjeyya, āpatti dukkaṭassā’’ti.

He questioned, "Who, monk, requested meat from Suppiya the laywoman?" When this was said, that monk replied to the Blessed One, "I, venerable sir, requested meat from Suppiya the laywoman." "Was it brought, monk?" "It was brought, Blessed One." "Did you eat it, monk?" "I ate it, Blessed One." "Did you examine it, monk?" "I did not examine it, Blessed One." The Blessed One, the Buddha, rebuked him... "How could you, foolish man, eat meat without examining it? You have eaten human flesh, foolish man! This is not, foolish man, for inspiring confidence in the faithless...!" Having rebuked him and given a Dhamma talk, he addressed the monks: "Monks, there are faithful and devoted people who even sacrifice their own flesh. Monks, human flesh should not be eaten. Whoever eats it commits a grave offense. And, monks, meat should not be eaten without examining it. Whoever eats it commits an offense of wrong-doing."

Manussamaṃsapaṭikkhepakathā niṭṭhitā.

The Discourse on the Prohibition of Human Flesh is concluded.

### 169. Hatthimaṃsādipaṭikkhepakathā ^10

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv6-brahmali-pali#^10|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch5|BMC Chapter 5]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-MV6.10" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


169.The Account of the Prohibition of Elephant Meat and So Forth

281. Tena kho pana samayena rañño hatthī maranti. Manussā dubbhikkhe hatthimaṃsaṃ paribhuñjanti, bhikkhūnaṃ piṇḍāya carantānaṃ hatthimaṃsaṃ denti. Bhikkhū hatthimaṃsaṃ paribhuñjanti. Manussā ujjhāyanti khiyyanti vipācenti – ‘‘kathañhi nāma samaṇā sakyaputtiyā hatthimaṃsaṃ paribhuñjissanti. Rājaṅgaṃ hatthī, sace rājā jāneyya, na nesaṃ attamano assā’’ti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Na, bhikkhave, hatthimaṃsaṃ paribhuñjitabbaṃ. Yo paribhuñjeyya, āpatti dukkaṭassāti.

281.Now at that time, the king’s elephants died. People, suffering from famine, were eating elephant meat, and gave elephant meat to the bhikkhus who were on their almsround. The bhikkhus ate the elephant meat. People grumbled, complained, and spread it about: “How can these Sakyan recluses eat elephant meat? An elephant is royal property. If the king were to know, he would not be pleased with them.” They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, elephant meat should not be eaten. Whoever eats it commits a dukkata offense.”

Tena kho pana samayena rañño assā maranti. Manussā dubbhikkhe assamaṃsaṃ paribhuñjanti, bhikkhūnaṃ piṇḍāya carantānaṃ assamaṃsaṃ denti. Bhikkhū assamaṃsaṃ paribhuñjanti. Manussā ujjhāyanti khiyyanti vipācenti – ‘‘kathañhi nāma samaṇā sakyaputtiyā assamaṃsaṃ paribhuñjissanti. Rājaṅgaṃ assā, sace rājā jāneyya, na nesaṃ attamano assā’’ti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Na, bhikkhave, assamaṃsaṃ paribhuñjitabbaṃ. Yo paribhuñjeyya, āpatti dukkaṭassāti.

Now at that time, the king’s horses died. People, suffering from famine, were eating horse meat, and gave horse meat to the bhikkhus who were on their almsround. The bhikkhus ate the horse meat. People grumbled, complained, and spread it about: “How can these Sakyan recluses eat horse meat? A horse is royal property. If the king were to know, he would not be pleased with them.” They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, horse meat should not be eaten. Whoever eats it commits a dukkata offense.”

Tena kho pana samayena manussā dubbhikkhe sunakhamaṃsaṃ paribhuñjanti, bhikkhūnaṃ piṇḍāya carantānaṃ sunakhamaṃsaṃ denti. Bhikkhū sunakhamaṃsaṃ paribhuñjanti. Manussā ujjhāyanti khiyyanti vipācenti – ‘‘kathañhi nāma samaṇā sakyaputtiyā sunakhamaṃsaṃ paribhuñjissanti, jeguccho sunakho paṭikūlo’’ti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Na, bhikkhave, sunakhamaṃsaṃ paribhuñjitabbaṃ. Yo paribhuñjeyya, āpatti dukkaṭassāti.

Now at that time, people, suffering from famine, were eating dog meat. When the bhikkhus went for alms, they gave dog meat to them. The bhikkhus ate the dog meat. The people grumbled, complained, and spread it about: “How can these Sakyan recluses eat dog meat? A dog is disgusting and repulsive!” They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, dog meat should not be eaten. Whoever eats it commits a dukkata offense.”

Tena kho pana samayena manussā dubbhikkhe ahimaṃsaṃ paribhuñjanti, bhikkhūnaṃ piṇḍāya carantānaṃ ahimaṃsaṃ denti. Bhikkhū ahimaṃsaṃ paribhuñjanti. Manussā ujjhāyanti khiyyanti vipācenti – ‘‘kathañhi nāma samaṇā sakyaputtiyā ahimaṃsaṃ paribhuñjissanti, jeguccho ahi paṭikūlo’’ti. Supassopi [suphasso (sī.)] nāgarājā yena bhagavā tenupasaṅkami, upasaṅkamitvā bhagavantaṃ abhivādetvā ekamantaṃ aṭṭhāsi. Ekamantaṃ ṭhito kho supasso nāgarājā bhagavantaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘santi, bhante, nāgā assaddhā appasannā. Te appamattakehipi bhikkhū viheṭheyyuṃ. Sādhu, bhante, ayyā ahimaṃsaṃ na paribhuñjeyyu’’nti. Atha kho bhagavā supassaṃ nāgarājānaṃ dhammiyā kathāya sandassesi…pe… padakkhiṇaṃ katvā pakkāmi. Atha kho bhagavā etasmiṃ nidāne etasmiṃ pakaraṇe dhammiṃ kathaṃ katvā bhikkhū āmantesi – ‘‘na, bhikkhave, ahimaṃsaṃ paribhuñjitabbaṃ. Yo paribhuñjeyya, āpatti dukkaṭassā’’ti.

Now at that time, people, suffering from famine, were eating snake meat, and when bhikkhus went for alms, they gave them snake meat. The bhikkhus ate the snake meat. The people grumbled, complained, and spread it about: “How can these Sakyan recluses eat snake meat? A snake is disgusting and repulsive!” Then the Nāga king Supassa approached the Blessed One, paid homage to him, and stood to one side. Standing to one side, the Nāga king Supassa said to the Blessed One: “Venerable sir, there are Nāgas who are faithless and lacking confidence. They might harm the bhikkhus even for minor reasons. It would be good, venerable sir, if the noble ones did not eat snake meat.” Then the Blessed One instructed, urged, inspired, and gladdened the Nāga king Supassa with a Dhamma talk... and after circumambulating him, he departed. Then the Blessed One, on this occasion, having given a Dhamma talk, addressed the bhikkhus: “Monks, snake meat should not be eaten. Whoever eats it commits a dukkata offense.”

Tena kho pana samayena luddakā sīhaṃ hantvā sīhamaṃsaṃ [maṃsaṃ (ka.)] paribhuñjanti, bhikkhūnaṃ piṇḍāya carantānaṃ sīhamaṃsaṃ denti. Bhikkhū sīhamaṃsaṃ paribhuñjitvā araññe viharanti. Sīhā sīhamaṃsagandhena bhikkhū paripātenti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Na, bhikkhave, sīhamaṃsaṃ paribhuñjitabbaṃ. Yo paribhuñjeyya, āpatti dukkaṭassāti.

Now at that time, hunters killed a lion and were eating lion meat. While the bhikkhus were on their almsround, they gave them lion meat. The bhikkhus, having eaten the lion meat, lived in the wilderness. Lions, because of the smell of lion meat, attacked the bhikkhus. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, lion meat should not be eaten. Whoever eats it commits a dukkata offense.”

Tena kho pana samayena luddakā byagghaṃ hantvā…pe… dīpiṃ hantvā…pe… acchaṃ hantvā…pe… taracchaṃ hantvā taracchamaṃsaṃ paribhuñjanti, bhikkhūnaṃ piṇḍāya carantānaṃ taracchamaṃsaṃ denti. Bhikkhū taracchamaṃsaṃ paribhuñjitvā araññe viharanti. Taracchā taracchamaṃsagandhena bhikkhū paripātenti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Na, bhikkhave, taracchamaṃsaṃ paribhuñjitabbaṃ. Yo paribhuñjeyya, āpatti dukkaṭassāti.

Now at that time, hunters killed a tiger…killed a leopard…killed a bear…killed a hyena and were eating the hyena meat. While on their almsround, they gave hyena meat to the bhikkhus. The bhikkhus, having eaten the hyena meat, lived in the wilderness. Hyenas, because of the smell of hyena meat, attacked the bhikkhus. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, hyena meat should not be eaten. Whoever eats it commits a dukkata offense.”

Hatthimaṃsādipaṭikkhepakathā niṭṭhitā.

The Account of the Prohibition of Elephant Meat and So Forth is concluded.

Suppiyabhāṇavāro niṭṭhito dutiyo.

The second recitation section on Suppiya is concluded.

### 170. Yāgumadhugoḷakānujānanā ^11

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv6-brahmali-pali#^11|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch5|BMC Chapter 5]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-MV6.11" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


170.The Permission for Rice Gruel and Honey-Balls.

282. Atha kho bhagavā bārāṇasiyaṃ yathābhirantaṃ viharitvā yena andhakavindaṃ tena cārikaṃ pakkāmi, mahatā bhikkhusaṅghena saddhiṃ, aḍḍhatelasehi bhikkhusatehi. Tena kho pana samayena jānapadā manussā bahuṃ loṇampi, telampi, taṇḍulampi, khādanīyampi sakaṭesu āropetvā buddhappamukhassa bhikkhusaṅghassa piṭṭhito piṭṭhito anubandhā honti – yadā paṭipāṭiṃ labhissāma tadā bhattaṃ karissāmāti, pañcamattāni ca vighāsādasatāni. Atha kho bhagavā anupubbena cārikaṃ caramāno yena andhakavindaṃ tadavasari. Atha kho aññatarassa brāhmaṇassa paṭipāṭiṃ alabhantassa etadahosi – ‘‘atītāni [adhikāni (sī. syā.)] kho me dve māsāni buddhappamukhaṃ bhikkhusaṅghaṃ anubandhantassa ‘yadā paṭipāṭiṃ labhissāmi tadā bhattaṃ karissāmī’ti, na ca me paṭipāṭi labbhati, ahañcamhi ekattako [ekato (sī. syā.)], bahu ca me gharāvāsattho hāyati. Yaṃnūnāhaṃ bhattaggaṃ olokeyyaṃ; yaṃ bhattagge nāssa, taṃ paṭiyādeyya’’nti. Atha kho so brāhmaṇo bhattaggaṃ olokento dve nāddasa – yāguñca madhugoḷakañca. Atha kho so brāhmaṇo yenāyasmā ānando tenupasaṅkami, upasaṅkamitvā āyasmantaṃ ānandaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘idha me, bho ānanda, paṭipāṭiṃ alabhantassa etadahosi ‘atītāni kho me dve māsāni buddhappamukhaṃ bhikkhusaṅghaṃ anubandhantassa, yadā paṭipāṭiṃ labhissāmi tadā bhattaṃ karissāmīti. Na ca me paṭipāṭi labbhati, ahañcamhi ekattako, bahu ca me gharāvāsattho hāyati. Yaṃnūnāhaṃ bhattaggaṃ olokeyyaṃ; yaṃ bhattagge nāssa, taṃ paṭiyādeyya’nti. So kho ahaṃ, bho ānanda, bhattaggaṃ olokento dve nāddasaṃ – yāguñca madhugoḷakañca. Sacāhaṃ, bho ānanda, paṭiyādeyyaṃ yāguñca madhugoḷakañca, paṭiggaṇheyya me bhavaṃ gotamo’’ti? ‘‘Tena hi, brāhmaṇa, bhagavantaṃ paṭipucchissāmī’’ti. Atha kho āyasmā ānando bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesi. Tena hānanda, paṭiyādetūti. Tena hi, brāhmaṇa, paṭiyādehīti. Atha kho so brāhmaṇo tassā rattiyā accayena pahūtaṃ yāguñca madhugoḷakañca paṭiyādāpetvā bhagavato upanāmesi – paṭiggaṇhātu me bhavaṃ gotamo yāguñca madhugoḷakañcāti. Tena hi, brāhmaṇa, bhikkhūnaṃ dehīti. Bhikkhū kukkuccāyantā na paṭiggaṇhanti. Paṭiggaṇhatha, bhikkhave, paribhuñjathāti. Atha kho so brāhmaṇo buddhappamukhaṃ bhikkhusaṅghaṃ pahūtāya yāguyā ca madhugoḷakena ca sahatthā santappetvā sampavāretvā bhagavantaṃ dhotahatthaṃ onītapattapāṇiṃ ekamantaṃ nisīdi. Ekamantaṃ nisinnaṃ kho taṃ brāhmaṇaṃ bhagavā etadavoca –

282.Then the Blessed One, having stayed at Bārāṇasī as long as he pleased, set out on a journey to Andhakavinda with a large company of bhikkhus—twelve hundred and fifty bhikkhus. At that time, many country folk loaded carts with salt, oil, rice, and hard food and followed behind the Sangha of bhikkhus headed by the Buddha, thinking, "When we get our turn, we will prepare a meal." There were also about five hundred groups of those who lived on scraps. Then the Blessed One, traveling by stages, arrived at Andhakavinda. Then a certain brahmin, not getting his turn, thought: "For the past two months I have been following the Sangha of bhikkhus headed by the Buddha, thinking, 'When I get my turn, I will prepare a meal.' But I have not gotten my turn. I am alone, and much of my household affairs is neglected. Why don’t I inspect the meal offerings? Whatever is lacking in the meal offerings, I will provide." Then that brahmin, inspecting the meal offerings, did not see two things: rice gruel and honey-balls. Then that brahmin approached Venerable Ānanda and said: "Venerable Ānanda, not getting my turn, I thought: 'For the past two months I have been following the Sangha of bhikkhus headed by the Buddha, thinking, "When I get my turn, I will prepare a meal." But I have not gotten my turn. I am alone, and much of my household affairs is neglected. Why don’t I inspect the meal offerings? Whatever is lacking in the meal offerings, I will provide.' Venerable Ānanda, inspecting the meal offerings, I did not see two things: rice gruel and honey-balls. If I were to provide rice gruel and honey-balls, would Master Gotama accept them from me?" "Then, brahmin, I will ask the Blessed One." Then Venerable Ānanda informed the Blessed One of the matter. "Then, Ānanda, let him provide them." "Then, brahmin, provide them." Then that brahmin, when the night had passed, had abundant rice gruel and honey-balls prepared and offered them to the Blessed One, saying: "May Master Gotama accept the rice gruel and honey-balls from me." "Then, brahmin, give them to the bhikkhus." The bhikkhus, being scrupulous, did not accept them. "Accept them, bhikkhus, and partake of them." Then that brahmin personally served and satisfied the Sangha of bhikkhus headed by the Buddha with abundant rice gruel and honey-balls. When the Blessed One had washed his hands and the bowl had been removed, the brahmin sat down to one side. Sitting to one side, the Blessed One said to that brahmin:

‘‘Dasayime, brāhmaṇa, ānisaṃsā yāguyā. Katame dasa? Yāguṃ dento āyuṃ deti, vaṇṇaṃ deti, sukhaṃ deti, balaṃ deti, paṭibhānaṃ deti, yāgu pītā khuddaṃ [khudaṃ (sī. syā.)] paṭihanati, pipāsaṃ vineti, vātaṃ anulometi, vatthiṃ sodheti, āmāvasesaṃ pāceti – ime kho, brāhmaṇa, dasānisaṃsā yāguyā’’ti [pacchimā pañca ānisaṃsā a. ni. 5.207].

“These, brahmin, are the ten benefits of rice gruel. What ten? Giving rice gruel, one gives life, gives beauty, gives happiness, gives strength, gives eloquence. Rice gruel, when drunk, wards off hunger, dispels thirst, regulates the wind, cleanses the bladder, and digests the remnant of undigested food. These, brahmin, are the ten benefits of rice gruel.”

[a. ni. 4.58-59 thokaṃ visadisaṃ] Yo saññatānaṃ paradattabhojinaṃ;Kālena sakkacca dadāti yāguṃ;Dasassa ṭhānāni anuppavecchati;Āyuñca vaṇṇañca sukhaṃ balañca.

For one who is restrained, eating food offered by others, who gives rice gruel at the right time with due respect, he bestows ten things: longevity, beauty, happiness, and strength.

Paṭibhānamassa upajāyate tato;Khuddaṃ pipāsañca byapaneti vātaṃ;Sodheti vatthiṃ pariṇāmeti bhuttaṃ;Bhesajjametaṃ sugatena vaṇṇitaṃ.

From this, eloquence arises in him; it dispels hunger, thirst, and wind; it cleanses the bladder and digests what has been eaten. This medicine was praised by the Sugata.

Tasmā hi yāguṃ alameva dātuṃ;Niccaṃ manussena sukhatthikena;Dibbāni vā patthayatā sukhāni;Manussasobhagyatamicchatā vāti.

Therefore, one desiring happiness should always give rice gruel; indeed, whether aspiring for heavenly pleasures or wishing for human good fortune.

Atha kho bhagavā taṃ brāhmaṇaṃ imāhi gāthāhi anumoditvā uṭṭhāyāsanā pakkāmi. Atha kho bhagavā etasmiṃ nidāne etasmiṃ pakaraṇe dhammiṃ kathaṃ katvā bhikkhū āmantesi – ‘‘anujānāmi, bhikkhave, yāguñca madhugoḷakañcā’’ti.

Then the Blessed One, having rejoiced the brahmin with these verses, rose from his seat and departed. Then the Blessed One, on this occasion, in this connection, having given a Dhamma talk, addressed the bhikkhus: "Bhikkhus, I allow rice gruel and honey-balls."

Yāgumadhugoḷakānujānanā niṭṭhitā.

The allowance for rice gruel and honey-balls is concluded.

### 171. Taruṇapasannamahāmattavatthu ^12

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv6-brahmali-pali#^12|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch5|BMC Chapter 5]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-MV6.12" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


171.The Story of the Newly Devoted High Official

283. Assosuṃ kho manussā bhagavatā kira yāgu anuññātā madhugoḷakañcāti. Te kālasseva, bhojjayāguṃ paṭiyādenti madhugoḷakañca. Bhikkhū kālasseva bhojjayāguyā dhātā madhugoḷakena ca bhattagge na cittarūpaṃ paribhuñjanti. Tena kho pana samayena aññatarena taruṇapasannena mahāmattena svātanāya buddhappamukho bhikkhusaṅgho nimantito hoti. Atha kho tassa taruṇapasannassa mahāmattassa etadahosi – ‘‘yaṃnūnāhaṃ aḍḍhatelasannaṃ bhikkhusatānaṃ aḍḍhatelasāni maṃsapātisatāni paṭiyādeyyaṃ, ekamekassa bhikkhuno ekamekaṃ maṃsapātiṃ upanāmeyya’’nti. Atha kho so taruṇapasanno mahāmatto tassā rattiyā accayena paṇītaṃ khādanīyaṃ bhojanīyaṃ paṭiyādāpetvā aḍḍhatelasāni ca maṃsapātisatāni, bhagavato kālaṃ ārocāpesi – ‘‘kālo, bhante, niṭṭhitaṃ bhatta’’nti. Atha kho bhagavā pubbaṇhasamayaṃ nivāsetvā pattacīvaramādāya yena tassa taruṇapasannassa mahāmattassa nivesanaṃ tenupasaṅkami, upasaṅkamitvā paññatte āsane nisīdi, saddhiṃ bhikkhusaṅghena. Atha kho so taruṇapasanno mahāmatto bhattagge bhikkhū parivisati. Bhikkhū evamāhaṃsu – ‘‘thokaṃ, āvuso, dehi; thokaṃ, āvuso, dehī’’ti. ‘‘Mā kho tumhe, bhante, – ‘ayaṃ taruṇapasanno mahāmatto’ti – thokaṃ thokaṃ paṭiggaṇhatha. Bahuṃ me khādanīyaṃ bhojanīyaṃ paṭiyattaṃ, aḍḍhatelasāni ca maṃsapātisatāni. Ekamekassa bhikkhuno ekamekaṃ maṃsapātiṃ upanāmessāmīti. Paṭiggaṇhatha, bhante, yāvadattha’’nti. ‘‘Na kho mayaṃ, āvuso, etaṃkāraṇā thokaṃ thokaṃ paṭiggaṇhāma, api ca mayaṃ kālasseva bhojjayāguyā dhātā madhugoḷakena ca. Tena mayaṃ thokaṃ thokaṃ paṭiggaṇhāmā’’ti. Atha kho so taruṇapasanno mahāmatto ujjhāyati khiyyati vipāceti – ‘‘kathañhi nāma bhadantā mayā nimantitā aññassa bhojjayāguṃ paribhuñjissanti, na cāhaṃ paṭibalo yāvadatthaṃ dātu’’nti kupito anattamano āsādanāpekkho bhikkhūnaṃ patte pūrento agamāsi – bhuñjatha vā haratha vāti. Atha kho so taruṇapasanno mahāmatto buddhappamukhaṃ bhikkhusaṅghaṃ paṇītena khādanīyena bhojanīyena sahatthā santappetvā sampavāretvā bhagavantaṃ bhuttāviṃ onītapattapāṇiṃ ekamantaṃ nisīdi. Ekamantaṃ nisinnaṃ kho taṃ taruṇapasannaṃ mahāmattaṃ bhagavā dhammiyā kathāya sandassetvā samādapetvā samuttejetvā sampahaṃsetvā uṭṭhāyāsanā pakkāmi.

283.People heard that the Blessed One had allowed congee and honey balls. So, early in the morning, they prepared congee and honey balls. The monks, having been satiated with congee and honey balls early in the morning, did not partake of their meal at the alms hall with relish. At that time, a newly devoted high official had invited the Sangha of monks headed by the Buddha for the next day. Then that newly devoted high official thought: "Why don’t I prepare thirteen hundred and fifty bowls of meat for thirteen hundred and fifty monks, offering one bowl of meat to each monk?" Then that newly devoted high official, after that night had passed, had fine hard and soft food prepared, along with thirteen hundred and fifty bowls of meat. He informed the Blessed One that the meal was ready: "Venerable sir, it is time; the meal is ready." Then the Blessed One, having dressed in the morning, took his bowl and robe and went to the residence of that newly devoted high official. Having arrived, he sat down on the prepared seat together with the Sangha of monks. Then that newly devoted high official served the monks in the dining hall. The monks said: "Give a little, friend; give a little, friend." "Venerable sirs, do not take just a little because you think, 'This is a newly devoted high official.' I have prepared much hard and soft food and thirteen hundred and fifty bowls of meat. I intend to offer one bowl of meat to each monk. Please accept, venerable sirs, as much as you wish." "Friend, we are not taking just a little for that reason. But we have already been satiated with congee and honey balls early in the morning. That is why we are taking just a little." Then that newly devoted high official complained, grumbled, and criticized: "How can these venerable ones, invited by me, partake of congee elsewhere? Am I not capable of giving as much as they want?" Angry and displeased, and wanting to cause offence, he went around filling the monks’ bowls to the brim, saying, "Eat it or take it away!" Then that newly devoted high official, having personally served and satisfied the Sangha of monks headed by the Buddha with fine hard and soft food, sat down to one side when the Blessed One had finished his meal and taken his hand from the bowl. Seated to one side, the Blessed One instructed, urged, inspired, and gladdened that newly devoted high official with a Dhamma talk. Then he rose from his seat and departed.

Atha kho tassa taruṇapasannassa mahāmattassa acirapakkantassa bhagavato ahudeva kukkuccaṃ, ahu vippaṭisāro – ‘‘alābhā vata me, na vata me lābhā; dulladdhaṃ vata me, na vata me suladdhaṃ; yohaṃ kupito anattamano āsādanāpekkho bhikkhūnaṃ patte pūrento agamāsiṃ – ‘bhuñjatha vā haratha vā’ti. Kiṃ nu kho mayā bahuṃ pasutaṃ puññaṃ vā apuññaṃ vā’’ti? Atha kho so taruṇapasanno mahāmatto yena bhagavā tenupasaṅkami, upasaṅkamitvā bhagavantaṃ abhivādetvā ekamantaṃ nisīdi. Ekamantaṃ nisinno kho so taruṇapasanno mahāmatto bhagavantaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘idha mayhaṃ, bhante, acirapakkantassa bhagavato ahudeva kukkuccaṃ, ahu vippaṭisāro ‘alābhā vata me, na vata me lābhā; dulladdhaṃ vata me, na vata me suladdhaṃ; yohaṃ kupito anattamano āsādanāpekkho bhikkhūnaṃ patte pūrento agamāsiṃ – bhuñjatha vā haratha vāti. Kiṃ nu kho mayā bahuṃ pasutaṃ, puññaṃ vā apuññaṃ vā’ti. Kiṃ nu kho mayā, bhante, bahuṃ pasutaṃ, puññaṃ vā apuññaṃ vā’’ti? ‘‘Yadaggena tayā, āvuso, svātanāya buddhappamukho bhikkhusaṅgho nimantito tadaggena te bahuṃ puññaṃ pasutaṃ. Yadaggena te ekamekena bhikkhunā ekamekaṃ sitthaṃ paṭiggahitaṃ tadaggena te bahuṃ puññaṃ pasutaṃ, saggā te āraddhā’’ti. Atha kho so taruṇapasanno mahāmatto – ‘‘lābhā kira me, suladdhaṃ kira me, bahuṃ kira mayā puññaṃ pasutaṃ, saggā kira me āraddhā’’ti – haṭṭho udaggo uṭṭhāyāsanā bhagavantaṃ abhivādetvā padakkhiṇaṃ katvā pakkāmi. Atha kho bhagavā etasmiṃ nidāne etasmiṃ pakaraṇe bhikkhusaṅghaṃ sannipātāpetvā bhikkhū paṭipucchi – ‘‘saccaṃ kira, bhikkhave, bhikkhū aññatra nimantitā aññassa bhojjayāguṃ paribhuñjantī’’ti? ‘‘Saccaṃ, bhagavā’’ti. Vigarahi buddho bhagavā…pe… kathañhi nāma te, bhikkhave, moghapurisā aññatra nimantitā aññassa bhojjayāguṃ paribhuñjissanti. Netaṃ, bhikkhave, appasannānaṃ vā pasādāya…pe… vigarahitvā dhammiṃ kathaṃ katvā bhikkhū āmantesi – ‘‘na, bhikkhave, aññatra nimantitena aññassa bhojjayāgu paribhuñjitabbā. Yo paribhuñjeyya, yathādhammo kāretabbo’’ti.

Then, soon after the Blessed One had departed, doubt and regret arose in that newly devoted high official: "Alas, it is truly my loss, not my gain; my misfortune, not my good fortune, that I went angry and displeased, seeking an occasion for offense, filling the monks' bowls while saying, 'Eat it or carry it away.' What have I produced in abundance—merit or demerit?" Then that newly devoted high official approached the Blessed One, paid homage to him, and sat down to one side. Seated to one side, he said to the Blessed One: "Venerable sir, soon after you departed, doubt and regret arose in me: 'Alas, it is truly my loss, not my gain; my misfortune, not my good fortune, that I went angry and displeased, seeking an occasion for offense, filling the monks' bowls while saying, "Eat it or carry it away." What have I produced in abundance—merit or demerit?' Venerable sir, what have I produced in abundance—merit or demerit?" "Friend, by the fact that you invited the Saṅgha of monks headed by the Buddha for tomorrow's meal, you have produced abundant merit. By the fact that each monk accepted a single morsel from you, you have produced abundant merit; heaven has been set in motion for you." Then that newly devoted high official, joyful and elated, rose from his seat, paid homage to the Blessed One, circumambulated him, and departed, thinking: "Truly, it is my gain, my good fortune! I have produced abundant merit, and heaven has been set in motion for me!" Then, on this occasion, the Blessed One convened the Saṅgha of monks, and asked the monks: "Is it true, monks, that monks partake of another's congee when invited elsewhere?" "It is true, Blessed One." The Buddha, the Blessed One, rebuked them…pe… "How can you, foolish men, partake of another's congee when invited elsewhere? This will not inspire confidence in those without it…pe…" Having rebuked them, he gave a Dhamma talk and addressed the monks: "Monks, one should not partake of another's congee when invited elsewhere. Whoever does so, he should be dealt with according to the rule."

Taruṇapasannamahāmattavatthu niṭṭhitaṃ.

The Story of the Newly Devoted High Official is concluded.

### 172. Belaṭṭhakaccānavatthu ^13

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv6-brahmali-pali#^13|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch5|BMC Chapter 5]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-MV6.13" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


172.The Story of Belaṭṭha Kaccāna

284. Atha kho bhagavā andhakavinde yathābhirantaṃ viharitvā yena rājagahaṃ tena cārikaṃ pakkāmi, mahatā bhikkhusaṅghena saddhiṃ, aḍḍhatelasehi bhikkhusatehi. Tena kho pana samayena belaṭṭho kaccāno rājagahā andhakavindaṃ addhānamaggappaṭipanno hoti, pañcamattehi sakaṭasatehi, sabbeheva guḷakumbhapūrehi. Addasā kho bhagavā belaṭṭhaṃ kaccānaṃ dūratova āgacchantaṃ, disvāna maggā okkamma aññatarasmiṃ rukkhamūle nisīdi. Atha kho belaṭṭho kaccāno yena bhagavā tenupasaṅkami, upasaṅkamitvā bhagavantaṃ abhivādetvā ekamantaṃ aṭṭhāsi. Ekamantaṃ ṭhito kho belaṭṭho kaccāno bhagavantaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘icchāmahaṃ, bhante, ekamekassa bhikkhuno ekamekaṃ guḷakumbhaṃ dātu’’nti. ‘‘Tena hi tvaṃ, kaccāna, ekaṃyeva guḷakumbhaṃ āharā’’ti. ‘‘Evaṃ, bhante’’ti kho belaṭṭho kaccāno bhagavato paṭissuṇitvā ekaṃyeva guḷakumbhaṃ ādāya yena bhagavā tenupasaṅkami, upasaṅkamitvā bhagavantaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘ābhato [āhaṭo (sī. syā. ka.)], bhante, guḷakumbho; kathāhaṃ, bhante, paṭipajjāmī’’ti? ‘‘Tena hi tvaṃ, kaccāna, bhikkhūnaṃ guḷaṃ dehī’’ti. ‘‘Evaṃ, bhante’’ti kho belaṭṭho kaccāno bhagavato paṭissuṇitvā bhikkhūnaṃ guḷaṃ datvā bhagavantaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘dinno, bhante, bhikkhūnaṃ guḷo, bahu cāyaṃ guḷo avasiṭṭho. Kathāhaṃ, bhante, paṭipajjāmī’’ti? ‘‘Tena hi tvaṃ, kaccāna, bhikkhūnaṃ guḷaṃ yāvadatthaṃ dehī’’ti. ‘‘Evaṃ, bhante’’ti kho belaṭṭho kaccāno bhagavato paṭissuṇitvā bhikkhūnaṃ guḷaṃ yāvadatthaṃ datvā bhagavantaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘dinno, bhante, bhikkhūnaṃ guḷo yāvadattho, bahu cāyaṃ guḷo avasiṭṭho. Kathāhaṃ, bhante, paṭipajjāmī’’ti? ‘‘Tena hi tvaṃ, kaccāna, bhikkhū guḷehi santappehī’’ti. ‘‘Evaṃ, bhante’’ti kho belaṭṭho kaccāno bhagavato paṭissuṇitvā bhikkhū guḷehi santappesi. Ekacce bhikkhū pattepi pūresuṃ parissāvanānipi thavikāyopi pūresuṃ. Atha kho belaṭṭho kaccāno bhikkhū guḷehi santappetvā bhagavantaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘santappitā, bhante, bhikkhū guḷehi, bahu cāyaṃ guḷo avasiṭṭho. Kathāhaṃ, bhante, paṭipajjāmī’’ti? ‘‘Tena hi tvaṃ, kaccāna, vighāsādānaṃ guḷaṃ dehī’’ti. ‘‘Evaṃ, bhante’’ti kho belaṭṭho kaccāno bhagavato paṭissuṇitvā vighāsādānaṃ guḷaṃ datvā bhagavantaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘dinno, bhante, vighāsādānaṃ guḷo, bahu cāyaṃ guḷo avasiṭṭho. Kathāhaṃ, bhante, paṭipajjāmī’’ti? ‘‘Tena hi tvaṃ, kaccāna, vighāsādānaṃ guḷaṃ yāvadatthaṃ dehī’’ti. ‘‘Evaṃ, bhante’’ti kho belaṭṭho kaccāno bhagavato paṭissuṇitvā vighāsādānaṃ guḷaṃ yāvadatthaṃ datvā bhagavantaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘dinno, bhante, vighāsādānaṃ guḷo yāvadattho, bahu cāyaṃ guḷo avasiṭṭho. Kathāhaṃ, bhante, paṭipajjāmī’’ti? ‘‘Tena hi tvaṃ, kaccāna, vighāsāde guḷehi santappehī’’ti. ‘‘Evaṃ, bhante’’ti kho belaṭṭho kaccāno bhagavato paṭissuṇitvā vighāsāde guḷehi santappesi. Ekacce vighāsādā kolambepi ghaṭepi pūresuṃ, piṭakānipi ucchaṅgepi pūresuṃ. Atha kho belaṭṭho kaccāno vighāsāde guḷehi santappetvā bhagavantaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘santappitā, bhante, vighāsādā guḷehi, bahu cāyaṃ guḷo avasiṭṭho. Kathāhaṃ, bhante, paṭipajjāmī’’ti? ‘‘Nāhaṃ taṃ, kaccāna, passāmi sadevake loke samārake sabrahmake sassamaṇabrāhmaṇiyā pajāya sadevamanussāya yassa so guḷo paribhutto sammā pariṇāmaṃ gaccheyya, aññatra tathāgatassa vā tathāgatasāvakassa vā. Tena hi tvaṃ, kaccāna, taṃ guḷaṃ appaharite vā chaḍḍehi, appāṇake vā udake opilāpehī’’ti. ‘‘Evaṃ, bhante’’ti kho belaṭṭho kaccāno bhagavato paṭissuṇitvā taṃ guḷaṃ appāṇake udake opilāpeti. Atha kho so guḷo udake pakkhitto cicciṭāyati ciṭiciṭāyati padhūpāyati [sandhūpāyati (sī. syā.)] sampadhūpāyati. Seyyathāpi nāma phālo divasaṃsantatto udake pakkhitto cicciṭāyati ciṭiciṭāyati padhūpāyati sampadhūpāyati, evameva so guḷo udake pakkhitto cicciṭāyati ciṭiciṭāyati padhūpāyati sampadhūpāyati.

284.Then the Blessed One, having stayed at Andhakavinda as long as he pleased, set out on a journey to Rājagaha with a large company of bhikkhus—one thousand two hundred and fifty bhikkhus. Now at that time, Belaṭṭha Kaccāna was traveling from Rājagaha to Andhakavinda on the road, with five hundred carts, all loaded with pots of molasses. From a distance, the Blessed One saw Belaṭṭha Kaccāna approaching. Seeing him, he stepped off the road and sat down at the foot of a certain tree. Then Belaṭṭha Kaccāna approached the Blessed One, paid homage to him, and stood to one side. Standing there, Belaṭṭha Kaccāna said to the Blessed One: “Venerable sir, I wish to give each bhikkhu one pot of molasses.” “Then, Kaccāna, bring just one pot of molasses.” “Yes, venerable sir,” replied Belaṭṭha Kaccāna. He took one pot of molasses, approached the Blessed One, and said: “Venerable sir, the pot of molasses has been brought. What should I do now?” “Then, Kaccāna, give the molasses to the bhikkhus.” “Yes, venerable sir,” replied Belaṭṭha Kaccāna. After giving the molasses to the bhikkhus, he said to the Blessed One: “Venerable sir, the molasses has been given to the bhikkhus, but much remains. What should I do now?” “Then, Kaccāna, give the bhikkhus molasses as much as they desire.” “Yes, venerable sir,” replied Belaṭṭha Kaccāna. After giving the bhikkhus molasses as much as they desired, he said to the Blessed One: “Venerable sir, the bhikkhus have taken molasses as much as they desired, but much still remains. What should I do now?” “Then, Kaccāna, satiate the bhikkhus with molasses.” “Yes, venerable sir,” replied Belaṭṭha Kaccāna. He satiated the bhikkhus with molasses. Some bhikkhus filled their bowls, some filled their strainers, and some filled their bags. Then Belaṭṭha Kaccāna, having satiated the bhikkhus with molasses, said to the Blessed One: “Venerable sir, the bhikkhus have been satiated with molasses, but much still remains. What should I do now?” “Then, Kaccāna, give the molasses to those who live on leftovers.” “Yes, venerable sir,” replied Belaṭṭha Kaccāna. After giving the molasses to those who live on leftovers, he said to the Blessed One: “Venerable sir, the molasses has been given to those who live on leftovers, but much still remains. What should I do now?” “Then, Kaccāna, give those who live on leftovers molasses as much as they desire.” “Yes, venerable sir,” replied Belaṭṭha Kaccāna. After giving those who live on leftovers molasses as much as they desired, he said to the Blessed One: “Venerable sir, those who live on leftovers have taken molasses as much as they desired, but much still remains. What should I do now?” “Then, Kaccāna, satiate those who live on leftovers with molasses.” “Yes, venerable sir,” replied Belaṭṭha Kaccāna. He satiated those who live on leftovers with molasses. Some who lived on leftovers filled their buckets, some filled their pots, some filled their baskets, and some even filled their laps. Then Belaṭṭha Kaccāna, having satiated those who live on leftovers with molasses, said to the Blessed One: “Venerable sir, those who live on leftovers have been satiated with molasses, but much still remains. What should I do now?” “I do not see, Kaccāna, in this world with its gods, Māras, and Brahmās, among this generation with its ascetics and brahmins, its gods and humans, anyone by whom this molasses, having been eaten, could be properly digested, except the Tathāgata or a disciple of the Tathāgata. Therefore, Kaccāna, discard this molasses in a place where there is no green vegetation or immerse it in water where there are no living beings.” “Yes, venerable sir,” replied Belaṭṭha Kaccāna. He immersed the molasses in water where there were no living beings. When the molasses was thrown into the water, it crackled, sputtered, steamed, and sent up clouds of smoke—just as a plowshare heated all day crackles, sputters, steams, and sends up clouds of smoke when thrown into water, so too did that molasses crackle, sputter, steam, and send up clouds of smoke when thrown into the water.

Atha kho belaṭṭho kaccāno saṃviggo lomahaṭṭhajāto yena bhagavā tenupasaṅkami, upasaṅkamitvā bhagavantaṃ abhivādetvā ekamantaṃ nisīdi. Ekamantaṃ nisinnassa kho belaṭṭhassa kaccānassa bhagavā anupubbiṃ kathaṃ kathesi, seyyathidaṃ – ‘‘dānakathaṃ sīlakathaṃ saggakathaṃ, kāmānaṃ ādīnavaṃ okāraṃ saṃkilesaṃ, nekkhamme ānisaṃsaṃ pakāsesi. Yadā bhagavā aññāsi belaṭṭhaṃ kaccānaṃ kallacittaṃ, muducittaṃ, vinīvaraṇacittaṃ, udaggacittaṃ, pasannacittaṃ, atha yā buddhānaṃ sāmukkaṃsikā dhammadesanā, taṃ pakāsesi…pe… evameva belaṭṭhassa kaccānassa tasmiṃyeva āsane virajaṃ vītamalaṃ dhammacakkhuṃ udapādi – yaṃ kiñci samudayadhammaṃ sabbaṃ taṃ nirodhadhammanti. Atha kho belaṭṭho kaccāno diṭṭhadhammo pattadhammo viditadhammo pariyogāḷhadhammo tiṇṇavicikiccho vigatakathaṃkatho vesārajjappatto aparappaccayo satthusāsane bhagavantaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘abhikkantaṃ, bhante. Abhikkantaṃ, bhante. Seyyathāpi, bhante, nikkujjitaṃ vā ukkujjeyya…pe… evamevaṃ kho bhagavatā anekapariyāyena dhammo pakāsito. Esāhaṃ, bhante, bhagavantaṃ saraṇaṃ gacchāmi, dhammañca, bhikkhusaṅghañca. Upāsakaṃ maṃ bhagavā dhāretu ajjatagge pāṇupetaṃ saraṇagata’’nti.

Then Belaṭṭha Kaccāna, agitated and with hair standing on end, approached the Blessed One. Having approached, he paid homage to the Blessed One and sat down to one side. Sitting to one side, the Blessed One gave Belaṭṭha Kaccāna a progressive talk, that is to say, a talk on generosity, on virtue, on heaven; on the danger, worthlessness, and defilement of sensual pleasures; and on the benefits of renunciation. When the Blessed One knew that Belaṭṭha Kaccāna's mind was ready, pliable, free from hindrances, uplifted, and confident, he revealed the teaching unique to the Buddhas: suffering, its origin, its cessation, and the path. Just as a clean cloth [readily] absorbs dye, so too in Belaṭṭha Kaccāna, as he sat there, arose the dust-free, stainless vision of the Dhamma: “Whatever is subject to origination is all subject to cessation.” Then Belaṭṭha Kaccāna, having seen the Dhamma, attained the Dhamma, known the Dhamma, plunged into the Dhamma, crossed beyond doubt, got rid of perplexity, attained assurance, and become independent of others in the Teacher’s Dispensation, said to the Blessed One: “Excellent, venerable sir! Excellent, venerable sir! Just as one might set upright what had been overturned, reveal what was hidden, show the way to one who was lost, or bring a lamp into the darkness so that those with eyes could see—in the same way, the Blessed One has made the Dhamma clear in many ways. I go for refuge to the Blessed One, to the Dhamma, and to the Sangha of bhikkhus. May the Blessed One accept me as a lay follower who has gone for refuge from this day forward, for as long as life lasts.”

Atha kho bhagavā anupubbena cārikaṃ caramāno yena rājagahaṃ tadavasari. Tatra sudaṃ bhagavā rājagahe viharati veḷuvane kalandakanivāpe. Tena kho pana samayena rājagahe guḷo ussanno hoti. Bhikkhū – gilānasseva bhagavatā guḷo anuññāto, no agilānassāti – kukkuccāyantā guḷaṃ na bhuñjanti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, gilānassa guḷaṃ, agilānassa guḷodakanti.

Then the Blessed One, wandering by stages, arrived at Rājagaha. There the Blessed One stayed in Rājagaha, in the Bamboo Grove, the Squirrel Sanctuary. Now at that time, molasses was plentiful in Rājagaha. The bhikkhus—thinking, “The Blessed One has allowed molasses only for the sick, not for the healthy”—were scrupulous and did not consume molasses. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “I allow, bhikkhus, molasses for the sick and molasses-water for the healthy.”

Belaṭṭhakaccānavatthu niṭṭhitaṃ.

The story about Belaṭṭha Kaccāna is concluded.

### 173. Pāṭaligāmavatthu ^14

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv6-brahmali-pali#^14|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch5|BMC Chapter 5]] and the following cites:
