173.The Pāṭaligāma Incident

285. [ito paraṃ mahāva. 286-287 ‘tiṇṇā medhāvino janā’ti pāṭho dī. ni. 2.148; udā. 76 ādayo] Atha kho bhagavā rājagahe yathābhirantaṃ viharitvā yena pāṭaligāmo tena cārikaṃ pakkāmi, mahatā bhikkhusaṅghena saddhiṃ, aḍḍhatelasehi bhikkhusatehi. Atha kho bhagavā anupubbena cārikaṃ caramāno yena pāṭaligāmo tadavasari. Assosuṃ kho pāṭaligāmikā upāsakā – ‘‘bhagavā kira pāṭaligāmaṃ anuppatto’’ti. Atha kho pāṭaligāmikā upāsakā yena bhagavā tenupasaṅkamiṃsu, upasaṅkamitvā bhagavantaṃ abhivādetvā ekamantaṃ nisīdiṃsu. Ekamantaṃ nisinne kho pāṭaligāmike upāsake bhagavā dhammiyā kathāya sandassesi, samādapesi, samuttejesi, sampahaṃsesi. Atha kho pāṭaligāmikā upāsakā bhagavatā dhammiyā kathāya sandassitā samādapitā samuttejitā sampahaṃsitā bhagavantaṃ etadavocuṃ – ‘‘adhivāsetu no, bhante, bhagavā āvasathāgāraṃ saddhiṃ bhikkhusaṅghenā’’ti. Adhivāsesi bhagavā tuṇhībhāvena. Atha kho pāṭaligāmikā upāsakā bhagavato adhivāsanaṃ viditvā uṭṭhāyāsanā bhagavantaṃ abhivādetvā padakkhiṇaṃ katvā yena āvasathāgāraṃ tenupasaṅkamiṃsu, upasaṅkamitvā sabbasanthariṃ āvasathāgāraṃ santharitvā, āsanāni paññapetvā, udakamaṇikaṃ patiṭṭhāpetvā, telapadīpaṃ āropetvā yena bhagavā tenupasaṅkamiṃsu, upasaṅkamitvā bhagavantaṃ abhivādetvā ekamantaṃ aṭṭhaṃsu. Ekamantaṃ ṭhitā kho pāṭaligāmikā upāsakā bhagavantaṃ etadavocuṃ – ‘‘sabbasantharisanthataṃ, bhante, āvasathāgāraṃ. Āsanāni paññattāni. Udakamaṇiko patiṭṭhāpito. Telapadīpo āropito. Yassadāni, bhante, bhagavā kālaṃ maññatī’’ti.

285.Then the Blessed One, having stayed in Rājagaha as long as he pleased, set out on a journey toward Pāṭaligāma with a large company of monks—thirteen hundred and fifty monks. Traveling stage by stage, the Blessed One arrived at Pāṭaligāma. The lay followers of Pāṭaligāma heard: "The Blessed One, it seems, has arrived at Pāṭaligāma." Then the lay followers of Pāṭaligāma approached the Blessed One, paid homage to him, and sat down to one side. Sitting to one side, the Blessed One instructed, inspired, aroused, and gladdened them with a Dhamma talk. Having been instructed, inspired, aroused, and gladdened by the Blessed One with a Dhamma talk, the lay followers of Pāṭaligāma said to him: "May the Blessed One, venerable sir, consent to accept our rest house together with the community of monks." The Blessed One consented by silence. Then the lay followers of Pāṭaligāma, understanding the Blessed One's consent, rose from their seats, paid homage to him, circumambulated him, keeping him to their right, and approached the rest house. Having approached, they spread out the rest house completely with mats, prepared seats, set up a water vessel, and lit an oil lamp. Then they approached the Blessed One, paid homage to him, and stood to one side. Standing to one side, the lay followers of Pāṭaligāma said to the Blessed One: "Venerable sir, the rest house is completely spread out with mats, seats are prepared, a water vessel is set up, and an oil lamp is lit. Now, venerable sir, the Blessed One may go at his convenience."

Atha kho bhagavā nivāsetvā pattacīvaramādāya saddhiṃ bhikkhusaṅghena yena āvasathāgāraṃ tenupasaṅkami; upasaṅkamitvā pāde pakkhāletvā āvasathāgāraṃ pavisitvā majjhimaṃ thambhaṃ nissāya puratthābhimukho nisīdi. Bhikkhusaṅghopi kho pāde pakkhāletvā āvasathāgāraṃ pavisitvā pacchimaṃ bhittiṃ nissāya puratthābhimukho nisīdi, bhagavantaṃyeva purakkhatvā. Pāṭaligāmikāpi kho upāsakā pāde pakkhāletvā āvasathāgāraṃ pavisitvā puratthimaṃ bhittiṃ nissāya pacchimābhimukhā nisīdiṃsu, bhagavantaṃyeva purakkhatvā. Atha kho bhagavā pāṭaligāmike upāsake āmantesi –

Then the Blessed One, having dressed, taking his bowl and robe, together with the community of monks, approached the rest house. Having approached, he washed his feet, entered the rest house, and sat down facing east, leaning against the central pillar. The community of monks also washed their feet, entered the rest house, and sat down facing east, leaning against the western wall, regarding the Blessed One as foremost. The lay followers of Pāṭaligāma also washed their feet, entered the rest house, and sat down facing west, leaning against the eastern wall, regarding the Blessed One as foremost. Then the Blessed One addressed the lay followers of Pāṭaligāma:

[dī. ni. 3.316; a. ni. 5.213 ādayo], Gahapatayo, ādīnavā dussīlassa sīlavipattiyā. Katame pañca? Idha, gahapatayo, dussīlo sīlavipanno pamādādhikaraṇaṃ mahatiṃ bhogajāniṃ nigacchati. Ayaṃ paṭhamo ādīnavo dussīlassa sīlavipattiyā. Puna caparaṃ, gahapatayo, dussīlassa sīlavipannassa pāpako kittisaddo abbhuggacchati. Ayaṃ dutiyo ādīnavo dussīlassa sīlavipattiyā. Puna caparaṃ, gahapatayo, dussīlo sīlavipanno yaññadeva parisaṃ upasaṅkamati, yadi khattiyaparisaṃ, yadi brāhmaṇaparisaṃ, yadi gahapatiparisaṃ, yadi samaṇaparisaṃ, avisārado upasaṅkamati maṅkubhūto. Ayaṃ tatiyo ādīnavo dussīlassa sīlavipattiyā. Puna caparaṃ, gahapatayo, dussīlo sīlavipanno sammūḷho kālaṃkaroti. Ayaṃ catuttho ādīnavo dussīlassa sīlavipattiyā. Puna caparaṃ, gahapatayo, dussīlo sīlavipanno kāyassa bhedā paraṃ maraṇā apāyaṃ duggatiṃ vinipātaṃ nirayaṃ upapajjati. Ayaṃ pañcamo ādīnavo dussīlassa sīlavipattiyā. Ime kho, gahapatayo, pañca ādīnavā dussīlassa sīlavipattiyā.

Householders, these are the five drawbacks for the immoral, due to failure in virtue. What five? First, householders, the immoral person, due to failure in virtue, through negligence incurs a great loss of wealth. This is the first drawback for the immoral, due to failure in virtue. Furthermore, householders, an evil report spreads about the immoral person who has failed in virtue. This is the second drawback for the immoral, due to failure in virtue. Furthermore, householders, the immoral person who has failed in virtue enters any assembly—whether of nobles, brahmins, householders, or ascetics—unassured and shrinking. This is the third drawback for the immoral, due to failure in virtue. Furthermore, householders, the immoral person who has failed in virtue dies confused. This is the fourth drawback for the immoral, due to failure in virtue. Furthermore, householders, the immoral person who has failed in virtue, upon the breakup of the body, after death, is reborn in the plane of misery, a bad destination, the lower realms, even in hell. This is the fifth drawback for the immoral, due to failure in virtue. These, householders, are the five drawbacks for the immoral, due to failure in virtue.

[dī. ni. 3.316; a. ni. 5.213 ādayo] ‘‘Pañcime, gahapatayo, ānisaṃsā sīlavato sīlasampadāya. Katame pañca? Idha, gahapatayo, sīlavā sīlasampanno appamādādhikaraṇaṃ mahantaṃ bhogakkhandhaṃ adhigacchati. Ayaṃ paṭhamo ānisaṃso sīlavato sīlasampadāya. Puna caparaṃ, gahapatayo, sīlavato sīlasampannassa kalyāṇo kittisaddo abbhuggacchati. Ayaṃ dutiyo ānisaṃso sīlavato sīlasampadāya. Puna caparaṃ, gahapatayo, sīlavā sīlasampanno yaññadeva parisaṃ upasaṅkamati, yadi khattiyaparisaṃ, yadi brāhmaṇaparisaṃ, yadi gahapatiparisaṃ, yadi samaṇaparisaṃ, visārado upasaṅkamati amaṅkubhūto. Ayaṃ tatiyo ānisaṃso sīlavato sīlasampadāya. Puna caparaṃ, gahapatayo, sīlavā sīlasampanno asammūḷho kālaṃkaroti. Ayaṃ catuttho ānisaṃso sīlavato sīlasampadāya. Puna caparaṃ, gahapatayo, sīlavā sīlasampanno kāyassa bhedā paraṃ maraṇā sugatiṃ saggaṃ lokaṃ upapajjati. Ayaṃ pañcamo ānisaṃso sīlavato sīlasampadāya. Ime kho, gahapatayo, pañca ānisaṃsā sīlavato sīlasampadāyāti.

"Householders, there are these five benefits of virtue for one accomplished in virtue. What are the five? Firstly, householders, a virtuous person, accomplished in virtue, through diligence acquires a great mass of wealth. This is the first benefit of virtue for one accomplished in virtue. Furthermore, householders, a virtuous person, accomplished in virtue, obtains a good reputation. This is the second benefit of virtue for one accomplished in virtue. Moreover, householders, a virtuous person, accomplished in virtue, approaches any assembly—whether of nobles, brahmins, householders, or ascetics—confidently and without embarrassment. This is the third benefit of virtue for one accomplished in virtue. Furthermore, householders, a virtuous person, accomplished in virtue, dies unconfused. This is the fourth benefit of virtue for one accomplished in virtue. Finally, householders, a virtuous person, accomplished in virtue, upon the breakup of the body, after death, is reborn in a good destination, in a heavenly world. This is the fifth benefit of virtue for one accomplished in virtue. These, householders, are the five benefits of virtue for one accomplished in virtue."

Atha kho bhagavā pāṭaligāmike upāsake bahudeva rattiṃ dhammiyā kathāya sandassetvā samādapetvā samuttejetvā sampahaṃsetvā uyyojesi – ‘‘abhikkantā kho, gahapatayo, ratti. Yassadāni tumhe kālaṃ maññathā’’ti. ‘‘Evaṃ, bhante’’ti, kho pāṭaligāmikā upāsakā bhagavato paṭissuṇitvā uṭṭhāyāsanā bhagavantaṃ abhivādetvā padakkhiṇaṃ katvā pakkamiṃsu. Atha kho bhagavā acirapakkantesu pāṭaligāmikesu upāsakesu suññāgāraṃ pāvisi.

Then the Blessed One, having instructed, roused, inspired, and gladdened the Pāṭaligāma lay followers with a Dhamma talk far into the night, dismissed them, saying: "The night is far advanced, householders. It is time for you to do as you think fit." "Yes, venerable sir," the Pāṭaligāma lay followers replied to the Blessed One. Then they rose from their seats, paid homage to him, circumambulated him keeping the right side toward him, and departed. Soon after the Pāṭaligāma lay followers had left, the Blessed One entered an empty dwelling.

Pāṭaligāmavatthu niṭṭhitaṃ.

The Pāṭaligāma Incident is finished.

### 174. Sunidhavassakāravatthu ^15

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv6-brahmali-pali#^15|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch5|BMC Chapter 5]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-MV6.15" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


174.The Story of Sunidha and Vassakāra

286. Tena kho pana samayena sunidhavassakārā magadhamahāmattā pāṭaligāme nagaraṃ māpenti vajjīnaṃ paṭibāhāya. Addasā kho bhagavā rattiyā paccūsasamayaṃ paccuṭṭhāya dibbena cakkhunā visuddhena atikkantamānusakena sambahulā devatāyo pāṭaligāme vatthūni pariggaṇhantiyo. Yasmiṃ padese mahesakkhā devatā vatthūni pariggaṇhanti, mahesakkhānaṃ tattha rājūnaṃ rājamahāmattānaṃ cittāni namanti nivesanāni māpetuṃ. Yasmiṃ padese majjhimā devatā vatthūni pariggaṇhanti, majjhimānaṃ tattha rājūnaṃ rājamahāmattānaṃ cittāni namanti nivesanāni māpetuṃ. Yasmiṃ padese nīcā devatā vatthūni pariggaṇhanti, nīcānaṃ tattha rājūnaṃ rājamahāmattānaṃ cittāni namanti nivesanāni māpetuṃ. Atha kho bhagavā āyasmantaṃ ānandaṃ āmantesi – ‘‘ke nu kho te, ānanda, pāṭaligāme nagaraṃ māpentī’’ti? ‘‘Sunidhavassakārā, bhante, magadhamahāmattā pāṭaligāme nagaraṃ māpenti vajjīnaṃ paṭibāhāyā’’ti. Seyyathāpi, ānanda, devehi tāvatiṃsehi saddhiṃ mantetvā, evameva kho, ānanda, sunidhavassakārā magadhamahāmattā pāṭaligāme nagaraṃ māpenti vajjīnaṃ paṭibāhāya. Idhāhaṃ, ānanda, rattiyā paccūsasamayaṃ paccuṭṭhāya addasaṃ dibbena cakkhunā visuddhena atikkantamānusakena sambahulā devatāyo pāṭaligāme vatthūni pariggaṇhantiyo. Yasmiṃ padese mahesakkhā devatā vatthūni pariggaṇhanti, mahesakkhānaṃ tattha rājūnaṃ rājamahāmattānaṃ cittāni namanti nivesanāni māpetuṃ. Yasmiṃ padese majjhimā devatā vatthūni pariggaṇhanti, majjhimānaṃ tattha rājūnaṃ rājamahāmattānaṃ cittāni namanti nivesanāni māpetuṃ. Yasmiṃ padese nīcā devatā vatthūni pariggaṇhanti, nīcānaṃ tattha rājūnaṃ rājamahāmattānaṃ cittāni namanti nivesanāni māpetuṃ. Yāvatā, ānanda, ariyaṃ āyatanaṃ, yāvatā vaṇippatho, idaṃ agganagaraṃ bhavissati pāṭaliputtaṃ puṭabhedanaṃ. Pāṭaliputtassa kho, ānanda, tayo antarāyā bhavissanti – aggito vā udakato vā abbhantarato vā mithubhedāti.

286.Now at that time, Sunidha and Vassakāra, the chief ministers of Magadha, were building a city at Pāṭaligāma to keep out the Vajjians. Then the Blessed One, having risen at the break of day, saw with his divine eye, clear and surpassing the human, many deities taking up their dwelling places in Pāṭaligāma. In whatever place the powerful deities took up their dwelling places, there the minds of powerful kings and royal ministers inclined to build dwellings. In whatever place the middling deities took up their dwelling places, there the minds of middling kings and royal ministers inclined to build dwellings. In whatever place the lowly deities took up their dwelling places, there the minds of lowly kings and royal ministers inclined to build dwellings. Then the Blessed One addressed the Venerable Ānanda: “Ānanda, who is building a city at Pāṭaligāma?” “Sunidha and Vassakāra, Venerable Sir, the chief ministers of Magadha, are building a city at Pāṭaligāma to keep out the Vajjians.” “Just as if, Ānanda, they had consulted with the Tāvatiṃsa gods, so indeed, Ānanda, Sunidha and Vassakāra, the chief ministers of Magadha, are building a city at Pāṭaligāma to keep out the Vajjians. Here, Ānanda, having risen at the break of day, I saw with my divine eye, clear and surpassing the human, many deities taking up their dwelling places in Pāṭaligāma. In whatever place the powerful deities took up their dwelling places, there the minds of powerful kings and royal ministers inclined to build dwellings. In whatever place the middling deities took up their dwelling places, there the minds of middling kings and royal ministers inclined to build dwellings. In whatever place the lowly deities took up their dwelling places, there the minds of lowly kings and royal ministers inclined to build dwellings. Ānanda, as far as the Aryan territory extends, as far as the trade route reaches, this will be the foremost city—Pāṭaliputta, the breaking-open city. But, Ānanda, three dangers will come upon Pāṭaliputta—from fire, from water, or from internal dissension.”

Atha kho sunidhavassakārā magadhamahāmattā yena bhagavā tenupasaṅkamiṃsu, upasaṅkamitvā bhagavatā saddhiṃ sammodiṃsu, sammodanīyaṃ kathaṃ sāraṇīyaṃ vītisāretvā ekamantaṃ aṭṭhaṃsu. Ekamantaṃ ṭhitā kho sunidhavassakārā magadhamahāmattā bhagavantaṃ etadavocuṃ – ‘‘adhivāsetu no bhavaṃ gotamo ajjatanāya bhattaṃ saddhiṃ bhikkhusaṅghenā’’ti. Adhivāsesi bhagavā tuṇhībhāvena. Atha kho sunidhavassakārā magadhamahāmattā bhagavato adhivāsanaṃ viditvā pakkamiṃsu. Atha kho sunidhavassakārā magadhamahāmattā paṇītaṃ khādanīyaṃ bhojanīyaṃ paṭiyādāpetvā bhagavato kālaṃ ārocāpesuṃ – ‘‘kālo, bho gotama, niṭṭhitaṃ bhatta’’nti. Atha kho bhagavā pubbaṇhasamayaṃ nivāsetvā pattacīvaramādāya yena sunidhavassakārānaṃ magadhamahāmattānaṃ parivesanā tenupasaṅkami; upasaṅkamitvā paññatte āsane nisīdi saddhiṃ bhikkhusaṅghena. Atha kho sunidhavassakārā magadhamahāmattā buddhappamukhaṃ bhikkhusaṅghaṃ paṇītena khādanīyena bhojanīyena sahatthā santappetvā sampavāretvā bhagavantaṃ bhuttāviṃ onītapattapāṇiṃ ekamantaṃ nisīdiṃsu. Ekamantaṃ nisinne kho sunidhavassakāre magadhamahāmatte bhagavā imāhi gāthāhi anumodi –

Then the Magadhan ministers Sunidha and Vassakāra approached the Blessed One. Having approached, they exchanged greetings with the Blessed One. After exchanging polite conversation, they stood to one side. Standing to one side, the Magadhan ministers Sunidha and Vassakāra said to the Blessed One: “May Master Gotama accept our meal for today together with the Saṅgha of monks.” The Blessed One consented by silence. Then the Magadhan ministers Sunidha and Vassakāra, understanding the Blessed One’s consent, departed. Then the Magadhan ministers Sunidha and Vassakāra had fine food prepared and informed the Blessed One when the time came: “It is time, Master Gotama, the meal is ready.” Then the Blessed One, having dressed in the morning, took his bowl and robe and went to where the Magadhan ministers Sunidha and Vassakāra were serving the meal. Having arrived, he sat down on the prepared seat together with the Saṅgha of monks. Then the Magadhan ministers Sunidha and Vassakāra personally served and satisfied the Saṅgha of monks headed by the Buddha with fine food. When the Blessed One had finished eating and had removed his bowl, they sat down to one side. Sitting to one side, the Blessed One expressed his appreciation to the Magadhan ministers Sunidha and Vassakāra with these verses:

‘‘Yasmiṃ padese kappeti, vāsaṃ paṇḍitajātiyo;Sīlavantettha bhojetvā, saññate brahmacārayo [brahmacārino (syā.)].

“In whatever place a wise person makes their dwelling, There, having fed the virtuous, the restrained, the holy life practitioners…”

‘‘Yā tattha devatā āsuṃ, tāsaṃ dakkhiṇamādise;Tā pūjitā pūjayanti, mānitā mānayanti naṃ.

“Whatever deities were there, he dedicated a gift to them; Worshipped, they worship him; respected, they respect him.”

‘‘Tato naṃ anukampanti, mātā puttaṃva orasaṃ;Devatānukampito poso, sadā bhadrāni passatī’’ti.

“Then they pity him, as a mother pities her own child; A person pitied by the deities always sees auspicious things.”

Atha kho bhagavā sunidhavassakāre magadhamahāmatte imāhi gāthāhi anumoditvā uṭṭhāyāsanā pakkāmi. Tena kho pana samayena sunidhavassakārā magadhamahāmattā bhagavantaṃ piṭṭhito piṭṭhito anubandhā honti, ‘‘yenajja samaṇo gotamo dvārena nikkhamissati, taṃ gotamadvāraṃ nāma bhavissati; yena titthena gaṅgaṃ nadiṃ uttarissati, taṃ gotamatitthaṃ nāma bhavissatī’’ti. Atha kho bhagavā yena dvārena nikkhami, taṃ gotamadvāraṃ nāma ahosi. Atha kho bhagavā yena gaṅgā nadī tenupasaṅkami. Tena kho pana samayena gaṅgā nadī pūrā hoti samatittikā kākapeyyā. Manussā aññe nāvaṃ pariyesanti, aññe uḷumpaṃ pariyesanti, aññe kullaṃ bandhanti orā pāraṃ gantukāmā. Addasā kho bhagavā te manusse aññe nāvaṃ pariyesante, aññe uḷumpaṃ pariyesante, aññe kullaṃ bandhante orā pāraṃ gantukāme, disvāna seyyathāpi nāma balavā puriso samiñjitaṃ vā bāhaṃ pasāreyya, pasāritaṃ vā bāhaṃ samiñjeyya, evameva kho gaṅgāya nadiyā orimatīre antarahito pārimatīre paccuṭṭhāsi saddhiṃ bhikkhusaṅghena. Atha kho bhagavā etamatthaṃ viditvā tāyaṃ velāyaṃ imaṃ udānaṃ udānesi –

Then the Blessed One, having expressed his appreciation to Sunidha and Vassakāra, the chief ministers of Magadha, with these verses, rose from his seat and departed. At that time Sunidha and Vassakāra, the chief ministers of Magadha, followed closely behind the Blessed One, thinking, “The gate through which the ascetic Gotama exits today will be called the Gotama Gate, and the ford where he crosses the Ganges River will be called the Gotama Ford.” Then the Blessed One exited through a certain gate, and it became known as the Gotama Gate. Then the Blessed One approached the Ganges River. At that time the Ganges River was full, brimful, and overflowing, so that a crow could drink from it. Some people were searching for boats, others for rafts, and others were tying together floats, wanting to cross over to the other shore. The Blessed One saw those people searching for boats, some looking for rafts, others tying together floats, wanting to cross over to the other shore. Seeing this, just as easily as a strong man might stretch out his drawn-in arm or draw in his outstretched arm, so too did the Blessed One vanish from this bank of the Ganges River and reappear on the far bank together with the Saṅgha of monks. Then the Blessed One, understanding the meaning of this, at that time uttered this verse of elation:

‘‘Ye taranti aṇṇavaṃ saraṃ;Setuṃ katvāna visajja pallalāni;Kullañhi jano bandhati;Tiṇṇā medhāvino janā’’ti.

“Those who cross the ocean and the pool, Having made a bridge, they abandon the swamps; People indeed bind a raft; The wise have crossed over.”

Sunidhavassakāravatthu niṭṭhitaṃ.

The story of Sunidha and Vassakāra is concluded.

### 175. Koṭigāme saccakathā ^16

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv6-brahmali-pali#^16|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch5|BMC Chapter 5]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-MV6.16" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


175.The Talk of Truth at Koṭigāma

287. Atha kho bhagavā yena koṭigāmo tenupasaṅkami. Tatra sudaṃ bhagavā koṭigāme viharati. Tatra kho bhagavā bhikkhū āmantesi – [dī. ni. 2.155] ‘‘catunnaṃ, bhikkhave, ariyasaccānaṃ ananubodhā appaṭivedhā evamidaṃ dīghamaddhānaṃ sandhāvitaṃ saṃsaritaṃ mamañceva tumhākañca. Katamesaṃ catunnaṃ? Dukkhassa, bhikkhave, ariyasaccassa ananubodhā appaṭivedhā evamidaṃ dīghamaddhānaṃ sandhāvitaṃ saṃsaritaṃ mamañceva tumhākañca. Dukkhasamudayassa ariyasaccassa…pe… dukkhanirodhassa ariyasaccassa…pe… dukkhanirodhagāminiyā paṭipadāya ariyasaccassa ananubodhā appaṭivedhā evamidaṃ dīghamaddhānaṃ sandhāvitaṃ saṃsaritaṃ mamañceva tumhākañca. Tayidaṃ, bhikkhave, dukkhaṃ ariyasaccaṃ anubuddhaṃ paṭividdhaṃ, dukkhasamudayaṃ [dukkhasamudayo (syā.)] ariyasaccaṃ anubuddhaṃ paṭividdhaṃ, dukkhanirodhaṃ [dukkhanirodho (syā.)] ariyasaccaṃ anubuddhaṃ paṭividdhaṃ, dukkhanirodhagāminī paṭipadā ariyasaccaṃ anubuddhaṃ paṭividdhaṃ, ucchinnā bhavataṇhā, khīṇā bhavanetti, natthidāni punabbhavo’’ti.

287.Then the Blessed One approached Koṭigāma. There the Blessed One stayed at Koṭigāma. There the Blessed One addressed the monks: "Monks, it is through not understanding, not penetrating the four noble truths that this long wandering and transmigrating has continued for both me and you. Which four? It is through not understanding, not penetrating the noble truth of suffering that this long wandering and transmigrating has continued for both me and you. It is through not understanding, not penetrating the noble truth of the origin of suffering... It is through not understanding, not penetrating the noble truth of the cessation of suffering... It is through not understanding, not penetrating the noble truth of the path leading to the cessation of suffering that this long wandering and transmigrating has continued for both me and you. But now, monks, the noble truth of suffering has been understood and penetrated; the noble truth of the origin of suffering has been understood and penetrated; the noble truth of the cessation of suffering has been understood and penetrated; the noble truth of the path leading to the cessation of suffering has been understood and penetrated; craving for existence has been cut off; the leading-string to existence is destroyed; now there is no more renewed existence."

Catunnaṃ ariyasaccānaṃ, yathābhūtaṃ adassanā;Saṃsitaṃ dīghamaddhānaṃ, tāsu tāsveva jātisu.

Not seeing the Four Noble Truths as they really are, Long have I transmigrated Through those various existences.

Tāni etāni diṭṭhāni, bhavanetti samūhatā;Ucchinnaṃ mūlaṃ dukkhassa, natthidāni punabbhavoti.

These have been seen; The leading-string to existence has been uprooted; The root of suffering has been cut off; Now there is no more renewed existence.

Koṭigāme saccakathā niṭṭhitā.

The Talk on Truth at Koṭigāma is concluded.

### 176. Ambapālīvatthu ^17

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv6-brahmali-pali#^17|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch5|BMC Chapter 5]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-MV6.17" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


176.The Ambapālī Narrative

288. [dī. ni. 2.161 ādayo] Assosi kho ambapālī gaṇikā – bhagavā kira koṭigāmaṃ anuppattoti. Atha kho ambapālī gaṇikā bhadrāni bhadrāni yānāni yojāpetvā bhadraṃ bhadraṃ yānaṃ abhiruhitvā bhadrehi bhadrehi yānehi vesāliyā niyyāsi bhagavantaṃ dassanāya. Yāvatikā yānassa bhūmi, yānena gantvā, yānā paccorohitvā, pattikāva yena bhagavā tenupasaṅkami; upasaṅkamitvā bhagavantaṃ abhivādetvā ekamantaṃ nisīdi. Ekamantaṃ nisinnaṃ kho ambapāliṃ gaṇikaṃ bhagavā dhammiyā kathāya sandassesi samādapesi samuttejesi sampahaṃsesi. Atha kho ambapālī gaṇikā bhagavatā dhammiyā kathāya sandassitā samādapitā samuttejitā sampahaṃsitā bhagavantaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘adhivāsetu me, bhante, bhagavā svātanāya bhattaṃ saddhiṃ bhikkhusaṅghenā’’ti. Adhivāsesi bhagavā tuṇhībhāvena. Atha kho ambapālī gaṇikā bhagavato adhivāsanaṃ viditvā uṭṭhāyāsanā bhagavantaṃ abhivādetvā padakkhiṇaṃ katvā pakkāmi.

288.The courtesan Ambapālī heard that the Blessed One had arrived at Koṭigāma. Then Ambapālī had fine carriages harnessed, mounted a fine carriage, and set out from Vesālī in her fine carriages to see the Blessed One. She went as far as the carriage could go, then dismounted from the carriage and approached the Blessed One on foot. Having approached, she paid homage to the Blessed One and sat down to one side. Sitting to one side, the Blessed One instructed, inspired, aroused, and gladdened Ambapālī with a Dhamma talk. Then Ambapālī, having been instructed, inspired, aroused, and gladdened by the Blessed One with a Dhamma talk, said to him: "Venerable Sir, may the Blessed One, together with the Sangha of monks, accept my meal tomorrow." The Blessed One consented in silence. Then Ambapālī, knowing the Blessed One's consent, rose from her seat, paid homage to him, circumambulated him keeping the right side toward him, and departed.

Ambapālīvatthu niṭṭhitaṃ.

The Ambapālī Narrative is concluded.

### 177. Licchavīvatthu ^18

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv6-brahmali-pali#^18|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch5|BMC Chapter 5]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-MV6.18" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


177.The Licchavi Narrative

289. [dī. ni. 2.161 ādayo] Assosuṃ kho vesālikā licchavī – bhagavā kira koṭigāmaṃ anuppattoti. Atha kho vesālikā licchavī bhadrāni bhadrāni yānāni yojāpetvā bhadraṃ bhadraṃ yānaṃ abhiruhitvā bhadrehi bhadrehi yānehi vesāliyā niyyāsuṃ bhagavantaṃ dassanāya. Appekacce licchavī nīlā honti nīlavaṇṇā nīlavatthā nīlālaṅkārā, appekacce licchavī pītā honti pītavaṇṇā pītavatthā pītālaṅkārā, appekacce licchavī lohitā honti lohitavaṇṇā lohitavatthā lohitālaṅkārā, appekacce licchavī odātā honti odātavaṇṇā odātavatthā odātālaṅkārā. Atha kho ambapālī gaṇikā daharānaṃ daharānaṃ licchavīnaṃ īsāya īsaṃ yugena yugaṃ cakkena cakkaṃ akkhena akkhaṃ paṭivaṭṭesi [paṭivattesi (ka.)]. Atha kho te licchavī ambapāliṃ gaṇikaṃ etadavocuṃ – ‘‘kissa, je ambapāli, daharānaṃ daharānaṃ [amhākaṃ daharānaṃ daharānaṃ (sī. syā.)] licchavīnaṃ īsāya īsaṃ yugena yugaṃ cakkena cakkaṃ akkhena akkhaṃ paṭivaṭṭesī’’ti? ‘‘Tathā hi pana mayā, ayyaputtā, svātanāya buddhappamukho bhikkhusaṅgho nimantito’’ti. ‘‘Dehi, je ambapāli, amhākaṃ etaṃ bhattaṃ satasahassenā’’ti. ‘‘Sacepi me, ayyaputtā, vesāliṃ sāhāraṃ dajjeyyātha, neva dajjāhaṃ taṃ bhatta’’nti. Atha kho te licchavī aṅguliṃ phoṭesuṃ – ‘‘jitamhā vata, bho, ambakāya, parājitamha vata, bho, ambakāyā’’ti. Atha kho te licchavī yena bhagavā tenupasaṅkamiṃsu. Addasā kho bhagavā te licchavī dūratova āgacchante, disvāna bhikkhū āmantesi – ‘‘yehi, bhikkhave, bhikkhūhi devā tāvatiṃsā adiṭṭhapubbā, oloketha, bhikkhave, licchavīparisaṃ; apaloketha, bhikkhave, licchavīparisaṃ; upasaṃharatha, bhikkhave, licchavīparisaṃ tāvatiṃsaparisa’’nti. Atha kho te licchavī yāvatikā yānassa bhūmi, yānena gantvā yānā paccorohitvā pattikāva yena bhagavā tenupasaṅkamiṃsu; upasaṅkamitvā bhagavantaṃ abhivādetvā ekamantaṃ nisīdiṃsu. Ekamantaṃ nisinne kho te licchavī bhagavā dhammiyā kathāya sandassesi samādapesi samuttejesi sampahaṃsesi. Atha kho te licchavī, bhagavatā dhammiyā kathāya sandassitā samādapitā samuttejitā sampahaṃsitā bhagavantaṃ etadavocuṃ – ‘‘adhivāsetu no, bhante, bhagavā svātanāya bhattaṃ saddhiṃ bhikkhusaṅghenā’’ti. ‘‘Adhivuṭṭhomhi, licchavī, svātanāya ambapāliyā gaṇikāya bhatta’’nti. Atha kho te licchavī aṅguliṃ phoṭesuṃ – ‘‘jitamha vata, bho, ambakāya, parājitamha vata, bho, ambakāyā’’ti. Atha kho te licchavī bhagavato bhāsitaṃ abhinanditvā anumoditvā uṭṭhāyāsanā bhagavantaṃ abhivādetvā padakkhiṇaṃ katvā pakkamiṃsu.

289.The Licchavis of Vesālī heard that the Blessed One had arrived at Koṭigāma. Then the Licchavis of Vesālī had fine carriages harnessed, mounted fine carriages, and set out from Vesālī in fine carriages to see the Blessed One. Some Licchavis were blue-colored, dressed in blue, adorned with blue. Some Licchavis were yellow-colored, dressed in yellow, adorned with yellow. Some Licchavis were red-colored, dressed in red, adorned with red. Some Licchavis were white-colored, dressed in white, adorned with white. Then the courtesan Ambapālī overtook the young Licchavis, chariot by chariot, yoke by yoke, wheel by wheel, axle by axle. Then those Licchavis said to the courtesan Ambapālī: "Why, lady Ambapālī, do you overtake the young Licchavis, chariot by chariot, yoke by yoke, wheel by wheel, axle by axle?" "Because, young lords, I have invited the Sangha of monks headed by the Buddha for tomorrow's meal." "Give us, lady Ambapālī, this meal for a hundred thousand." "Even if you were to give me Vesālī with its revenues, I would not give up this meal." Then those Licchavis snapped their fingers, saying: "We are beaten, sirs, by the mango woman! We are defeated, sirs, by the mango woman!" Then those Licchavis approached the Blessed One. The Blessed One saw those Licchavis coming from afar and addressed the monks: "Monks, those monks who have never seen the Tāvatiṃsa gods, look at this assembly of Licchavis! Observe this assembly of Licchavis! Compare this assembly of Licchavis to the assembly of Tāvatiṃsa gods!" Then those Licchavis went as far as the ground was passable by carriage, then dismounted from the carriages and approached the Blessed One on foot. Having approached, they paid homage to the Blessed One and sat down to one side. While sitting to one side, the Blessed One instructed, inspired, aroused, and gladdened those Licchavis with a Dhamma talk. Then those Licchavis, having been instructed, inspired, aroused, and gladdened by the Blessed One's Dhamma talk, said to the Blessed One: "Venerable sir, may the Blessed One together with the Sangha of monks accept our meal for tomorrow." "Licchavis, I have already accepted tomorrow's meal from the courtesan Ambapālī." Then those Licchavis snapped their fingers, saying: "We are beaten, sirs, by the mango woman! We are defeated, sirs, by the mango woman!" Then those Licchavis, having rejoiced and delighted in the Blessed One's words, rose from their seats, paid homage to the Blessed One, circumambulated him keeping the right side toward him, and departed.

Atha kho bhagavā koṭigāme yathābhirantaṃ viharitvā [mahāparinibbānasutte anusandhi aññathā āgato] yena nātikā [nādikā (sī. syā.)] tenupasaṅkami. Tatra sudaṃ bhagavā nātike viharati giñjakāvasathe. Atha kho ambapālī gaṇikā tassā rattiyā accayena sake ārāme paṇītaṃ khādanīyaṃ bhojanīyaṃ paṭiyādāpetvā bhagavato kālaṃ ārocāpesi – ‘‘kālo, bhante, niṭṭhitaṃ bhatta’’nti. Atha kho bhagavā pubbaṇhasamayaṃ nivāsetvā pattacīvaramādāya yena ambapāliyā gaṇikāya parivesanā tenupasaṅkami; upasaṅkamitvā paññatte āsane nisīdi saddhiṃ bhikkhusaṅghena. Atha kho ambapālī gaṇikā buddhappamukhaṃ bhikkhusaṅghaṃ paṇītena khādanīyena bhojanīyena sahatthā santappetvā sampavāretvā bhagavantaṃ bhuttāviṃ onītapattapāṇiṃ ekamantaṃ nisīdi. Ekamantaṃ nisinnā kho ambapālī gaṇikā bhagavantaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘imāhaṃ, bhante, ambavanaṃ buddhappamukhassa bhikkhusaṅghassa dammī’’ti. Paṭiggahesi bhagavā ārāmaṃ. Atha kho bhagavā ambapāliṃ gaṇikaṃ dhammiyā kathāya sandassetvā samādapetvā samuttejetvā sampahaṃsetvā uṭṭhāyāsanā yena mahāvanaṃ tenupasaṅkami. Tatra sudaṃ bhagavā vesāliyaṃ viharati mahāvane kūṭāgārasālāyaṃ.

Then the Blessed One, having stayed at Koṭigāma as long as he pleased, set out for Nātikā. There the Blessed One stayed at Nātikā in the Giñjakā rest house. Then the courtesan Ambapālī, when the night had passed, had fine food prepared in her own park and sent word to the Blessed One: "It is time, Venerable Sir, the meal is ready." Then the Blessed One, having dressed in the morning, took his bowl and robe and went to the residence of the courtesan Ambapālī; having arrived, he sat down on the prepared seat together with the community of monks. Then the courtesan Ambapālī personally served and satisfied the community of monks headed by the Buddha with fine food and drink. When the Blessed One had finished his meal and had put away his bowl and hand, she sat down to one side. Sitting to one side, the courtesan Ambapālī said to the Blessed One: "Venerable Sir, I give this mango grove to the community of monks headed by the Buddha." The Blessed One accepted the park. Then the Blessed One, having instructed, inspired, aroused, and gladdened the courtesan Ambapālī with a Dhamma talk, rose from his seat and went to the Great Wood. There the Blessed One stayed at Vesālī in the Great Wood, in the hall with the peaked roof.

Licchavīvatthu niṭṭhitaṃ.

The Licchavi Narrative is concluded.

Licchavibhāṇavāro niṭṭhito tatiyo.

The third recitation section on the Licchavis is concluded.

### 178. Sīhasenāpativatthu ^19

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv6-brahmali-pali#^19|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch5|BMC Chapter 5]] and the following cites:

> "VIN-MV6.19" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


178.The Story of General Sīha

290. [a. ni. 8.12 ādayo] Tena kho pana samayena abhiññātā abhiññātā licchavī sandhāgāre [santhāgāre (sī. syā.)] sannisinnā sannipatitā anekapariyāyena buddhassa vaṇṇaṃ bhāsanti, dhammassa vaṇṇaṃ bhāsanti, saṅghassa vaṇṇaṃ bhāsanti. Tena kho pana samayena sīho senāpati nigaṇṭhasāvako tassaṃ parisāyaṃ nisinno hoti. Atha kho sīhassa senāpatissa etadahosi – ‘‘nissaṃsayaṃ kho so bhagavā arahaṃ sammāsambuddho bhavissati, tathā hime abhiññātā abhiññātā licchavī santhāgāre sannisinnā sannipatitā anekapariyāyena buddhassa vaṇṇaṃ bhāsanti, dhammassa vaṇṇaṃ bhāsanti, saṅghassa vaṇṇaṃ bhāsanti. Yaṃnūnāhaṃ taṃ bhagavantaṃ dassanāya upasaṅkameyyaṃ arahantaṃ sammāsambuddha’’nti. Atha kho sīho senāpati yena nigaṇṭho nāṭaputto tenupasaṅkami, upasaṅkamitvā nigaṇṭhaṃ nāṭaputtaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘icchāmahaṃ, bhante, samaṇaṃ gotamaṃ dassanāya upasaṅkamitu’’nti. ‘‘Kiṃ pana tvaṃ, sīha, kiriyavādo samāno akiriyavādaṃ samaṇaṃ gotamaṃ dassanāya upasaṅkamissasi? Samaṇo hi, sīha, gotamo akiriyavādo akiriyāya dhammaṃ deseti, tena ca sāvake vinetī’’ti. Atha kho sīhassa senāpatissa yo ahosi gamikābhisaṅkhāro bhagavantaṃ dassanāya, so paṭippassambhi. Dutiyampi kho abhiññātā abhiññātā licchavī sandhāgāre sannisinnā sannipatitā anekapariyānena buddhassa vaṇṇaṃ bhāsanti, dhammassa vaṇṇaṃ bhāsanti, saṅghassa vaṇṇaṃ bhāsanti. Dutiyampi kho sīhassa senāpatissa etadahosi – ‘‘nissaṃsayaṃ kho so bhagavā arahaṃ sammāsambuddho bhavissati, tathā hime abhiññātā abhiññātā licchavī sandhāgāre sannisinnā sannipatitā anekapariyāyena buddhassa vaṇṇaṃ bhāsanti, dhammassa vaṇṇaṃ bhāsanti, saṅghassa vaṇṇaṃ bhāsanti. Yaṃnūnāhaṃ taṃ bhagavantaṃ dassanāya upasaṅkameyyaṃ arahantaṃ sammāsambuddha’’nti. Dutiyampi kho sīho senāpati yena nigaṇṭho nāṭaputto tenupasaṅkami, upasaṅkamitvā nigaṇṭhaṃ nāṭaputtaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘icchāmahaṃ, bhante, samaṇaṃ gotamaṃ dassanāya upasaṅkamitu’’nti. ‘‘Kiṃ pana tvaṃ, sīha, kiriyavādo samāno akiriyavādaṃ samaṇaṃ gotamaṃ dassanāya upasaṅkamissasi? Samaṇo hi, sīha, gotamo akiriyavādo akiriyāya dhammaṃ deseti, tena ca sāvake vinetī’’ti. Dutiyampi kho sīhassa senāpatissa yo ahosi gamikābhisaṅkhāro bhagavantaṃ dassanāya, so paṭippassambhi. Tatiyampi kho abhiññātā abhiññātā licchavī sandhāgāre sannisinnā sannipatitā anekapariyāyena buddhassa vaṇṇaṃ bhāsanti, dhammassa vaṇṇaṃ bhāsanti, saṅghassa vaṇṇaṃ bhāsanti. Tatiyampi kho sīhassa senāpatissa etadahosi – ‘‘nissaṃsayaṃ kho so bhagavā arahaṃ sammāsambuddho bhavissati, tathā hime abhiññātā abhiññātā licchavī sandhāgāre sannisinnā sannipatitā anekapariyāyena buddhassa vaṇṇaṃ bhāsanti, dhammassa vaṇṇaṃ bhāsanti, saṅghassa vaṇṇaṃ bhāsanti. Kiñhi me karissanti nigaṇṭhā apalokitā vā anapalokitā vā? Yaṃnūnāhaṃ anapaloketvāva nigaṇṭhe taṃ bhagavantaṃ dassanāya upasaṅkameyyaṃ arahantaṃ sammāsambuddha’’nti.

290.Now at that time, the well-known Licchavis were seated and assembled in the assembly hall, engaged in various discussions praising the Buddha, the Dhamma, and the Saṅgha. At that time, General Sīha, a disciple of the Nigaṇṭhas, was sitting in that assembly. Then General Sīha thought: "Surely, that Blessed One must be an Arahant, a Perfectly Self-Enlightened One, since these well-known Licchavis are seated and assembled in the assembly hall, engaged in various discussions praising the Buddha, the Dhamma, and the Saṅgha. Why don’t I go to see that Blessed One, the Arahant, the Perfectly Self-Enlightened One?" Then General Sīha approached the Nigaṇṭha Nāṭaputta and said: "Venerable sir, I wish to go see the ascetic Gotama." The Nigaṇṭha Nāṭaputta replied: "Why, Sīha, as one who advocates action, would you go to see the ascetic Gotama, who advocates non-action? For the ascetic Gotama teaches the doctrine of non-action and trains his disciples accordingly." At that, General Sīha’s intention to visit the Blessed One subsided. A second time, the well-known Licchavis were seated and assembled in the assembly hall, engaged in various discussions praising the Buddha, the Dhamma, and the Saṅgha. A second time, General Sīha thought: "Surely, that Blessed One must be an Arahant, a Perfectly Self-Enlightened One, since these well-known Licchavis are seated and assembled in the assembly hall, engaged in various discussions praising the Buddha, the Dhamma, and the Saṅgha. Why don’t I go to see that Blessed One, the Arahant, the Perfectly Self-Enlightened One?" A second time, General Sīha approached the Nigaṇṭha Nāṭaputta and said: "Venerable sir, I wish to go see the ascetic Gotama." Again, the Nigaṇṭha Nāṭaputta replied: "Why, Sīha, as one who advocates action, would you go to see the ascetic Gotama, who advocates non-action? For the ascetic Gotama teaches the doctrine of non-action and trains his disciples accordingly." A second time, General Sīha’s intention to visit the Blessed One subsided. A third time, the well-known Licchavis were seated and assembled in the assembly hall, engaged in various discussions praising the Buddha, the Dhamma, and the Saṅgha. A third time, General Sīha thought: "Surely, that Blessed One must be an Arahant, a Perfectly Self-Enlightened One, since these well-known Licchavis are seated and assembled in the assembly hall, engaged in various discussions praising the Buddha, the Dhamma, and the Saṅgha. What can the Nigaṇṭhas do to me, whether I ask for their permission or not? Why don’t I go to see that Blessed One, the Arahant, the Perfectly Self-Enlightened One, without asking permission from the Nigaṇṭhas?"

Atha kho sīho senāpati pañcahi rathasatehi divā divassa vesāliyā niyyāsi bhagavantaṃ dassanāya. Yāvatikā yānassa bhūmi, yānena gantvā yānā paccorohitvā pattikova yena bhagavā tenupasaṅkami; upasaṅkamitvā bhagavantaṃ abhivādetvā ekamantaṃ nisīdi. Ekamantaṃ nisinno kho sīho senāpati bhagavantaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘sutaṃ me taṃ, bhante, ‘akiriyavādo samaṇo gotamo akiriyāya dhammaṃ deseti, tena ca sāvake vinetī’ti. Ye te, bhante, evamāhaṃsu ‘akiriyavādo samaṇo gotamo, akiriyāya dhammaṃ deseti, tena ca sāvake vinetī’ti. Kacci te, bhante, bhagavato vuttavādino, na ca bhagavantaṃ abhūtena abbhācikkhanti, dhammassa cānudhammaṃ byākaronti, na ca koci sahadhammiko vādānuvādo gārayhaṃ ṭhānaṃ āgacchati? Anabbhakkhātukāmā hi mayaṃ, bhante, bhagavanta’’nti.

Then General Sīha set out from Vesālī in the middle of the day with five hundred chariots to see the Blessed One. As far as the ground was passable for vehicles, he went by vehicle; then dismounting from the vehicle, he approached the Blessed One on foot. Having approached, he paid homage to the Blessed One and sat down to one side. Sitting to one side, General Sīha said to the Blessed One: "Venerable sir, I have heard this: 'The ascetic Gotama is a proponent of inaction; he teaches the Dhamma of inaction, and disciplines his disciples accordingly.' Those, venerable sir, who say this: 'The ascetic Gotama is a proponent of inaction; he teaches the Dhamma of inaction, and disciplines his disciples accordingly'—do they speak in accordance with the Blessed One's words, and not misrepresent the Blessed One with what is untrue? Do they explain the Dhamma in accordance with the Dhamma, so that no legitimate ground for criticism arises from their assertion? For we do not wish, venerable sir, to misrepresent the Blessed One."

291. ‘‘Atthi, sīha, pariyāyo, yena maṃ pariyāyena sammā vadamāno vadeyya – akiriyavādo samaṇo gotamo, akiriyāya dhammaṃ deseti, tena ca sāvake vinetīti. Atthi, sīha, pariyāyo, yena maṃ pariyāyena sammā vadamāno vadeyya – kiriyavādo samaṇo gotamo kiriyāya dhammaṃ deseti, tena ca sāvake vinetīti. Atthi, sīha, pariyāyo yena maṃ pariyāyena sammā vadamāno vadeyya – ucchedavādo samaṇo gotamo ucchedāya dhammaṃ deseti, tena ca sāvake vinetīti. Atthi, sīha, pariyāyo, yena maṃ pariyāyena sammā vadamāno vadeyya – jegucchī samaṇo gotamo, jegucchitāya dhammaṃ deseti, tena ca sāvake vinetīti. Atthi, sīha, pariyāyo, yena maṃ pariyāyena sammā vadamāno vadeyya – venayiko samaṇo gotamo, vinayāya dhammaṃ deseti, tena ca sāvake vinetīti. Atthi, sīha, pariyāyo, yena maṃ pariyāyena sammā vadamāno vadeyya – tapassī samaṇo gotamo, tapassitāya dhammaṃ deseti, tena ca sāvake vinetīti. Atthi, sīha, pariyāyo, yena maṃ pariyāyena sammā vadamāno vadeyya – apagabbho samaṇo gotamo, apagabbhatāya dhammaṃ deseti, tena ca sāvake vinetīti. Atthi, sīha, pariyāyo, yena maṃ pariyāyena sammā vadamāno vadeyya – assattho samaṇo gotamo, assāsāya dhammaṃ deseti, tena ca sāvake vinetīti.

291."Sīha, there is a way in which one speaking rightly might say of me: 'The ascetic Gotama is an advocate of inaction; he teaches the doctrine of inaction, and trains his disciples accordingly.' Sīha, there is a way in which one speaking rightly might say of me: 'The ascetic Gotama is an advocate of action; he teaches the doctrine of action, and trains his disciples accordingly.' Sīha, there is a way in which one speaking rightly might say of me: 'The ascetic Gotama is an advocate of annihilation; he teaches the doctrine of annihilation, and trains his disciples accordingly.' Sīha, there is a way in which one speaking rightly might say of me: 'The ascetic Gotama is disgusted; he teaches the doctrine of disgust, and trains his disciples accordingly.' Sīha, there is a way in which one speaking rightly might say of me: 'The ascetic Gotama is an advocate of training; he teaches the doctrine of training, and trains his disciples accordingly.' Sīha, there is a way in which one speaking rightly might say of me: 'The ascetic Gotama is an ascetic; he teaches the doctrine of asceticism, and trains his disciples accordingly.' Sīha, there is a way in which one speaking rightly might say of me: 'The ascetic Gotama is not arrogant; he teaches the doctrine of non-arrogance, and trains his disciples accordingly.' Sīha, there is a way in which one speaking rightly might say of me: 'The ascetic Gotama brings reassurance; he teaches the doctrine of reassurance, and trains his disciples accordingly.'"

292. ‘‘Katamo ca, sīha, pariyāyo, yena maṃ pariyāyena sammā vadamāno vadeyya – akiriyavādo samaṇo gotamo, akiriyāya dhammaṃ deseti, tena ca sāvake vinetīti? Ahañhi, sīha, akiriyaṃ vadāmi kāyaduccaritassa vacīduccaritassa manoduccaritassa; anekavihitānaṃ pāpakānaṃ akusalānaṃ dhammānaṃ akiriyaṃ vadāmi. Ayaṃ kho, sīha, pariyāyo, yena maṃ pariyāyena sammā vadamāno vadeyya – akiriyavādo samaṇo gotamo, akiriyāya dhammaṃ deseti, tena ca sāvake vinetīti.

292."And what, Sīha, is the way by which one, speaking rightly, might say of me: ‘The ascetic Gotama is an advocate of inaction; he teaches the doctrine of inaction, and trains his disciples accordingly’? For I, Sīha, proclaim inaction in regard to misconduct of body, speech, and mind; I proclaim inaction in regard to the many kinds of evil, unwholesome qualities. This, Sīha, is the way by which one, speaking rightly, might say of me: ‘The ascetic Gotama is an advocate of inaction; he teaches the doctrine of inaction, and trains his disciples accordingly.’"

‘‘Katamo ca, sīha, pariyāyo, yena maṃ pariyāyena sammā vadamāno vadeyya – kiriyavādo samaṇo gotamo, kiriyāya dhammaṃ deseti, tena ca sāvake vinetīti? Ahañhi, sīha, kiriyaṃ vadāmi kāyasucaritassa vacīsucaritassa manosucaritassa, anekavihitānaṃ kusalānaṃ dhammānaṃ kiriyaṃ vadāmi. Ayaṃ kho, sīha, pariyāyo, yena maṃ pariyāyena sammā vadamāno vadeyya – kiriyavādo samaṇo gotamo, kiriyāya dhammaṃ deseti, tena ca sāvake vinetīti.

"And what, Sīha, is the way by which one speaking rightly might say of me: 'The ascetic Gotama is an advocate of action; he teaches the doctrine of action, and trains his disciples accordingly'? For I, Sīha, proclaim action in regard to good bodily conduct, good verbal conduct, and good mental conduct; I proclaim action in regard to the many kinds of wholesome qualities. This, Sīha, is the way by which one speaking rightly might say of me: 'The ascetic Gotama is an advocate of action; he teaches the doctrine of action, and trains his disciples accordingly.'"

‘‘Katamo ca, sīha, pariyāyo, yena maṃ pariyāyena sammā vadamāno vadeyya – ucchedavādo samaṇo gotamo, ucchedāya dhammaṃ deseti, tena ca sāvake vinetīti? Ahañhi, sīha, ucchedaṃ vadāmi rāgassa dosassa mohassa; anekavihitānaṃ pāpakānaṃ akusalānaṃ dhammānaṃ ucchedaṃ vadāmi. Ayaṃ kho, sīha, pariyāyo, yena maṃ pariyāyena sammā vadamāno vadeyya – ucchedavādo samaṇo gotamo ucchedāya dhammaṃ deseti, tena ca sāvake vinetīti.

"And what, Sīha, is the way by which one speaking rightly might say of me: 'The ascetic Gotama is an advocate of annihilation; he teaches the doctrine of annihilation, and trains his disciples accordingly'? For I, Sīha, proclaim the annihilation of lust, hate, and delusion; I proclaim the annihilation of many kinds of evil, unwholesome qualities. This, Sīha, is the way by which one speaking rightly might say of me: 'The ascetic Gotama is an advocate of annihilation; he teaches the doctrine of annihilation, and trains his disciples accordingly.'"

‘‘Katamo ca, sīha, pariyāyo yena maṃ pariyāyena sammā vadamāno vadeyya – jegucchī samaṇo gotamo, jegucchitāya dhammaṃ deseti, tena ca sāvake vinetīti? Ahañhi, sīha, jigucchāmi kāyaduccaritena vacīduccaritena manoduccaritena; anekavihitānaṃ pāpakānaṃ akusalānaṃ dhammānaṃ samāpattiyā jigucchāmi. Ayaṃ kho, sīha, pariyāyo, yena maṃ pariyāyena sammā vadamāno vadeyya – jegucchī samaṇo gotamo, jegucchitāya dhammaṃ deseti, tena ca sāvake vinetīti.

"And what, Sīha, is the principle by which one speaking rightly might say of me: 'The ascetic Gotama is scrupulous; he teaches a doctrine of scrupulousness, and he trains his disciples accordingly'? For I, Sīha, am scrupulous about misconduct of body, misconduct of speech, and misconduct of mind; I am scrupulous about engaging in various kinds of evil, unwholesome states. This, Sīha, is the principle by which one speaking rightly might say of me: 'The ascetic Gotama is scrupulous; he teaches a doctrine of scrupulousness, and he trains his disciples accordingly.'"

‘‘Katamo ca, sīha, pariyāyo, yena maṃ pariyāyena sammā vadamāno vadeyya – venayiko samaṇo gotamo, vinayāya dhammaṃ deseti, tena ca sāvake vinetīti? Ahañhi, sīha, vinayāya dhammaṃ desemi rāgassa dosassa mohassa; anekavihitānaṃ pāpakānaṃ akusalānaṃ dhammānaṃ vinayāya dhammaṃ desemi. Ayaṃ kho, sīha, pariyāyo, yena maṃ pariyāyena sammā vadamāno vadeyya – venayiko samaṇo gotamo, vinayāya dhammaṃ deseti, tena ca sāvake vinetīti.

"And what, Sīha, is the principle by which one speaking rightly might say of me: 'The ascetic Gotama is a discipliner; he teaches the Dhamma for discipline, and he trains his disciples accordingly'? For I, Sīha, teach the Dhamma for the discipline of lust, hate, and delusion; I teach the Dhamma for the discipline of various kinds of evil, unwholesome states. This, Sīha, is the principle by which one speaking rightly might say of me: 'The ascetic Gotama is a discipliner; he teaches the Dhamma for discipline, and he trains his disciples accordingly.'"

‘‘Katamo ca, sīha, pariyāyo, yena maṃ pariyāyena sammā vadamāno vadeyya – tapassī samaṇo gotamo, tapassitāya dhammaṃ deseti, tena ca sāvake vinetīti? Tapanīyāhaṃ, sīha, pāpake akusale dhamme vadāmi – kāyaduccaritaṃ vacīduccaritaṃ manoduccaritaṃ. Yassa kho, sīha, tapanīyā pāpakā akusalā dhammā pahīnā ucchinnamūlā tālāvatthukatā anabhāvaṅkatā āyatiṃ anuppādadhammā, tamahaṃ tapassīti vadāmi. Tathāgatassa kho, sīha, tapanīyā pāpakā akusalā dhammā pahīnā ucchīnnamūlā tālāvatthukatā anabhāvaṃkatā āyatiṃ anuppādadhammā. Ayaṃ kho, sīha, pariyāyo, yena maṃ pariyāyena sammā vadamāno vadeyya ‘‘tapassī samaṇo gotamo tapassitāya dhammaṃ deseti, tena ca sāvake vinetī’’ti.

"And what, Sīha, is the principle by which one speaking rightly might say of me: 'The ascetic Gotama is an ascetic; he teaches a doctrine of asceticism, and he trains his disciples accordingly'? I declare, Sīha, that evil, unwholesome states are to be burnt away—misconduct of body, misconduct of speech, and misconduct of mind. Whoever, Sīha, has abandoned these evil, unwholesome states to be burnt away—cut off at the root, made like a palm stump, obliterated, so that they are no more subject to future arising—him I call an ascetic. For the Tathāgata, Sīha, these evil, unwholesome states to be burnt away have been abandoned, cut off at the root, made like a palm stump, obliterated, so that they are no more subject to future arising. This, Sīha, is the principle by which one speaking rightly might say of me: 'The ascetic Gotama is an ascetic; he teaches a doctrine of asceticism, and he trains his disciples accordingly.'"

‘‘Katamo ca, sīha, pariyāyo, yena maṃ pariyāyena sammā vadamāno vadeyya – apagabbho samaṇo gotamo apagabbhatāya dhammaṃ deseti, tena ca sāvake vinetīti? Yassa kho, sīha, āyatiṃ gabbhaseyyā punabbhavābhinibbatti pahīnā ucchinnamūlā tālāvatthukatā anabhāvaṃkatā āyatiṃ anuppādadhammā, tamahaṃ apagabbhoti vadāmi. Tathāgatassa kho, sīha, āyatiṃ gabbhaseyyā punabbhavābhinibbatti pahīnā ucchinnamūlā tālāvatthukatā anabhāvaṃkatā āyatiṃ anuppādadhammā. Ayaṃ kho, sīha, pariyāyo, yena maṃ pariyāyena sammā vadamāno vadeyya – apagabbho samaṇo gotamo, apagabbhatāya dhammaṃ deseti, tena ca sāvake vinetīti.

"And what, Sīha, is the principle by which one speaking rightly might say of me: 'The ascetic Gotama is one who is free from rebirth; he teaches the Dhamma for freedom from rebirth, and he trains his disciples accordingly'? Whoever, Sīha, has abandoned future lying in the womb, renewal of being, and fresh becoming—cut off at the root, made like a palm stump, obliterated, so that they are no more subject to future arising—him I call one who is free from rebirth. For the Tathāgata, Sīha, future lying in the womb, renewal of being, and fresh becoming have been abandoned, cut off at the root, made like a palm stump, obliterated, so that they are no more subject to future arising. This, Sīha, is the principle by which one speaking rightly might say of me: 'The ascetic Gotama is one who is free from rebirth; he teaches the Dhamma for freedom from rebirth, and he trains his disciples accordingly.'"

‘‘Katamo ca, sīha, pariyāyo, yena maṃ pariyāyena sammā vadamāno vadeyya – assattho samaṇo gotamo assāsāya dhammaṃ deseti, tena ca sāvake vinetīti? Ahañhi, sīha, assattho paramena assāsena, assāsāya dhammaṃ desemi, tena ca sāvake vinemi. Ayaṃ kho, sīha, pariyāyo, yena maṃ pariyāyena sammā vadamāno vadeyya – assattho samaṇo gotamo assāsāya dhammaṃ deseti, tena ca sāvake vinetī’’ti.

"And what, Sīha, is the principle by which one speaking rightly might say of me: 'The ascetic Gotama is at peace; he teaches the Dhamma for peace, and he trains his disciples accordingly'? For I, Sīha, am at peace with the highest peace; I teach the Dhamma for peace, and I train my disciples accordingly. This, Sīha, is the principle by which one speaking rightly might say of me: 'The ascetic Gotama is at peace; he teaches the Dhamma for peace, and he trains his disciples accordingly.'"

293. Evaṃ vutte sīho senāpati bhagavantaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘abhikkantaṃ, bhante…pe… upāsakaṃ maṃ bhagavā dhāretu ajjatagge pāṇupetaṃ saraṇaṃ gata’’nti. ‘‘Anuviccakāraṃ [anuvijjakāraṃ (ka.)] kho, sīha, karohi; anuviccakāro tumhādisānaṃ ñātamanussānaṃ sādhu hotī’’ti. ‘‘Imināpāhaṃ, bhante, bhagavato bhiyyosomattāya attamano abhiraddho, yaṃ maṃ bhagavā evamāha – ‘anuviccakāraṃ kho, sīha, karohi; anuviccakāro tumhādisānaṃ ñātamanussānaṃ sādhu hotī’ti. Mamañhi, bhante, aññatitthiyā sāvakaṃ labhitvā kevalakappaṃ vesāliṃ paṭākaṃ parihareyyuṃ – ‘sīho kho amhākaṃ senāpati sāvakattaṃ upagato’ti. Atha ca pana maṃ bhagavā evamāha – ‘anuviccakāraṃ kho, sīha, karohi; anuviccakāro tumhādisānaṃ ñātamanussānaṃ sādhu hotī’ti. Esāhaṃ, bhante, dutiyampi bhagavantaṃ saraṇaṃ gacchāmi dhammañca bhikkhusaṅghañca. Upāsakaṃ maṃ bhagavā dhāretu ajjatagge pāṇupetaṃ saraṇaṃ gata’’nti. ‘‘Dīgharattaṃ kho te, sīha, nigaṇṭhānaṃ opānabhūtaṃ kulaṃ, yena nesaṃ upagatānaṃ piṇḍakaṃ dātabbaṃ maññeyyāsī’’ti. ‘‘Imināpāhaṃ, bhante, bhagavato bhiyyosomattāya attamano abhiraddho, yaṃ maṃ bhagavā evamāha – ‘dīgharattaṃ kho te, sīha, nigaṇṭhānaṃ opānabhūtaṃ kulaṃ, yena nesaṃ upagatānaṃ piṇḍakaṃ dātabbaṃ maññeyyāsī’ti. Sutaṃ me taṃ, bhante, samaṇo gotamo evamāha – ‘mayhameva dānaṃ dātabbaṃ, na aññesaṃ dānaṃ dātabbaṃ; mayhameva sāvakānaṃ dānaṃ dātabbaṃ, na aññesaṃ sāvakānaṃ dānaṃ dātabbaṃ; mayhameva dinnaṃ mahapphalaṃ, na aññesaṃ dinnaṃ mahapphalaṃ; mayhameva sāvakānaṃ dinnaṃ mahapphalaṃ, na aññesaṃ sāvakānaṃ dinnaṃ mahapphala’nti. Atha ca pana maṃ bhagavā nigaṇṭhesupi dāne samādapeti. Api ca, bhante, mayamettha kālaṃ jānissāma. Esāhaṃ, bhante, tatiyampi bhagavantaṃ saraṇaṃ gacchāmi dhammañca bhikkhusaṅghañca. Upāsakaṃ maṃ bhagavā dhāretu ajjatagge pāṇupetaṃ saraṇaṃ gata’’nti.

293.When this was said, General Sīha said this to the Blessed One: "Magnificent, venerable sir! Magnificent! Just as if he were to set upright what had been overturned, or to reveal what was hidden, or to show the way to one who was lost, or to light a lamp in the darkness so that those with eyesight can see forms—in the same way has the Blessed One made the Dhamma clear in various ways. I go for refuge to the Blessed One, to the Dhamma, and to the Saṅgha of bhikkhus. May the Blessed One remember me as a lay follower who has gone for refuge from this day forward for as long as life lasts." "Consider carefully, Sīha; careful consideration is good for people like you, who are well-known." "Venerable sir, I am even more pleased and delighted with the Blessed One for saying this: 'Consider carefully, Sīha; careful consideration is good for people like you, who are well-known.' For if other sectarians were to obtain me as a disciple, they would carry a banner all around Vesālī, proclaiming: 'General Sīha has become our disciple!' Yet the Blessed One tells me: 'Consider carefully, Sīha...' So, venerable sir, for the second time I go for refuge to the Blessed One, to the Dhamma, and to the Saṅgha of bhikkhus. May the Blessed One remember me as a lay follower who has gone for refuge from this day forward for as long as life lasts." "Your family, Sīha, has long been like a well of water for the Nigaṇṭhas, so you should think of giving alms to them when they come." "Venerable sir, I am even more pleased and delighted with the Blessed One for saying this: 'Your family, Sīha, has long been like a well of water for the Nigaṇṭhas, so you should think of giving alms to them when they come.' For I have heard, venerable sir, that the ascetic Gotama says: 'Gifts should be given only to me; gifts should not be given to others. Gifts should be given only to my disciples; gifts should not be given to the disciples of others. What is given to me is of great fruit; what is given to others is not of great fruit. What is given to my disciples is of great fruit; what is given to the disciples of others is not of great fruit.' Yet the Blessed One encourages me to give to the Nigaṇṭhas as well. But, venerable sir, we will know the proper time for this. So, venerable sir, for the third time I go for refuge to the Blessed One, to the Dhamma, and to the Saṅgha of bhikkhus. May the Blessed One remember me as a lay follower who has gone for refuge from this day forward for as long as life lasts."

Atha kho bhagavā sīhassa senāpatissa anupubbiṃ kathaṃ kathesi, seyyathidaṃ – dānakathaṃ…pe… aparappaccayo satthusāsane bhagavantaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘adhivāsetu me, bhante, bhagavā svātanāya bhattaṃ saddhiṃ bhikkhusaṅghenā’’ti. Adhivāsesi bhagavā tuṇhībhāvena. Atha kho sīho senāpati bhagavato adhivāsanaṃ viditvā uṭṭhāyāsanā bhagavantaṃ abhivādetvā padakkhiṇaṃ katvā pakkāmi.

Then the Blessed One gave General Sīha a progressive talk, that is to say, a talk on generosity, a talk on morality, a talk on heaven; he explained the danger, degradation, and defilement of sensual pleasures and the benefit of renunciation. When the Blessed One knew that General Sīha’s mind was ready, receptive, free from hindrances, uplifted, and confident, he then expounded to him the Dhamma that is the special teaching of the Buddhas: suffering, its origin, its cessation, and the path. Just as a clean cloth, free of stains, would readily absorb dye, so too in General Sīha, as he sat there, the dust-free, stainless Dhamma-eye arose: ‘Whatever is subject to origination is subject to cessation.’ Then, having seen the Dhamma, attained the Dhamma, understood the Dhamma, plunged into the Dhamma, having crossed over doubt, having put away perplexity, having gained full confidence in the Teacher’s instruction, independent of others, General Sīha said this to the Blessed One: "May the Blessed One, together with the Saṅgha of bhikkhus, consent to a meal from me tomorrow." The Blessed One consented by remaining silent. Then General Sīha, knowing of the Blessed One's consent, rose from his seat, paid homage to the Blessed One, circumambulated him, and departed.

294. Atha kho sīho senāpati aññataraṃ purisaṃ āṇāpesi – ‘‘gaccha, bhaṇe, pavattamaṃsaṃ jānāhī’’ti. Atha kho sīho senāpati tassā rattiyā accayena paṇītaṃ khādanīyaṃ bhojanīyaṃ paṭiyādāpetvā bhagavato kālaṃ ārocāpesi – ‘‘kālo, bhante, niṭṭhitaṃ bhatta’’nti. Atha kho bhagavā pubbaṇhasamayaṃ nivāsetvā pattacīvaramādāya yena sīhassa senāpatissa nivesanaṃ tenupasaṅkami; upasaṅkamitvā paññatte āsane nisīdi saddhiṃ bhikkhusaṅghena.

294.Then General Sīha ordered a certain man, saying, "Go, good man, and find out if meat is available." Then, after the night had passed, General Sīha had fine foods, both hard and soft, prepared and announced the time to the Blessed One, saying, "Venerable sir, it is time; the meal is ready." Then the Blessed One, having dressed in the morning, taking his bowl and outer robe, went to the residence of General Sīha. Having arrived, he sat down on the prepared seat together with the Saṅgha of bhikkhus.

Tena kho pana samayena sambahulā nigaṇṭhā vesāliyaṃ rathikāya rathikaṃ siṅghāṭakena siṅghāṭakaṃ bāhā paggayha kandanti – ‘‘ajja sīhena senāpatinā thūlaṃ pasuṃ vadhitvā samaṇassa gotamassa bhattaṃ kataṃ, taṃ samaṇo gotamo jānaṃ uddissakataṃ maṃsaṃ paribhuñjati paṭiccakamma’’nti. Atha kho aññataro puriso yena sīho senāpati tenupasaṅkami, upasaṅkamitvā sīhassa senāpatissa upakaṇṇake ārocesi ‘‘yagghe, bhante, jāneyyāsi, ete sambahulā nigaṇṭhā vesāliyaṃ rathikāya rathikaṃ siṅghāṭakena siṅghāṭakaṃ bāhā paggayha kandanti – ‘ajja sīhena senāpatinā thūlaṃ pasuṃ vadhitvā samaṇassa gotamassa bhattaṃ kataṃ, taṃ samaṇo gotamo jānaṃ uddissakataṃ maṃsaṃ paribhuñjati paṭiccakamma’’’nti. ‘‘Alaṃ ayyo, dīgharattampi te āyasmantā avaṇṇakāmā buddhassa, avaṇṇakāmā dhammassa, avaṇṇakāmā saṅghassa; na ca pana te āyasmantā jiridanti taṃ bhagavantaṃ asatā tucchā musā abhūtena abbhācikkhantā; na ca mayaṃ jīvitahetupi sañcicca pāṇaṃ jīvitā voropeyyāmā’’ti. Atha kho sīho senāpati buddhappamukhaṃ bhikkhusaṅghaṃ paṇītena khādanīyena bhojanīyena sahatthā santappetvā sampavāretvā bhagavantaṃ bhuttāviṃ onītapattapāṇiṃ ekamantaṃ nisīdi. Ekamantaṃ nisinnaṃ kho sīhaṃ senāpatiṃ bhagavā dhammiyā kathāya sandassetvā samādapetvā samuttejetvā sampahaṃsetvā uṭṭhāyāsanā pakkāmi. Atha kho bhagavā etasmiṃ nidāne etasmiṃ pakaraṇe dhammiṃ kathaṃ katvā bhikkhū āmantesi – ‘‘na, bhikkhave, jā naṃ uddissakataṃ maṃsaṃ paribhuñjitabbaṃ. Yo paribhuñjeyya āpatti dukkaṭassa. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, tikoṭiparisuddhaṃ macchamaṃsaṃ – adiṭṭhaṃ assutaṃ aparisaṅkita’’nti.

At that time, several Nigaṇṭhas were wandering through the streets and crossroads of Vesālī, raising their arms and wailing: "Today, General Sīha had a large animal killed to prepare a meal for the ascetic Gotama. The ascetic Gotama knowingly eats meat prepared especially for him, meat killed on his account." Then a certain man approached General Sīha and, having approached, whispered in his ear: "Sir, you should know that several Nigaṇṭhas are wandering through the streets and crossroads of Vesālī, raising their arms and wailing: 'Today, General Sīha had a large animal killed to prepare a meal for the ascetic Gotama. The ascetic Gotama knowingly eats meat prepared especially for him, meat killed on his account.'" "Enough, good sir! For a long time, these venerable ones have been eager to disparage the Buddha, the Dhamma, and the Saṅgha. Yet these venerable ones do not desist from falsely, baselessly, untruthfully, and groundlessly accusing the Blessed One. As for us, we would not intentionally deprive a living being of life even for the sake of life itself." Then General Sīha personally served and satisfied the Saṅgha of monks headed by the Buddha with fine foods, hard and soft. When the Blessed One had finished eating and had removed his bowl, General Sīha sat down to one side. Sitting there, the Blessed One instructed, inspired, gladdened, and encouraged him with a Dhamma talk, then rose from his seat and departed. Then, on this occasion, in this connection, the Blessed One gave a Dhamma talk and addressed the monks: "Monks, meat that one knows was specially prepared for one should not be eaten. Whoever should eat it commits an offense of wrong-doing. I allow, monks, fish and meat that is pure in three respects—not seen, not heard, and not suspected."

Sīhasenāpativatthu niṭṭhitaṃ.

The story about General Sīha is concluded.

### 179. Kappiyabhūmianujānanā ^20

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv6-brahmali-pali#^20|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch5|BMC Chapter 5]] and the following cites:

> "VIN-MV6.20" file:bmc2 -queryblock
