179.Permission for Suitable Ground

295. Tena kho pana samayena vesālī subhikkhā hoti susassā sulabhapiṇḍā, sukarā uñchena paggahena yāpetuṃ. Atha kho bhagavato rahogatassa paṭisallīnassa evaṃ cetaso parivitakko udapādi – ‘‘yāni tāni mayā bhikkhūnaṃ anuññātāni dubbhikkhe dussasse dullabhapiṇḍe anto vuṭṭhaṃ anto pakkaṃ sāmaṃ pakkaṃ uggahitapaṭiggahitakaṃ tato nīhaṭaṃ purebhattaṃ paṭiggahitaṃ vanaṭṭhaṃ pokkharaṭṭhaṃ, ajjāpi nu kho tāni bhikkhū paribhuñjantī’’ti. Atha kho bhagavā sāyanhasamayaṃ paṭisallānā vuṭṭhito āyasmantaṃ ānandaṃ āmantesi – ‘‘yāni tāni, ānanda, mayā bhikkhūnaṃ anuññātāni dubbhikkhe dussasse dullabhapiṇḍe anto vuṭṭhaṃ anto pakkaṃ sāmaṃ pakkaṃ uggahitapaṭiggahitakaṃ tato nīhaṭaṃ purebhattaṃ paṭiggahitaṃ vanaṭṭhaṃ pokkharaṭṭhaṃ, ajjāpi nu kho tāni bhikkhū paribhuñjantī’’ti? ‘‘Paribhuñjanti bhagavā’’ti. Atha kho bhagavā etasmiṃ nidāne etasmiṃ pakaraṇe dhammiṃ kathaṃ katvā bhikkhū āmantesi – ‘‘yāni tāni, bhikkhave, mayā bhikkhūnaṃ anuññātāni dubbhikkhe dussasse dullabhapiṇḍe anto vuṭṭhaṃ anto pakkaṃ sāmaṃ pakkaṃ uggahitapaṭiggahitakaṃ tato nīhaṭaṃ purebhattaṃ paṭiggahitaṃ vanaṭṭhaṃ pokkharaṭṭhaṃ, tānāhaṃ ajjatagge paṭikkhipāmi. Na, bhikkhave, anto vuṭṭhaṃ anto pakkaṃ sāmaṃ pakkaṃ uggahitapaṭiggahitakaṃ paribhuñjitabbaṃ. Yo paribhuñjeyya, āpatti dukkaṭassa. Na ca, bhikkhave, tato nīhaṭaṃ purebhattaṃ paṭiggahitaṃ vanaṭṭhaṃ pokkharaṭṭhaṃ bhuttāvinā pavāritena anatirittaṃ paribhuñjitabbaṃ. Yo paribhuñjeyya, yathādhammo kāretabbo’’ti.

295.At that time, Vesālī was prosperous, with abundant crops and easily obtained almsfood. It was easy to sustain oneself by gathering scraps. Then, while the Blessed One was alone in seclusion, this thought arose in his mind: "Those allowances I have permitted for the monks—during times of scarcity, poor harvests, and difficulty in obtaining alms—such as food grown indoors, food cooked indoors, food cooked by oneself, food received by special arrangement, food brought from there, food received before the meal, food gathered in the forest, or food gathered from a lotus pond—are the monks still partaking of these now?" Then, in the evening, the Blessed One emerged from seclusion and addressed Venerable Ānanda: "Ānanda, those allowances I have permitted for the monks—during times of scarcity, poor harvests, and difficulty in obtaining alms—such as food grown indoors, food cooked indoors, food cooked by oneself, food received by special arrangement, food brought from there, food received before the meal, food gathered in the forest, or food gathered from a lotus pond—are the monks still partaking of these now?" "They are, Blessed One." Then, on this occasion, the Blessed One gave a Dhamma talk and addressed the monks: "Monks, those allowances I have permitted for you—during times of scarcity, poor harvests, and difficulty in obtaining alms—such as food grown indoors, food cooked indoors, food cooked by oneself, or food received by special arrangement—from today onward, I revoke them. Monks, you should not partake of food grown indoors, food cooked indoors, or food received by special arrangement. Whoever does so commits an offense of wrongdoing. And, monks, food brought from there, food received before the meal, food gathered in the forest, or food gathered from a lotus pond should not be partaken of by one who has finished eating and declined further food, unless it is a permissible leftover. Whoever does so should be dealt with according to the rule."

Tena kho pana samayena jānapadā manussā bahuṃ loṇampi, telampi, taṇḍulampi, khādanīyampi sakaṭesu āropetvā bahārāmakoṭṭhake sakaṭaparivaṭṭaṃ karitvā acchanti – yadā paṭipāṭiṃ labhissāma, tadā bhattaṃ karissāmāti. Mahā ca megho uggato hoti. Atha kho te manussā yenāyasmā ānando tenupasaṅkamiṃsu, upasaṅkamitvā āyasmantaṃ ānandaṃ etadavocuṃ – ‘‘idha, bhante ānanda, bahuṃ loṇampi, telampi, taṇḍulampi, khādanīyampi sakaṭesu āropitā tiṭṭhanti, mahā ca megho uggato; kathaṃ nu kho, bhante ānanda, paṭipajjitabba’’nti? Atha kho āyasmā ānando bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesi. ‘‘Tena hānanda, saṅgho paccantimaṃ vihāraṃ kappiyabhūmiṃ sammannitvā tattha vāsetu, yaṃ saṅgho ākaṅkhati vihāraṃ vā aḍḍhayogaṃ vā pāsādaṃ vā hammiyaṃ vā guhaṃ vā. Evañca pana, bhikkhave, sammannitabbā. Byattena bhikkhunā paṭibalena saṅgho ñāpetabbo –

At that time, people from the countryside had loaded much salt, oil, rice, and food onto carts. After arranging their carts in a circle in the outer monastery enclosure, they stood waiting, thinking, "When we get our turn, we’ll prepare a meal." Then a great cloud arose. Those people approached Venerable Ānanda and said, "Venerable Ānanda, much salt, oil, rice, and food have been loaded onto carts and are standing here, and a great cloud has arisen. What should be done, Venerable Ānanda?" Then Venerable Ānanda reported the matter to the Blessed One. "In that case, Ānanda, let the Saṅgha designate a monastery as permissible ground and allow them to stay there—whatever the Saṅgha desires: a monastery, a lean-to, a mansion, a dwelling with an attic, or a cave. And this is how it should be designated, monks. A monk who is competent and able should inform the Saṅgha:

‘‘Suṇātu me, bhante, saṅgho. Yadi saṅghassa pattakallaṃ, saṅgho itthannāmaṃ vihāraṃ kappiyabhūmiṃ sammanneyya, esā ñatti.

"Venerable Sir, may the Saṅgha hear me. If the Saṅgha is ready, let the Saṅgha designate the dwelling of such-and-such a name as a permissible site. This is the motion."

‘‘Suṇātu me, bhante, saṅgho. Saṅgho itthannāmaṃ vihāraṃ kappiyabhūmiṃ sammannati. Yassāyasmato khamati itthannāmassa vihārassa kappiyabhūmiyā sammuti, so tuṇhassa; yassa nakkhamati, so bhāseyya.

"Venerable sir, may the Saṅgha hear me. The Saṅgha is designating such-and-such a monastery as a permissible ground. If it is agreeable to the venerable ones to designate such-and-such a monastery as a permissible ground, let them remain silent; if it is not agreeable, let them speak."

‘‘Sammato saṅghena itthannāmo vihāro kappiyabhūmi. Khamati saṅghassa, tasmā tuṇhī, evametaṃ dhārayāmī’’ti.

"The Saṅgha has approved the monastery named such-and-such as allowable ground. It is pleasing to the Saṅgha; therefore they are silent. Thus I hold it."

Tena kho pana samayena manussā tattheva sammutiyā [sammatikāya (syā.)] kappiyabhūmiyā yāguyo pacanti, bhattāni pacanti, sūpāni sampādenti, maṃsāni koṭṭenti, kaṭṭhāni phālenti. Assosi kho bhagavā rattiyā paccūsasamayaṃ paccuṭṭhāya uccāsaddaṃ mahāsaddaṃ kākoravasaddaṃ, sutvāna āyasmantaṃ ānandaṃ āmantesi – ‘‘kiṃ nu kho so, ānanda, uccāsaddo mahāsaddo kākoravasaddo’’ti? ‘‘Etarahi, bhante, manussā tattheva sammutiyā kappiyabhūmiyā yāguyo pacanti, bhattāni pacanti, sūpāni sampādenti, maṃsāni koṭṭenti, kaṭṭhāni phālenti. So eso, bhagavā, uccāsaddo mahāsaddo kākoravasaddo’’ti. Atha kho bhagavā etasmiṃ nidāne etasmiṃ pakaraṇe dhammiṃ kathaṃ katvā bhikkhū āmantesi – ‘‘na, bhikkhave, sammuti [sammatikā (syā.)] kappiyabhūmi paribhuñjitabbā. Yo paribhuñjeyya, āpatti dukkaṭassa. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, tisso kappiyabhūmiyo – ussāvanantikaṃ gonisādikaṃ gahapati’’nti.

At that time, people were cooking porridge, preparing meals, making soups, pounding meat, and splitting firewood right there in the designated permissible area. The Blessed One heard a loud noise, a great noise, the clamorous noise of crows early in the morning after rising. Hearing this, he addressed Venerable Ānanda: "Ānanda, what is this loud noise, great noise, the clamorous noise of crows?" "Venerable sir, people are now cooking porridge, preparing meals, making soups, pounding meat, and splitting firewood right there in the designated permissible area. That is why, Blessed One, there is this loud noise, great noise, the clamorous noise of crows." Then the Blessed One, on this occasion, in this connection, having given a Dhamma talk, addressed the monks: "Monks, a designated permissible area should not be used. Whoever uses it commits an offense of wrong conduct. I allow, monks, three types of permissible areas: an area designated by proclamation, an unenclosed area, and a householder's residence."

Tena kho pana samayena āyasmā yasojo gilāno hoti. Tassatthāya bhesajjāni āhariyanti. Tāni bhikkhū bahi vāsenti. Ukkapiṇḍikāpi khādanti, corāpi haranti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, sammutiṃ kappiyabhūmiṃ paribhuñjituṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, catasso kappiyabhūmiyo – ussāvanantikaṃ gonisādikaṃ gahapatiṃ sammutinti.

At that time, moreover, Venerable Yasojā was ill. Medicines were brought for him. The monks stored them outside. Rats also ate them, and thieves stole them. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. "I allow, monks, to make a designation to use a permissible area. I allow, monks, four kinds of permissible areas: an area designated by proclamation, an unenclosed area, a householder's residence, and an area designated by formal resolution."

Kappiyabhūmianujānanā niṭṭhitā.

The authorization of suitable grounds is concluded.

Sīhabhāṇavāro niṭṭhito catuttho.

The fourth chapter, "The Lion's Roar," is concluded.

### 180. Meṇḍakagahapativatthu ^21

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv6-brahmali-pali#^21|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch5|BMC Chapter 5]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-MV6.21" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


180.The Story of the Householder Meṇḍaka

296. Tena kho pana samayena bhaddiyanagare meṇḍako gahapati paṭivasati. Tassa evarūpo iddhānubhāvo hoti – sīsaṃ nahāyitvā dhaññāgāraṃ sammajjāpetvā bahidvāre nisīdati, antalikkhā dhaññassa dhārā opatitvā dhaññāgāraṃ pūreti. Bhariyāya evarūpo iddhānubhāvo hoti – ekaṃyeva āḷhakathālikaṃ upanisīditvā ekañca sūpabhiñjanakaṃ [sūpabhiñjarakaṃ (sī.)] dāsakammakaraporisaṃ bhattena parivisati, na tāva taṃ khiyyati [khīyati (sī. syā.)] yāva sā na vuṭṭhāti. Puttassa evarūpo iddhānubhāvo hoti – ekaṃyeva sahassathavikaṃ gahetvā dāsakammakaraporisassa chamāsikaṃ vetanaṃ deti, na tāva taṃ khiyyati yāvassa hatthagatā. Suṇisāya evarūpo iddhānubhāvo hoti – ekaṃyeva catudoṇikaṃ piṭakaṃ upanisīditvā dāsakammakaraporisassa chamāsikaṃ bhattaṃ deti, na tāva taṃ khiyyati yāva sā na vuṭṭhāti. Dāsassa evarūpo iddhānubhāvo hoti – ekena naṅgalena kasantassa satta sītāyo gacchanti.

296.Now at that time, the householder Meṇḍaka resided in the city of Bhaddiya. He possessed such supernormal power: after washing his head and having the granary swept, he would sit outside the door, and a stream of grain would fall from the sky, filling the granary. His wife possessed such supernormal power: sitting with a single āḷhaka-measure pot and a single pot of curry and relish, she would serve food to the servants and workers, and it would not diminish until she rose. Their son possessed such supernormal power: taking a single purse containing a thousand (coins), he would give six months’ wages to the servants and workers, and it would not diminish as long as it remained in his hand. Their daughter-in-law possessed such supernormal power: sitting with a single four-doṇa basket, she would give six months’ rations to the servants and workers, and it would not diminish until she rose. Their slave possessed such supernormal power: when plowing with a single plow, seven furrows would be made.

Assosi kho rājā māgadho seniyo bimbisāro – ‘‘amhākaṃ kira vijite bhaddiyanagare meṇḍako gahapati paṭivasati. Tassa evarūpo iddhānubhāvo – sīsaṃ nahāyitvā dhaññāgāraṃ sammajjāpetvā bahidvāre nisīdati, antalikkhā dhaññassa dhārā opatitvā dhaññāgāraṃ pūreti. Bhariyāya evarūpo iddhānubhāvo – ekaṃyeva āḷhakathālikaṃ upanisīditvā ekañca sūpabhiñjanakaṃ dāsakammakaraporisaṃ bhattena parivisati, na tāva taṃ khiyyati yāva sā na vuṭṭhāti. Puttassa evarūpo iddhānubhāvo – ekaṃyeva sahassathavikaṃ gahetvā dāsakammakaraporisassa chamāsikaṃ vetanaṃ deti, na tāva taṃ khiyyati yāvassa hatthagatā. Suṇisāya evarūpo iddhānubhāvo – ekaṃyeva catudoṇikaṃ piṭakaṃ upanisīditvā dāsakammakaraporisassa chamāsikaṃ bhattaṃ deti, na tāva taṃ khiyyati yāva sā na vuṭṭhāti. Dāsassa evarūpo iddhānubhāvo – ekena naṅgalena kasantassa satta sītāyo gacchantī’’ti. Atha kho rājā māgadho seniyo bimbisāro aññataraṃ sabbatthakaṃ mahāmattaṃ āmantesi – ‘‘amhākaṃ kira, bhaṇe, vijite bhaddiyanagare meṇḍako gahapati paṭivasati. Tassa evarūpo iddhānubhāvo – sīsaṃ nahāyitvā dhaññāgāraṃ sammajjāpetvā bahidvāre nisīdati, antalikkhā dhaññassa dhārā opatitvā dhaññāgāraṃ pūreti. Bhariyāya…pe… puttassa… suṇisāya… dāsassa evarūpo iddhānubhāvo, ekena naṅgalena kasantassa satta sītāyo gacchantīti. Gaccha, bhaṇe, jānāhi. Yathā mayā sāmaṃ diṭṭho, evaṃ tava diṭṭho bhavissatī’’ti.

King Seniya Bimbisāra of Magadha heard: “It is said that in our territory, in the city of Bhaddiya, lives the householder Meṇḍaka. He possesses such supernormal power—after washing his head and having the granary swept, he sits outside the door, and a stream of grain falls from the sky, filling the granary. His wife has such supernormal power—sitting down with just one āḷhaka-measure pot and one pot of curry and relish, she serves the servants and workers with food, and it does not run out until she gets up. His son has such supernormal power—taking just one purse containing a thousand (coins), he gives six months’ wages to the servants and workers, and it does not run out as long as it remains in his hand. His daughter-in-law has such supernormal power—sitting down with just one four-doṇa basket, she gives six months’ rations to the servants and workers, and it does not run out until she gets up. His slave has such supernormal power—plowing with one plow, he makes seven furrows at once.” Then King Seniya Bimbisāra of Magadha addressed a certain general minister: “Sir, it is said that in our territory, in the city of Bhaddiya, lives the householder Meṇḍaka. He possesses such supernormal power—after washing his head… his wife… his son… his daughter-in-law… his slave has such supernormal power, and when plowing with one plow, he makes seven furrows at once. Go, sir, and find out. What I have seen for myself, you will see.”

297. Evaṃ, devāti kho so mahāmatto rañño māgadhassa seniyassa bimbisārassa paṭissuṇitvā caturaṅginiyā senāya yena bhaddiyaṃ tena pāyāsi. Anupubbena yena bhaddiyaṃ yena meṇḍako gahapati tenupasaṅkami; upasaṅkamitvā meṇḍakaṃ gahapatiṃ etadavoca – ‘‘ahañhi, gahapati, raññā āṇatto ‘amhākaṃ kira, bhaṇe, vijite bhaddiyanagare meṇḍako gahapati paṭivasati, tassa evarūpo iddhānubhāvo, sīsaṃ nahāyitvā…pe… bhariyāya… puttassa… suṇisāya… dāsassa evarūpo iddhānubhāvo, ekena naṅgalena kasantassa satta sītāyo gacchantī’ti, gaccha, bhaṇe, jānāhi. Yathā mayā sāmaṃ diṭṭho, evaṃ tava diṭṭho bhavissatī’ti. Passāma te, gahapati, iddhānubhāva’’nti. Atha kho meṇḍako gahapati sīsaṃ nahāyitvā dhaññāgāraṃ sammajjāpetvā bahidvāre nisīdi, antalikkhā dhaññassa dhārā opatitvā dhaññāgāraṃ pūresi. ‘‘Diṭṭho te, gahapati, iddhānubhāvo. Bhariyāya te iddhānubhāvaṃ passissāmā’’ti. Atha kho meṇḍako gahapati bhariyaṃ āṇāpesi – ‘‘tena hi caturaṅginiṃ senaṃ bhattena parivisā’’ti. Atha kho meṇḍakassa gahapatissa bhariyā ekaṃyeva āḷhakathālikaṃ upanisīditvā ekañca sūpabhiñjanakaṃ caturaṅginiṃ senaṃ bhattena parivisi, na tāva taṃ khiyyati, yāva sā na vuṭṭhāti. ‘‘Diṭṭho te, gahapati, bhariyāyapi iddhānubhāvo. Puttassa te iddhānubhāvaṃ passissāmā’’ti. Atha kho meṇḍako gahapati puttaṃ āṇāpesi – ‘‘tena hi caturaṅginiyā senāya chamāsikaṃ vetanaṃ dehī’’ti. Atha kho meṇḍakassa gahapatissa putto ekaṃyeva sahassathavikaṃ gahetvā caturaṅginiyā senāya chamāsikaṃ vetanaṃ adāsi, na tāva taṃ khiyyati, yāvassa hatthagatā. ‘‘Diṭṭho te, gahapati, puttassapi iddhānubhāvo. Suṇisāya te iddhānubhāvaṃ passissāmā’’ti. Atha kho meṇḍako gahapati suṇisaṃ āṇāpesi – ‘‘tena hi caturaṅginiyā senāya chamāsikaṃ bhattaṃ dehī’’ti. Atha kho meṇḍakassa gahapatissa suṇisā ekaṃyeva catudoṇikaṃ piṭakaṃ upanisīditvā caturaṅginiyā senāya chamāsikaṃ bhattaṃ adāsi, na tāva taṃ khiyyati yāva sā na vuṭṭhāti. ‘‘Diṭṭho te, gahapati, suṇisāyapi iddhānubhāvo. Dāsassa te iddhānubhāvaṃ passissāmā’’ti. ‘‘Mayhaṃ kho, sāmi, dāsassa iddhānubhāvo khette passitabbo’’ti. ‘‘Alaṃ, gahapati, diṭṭho te dāsassapi iddhānubhāvo’’ti. Atha kho so mahāmatto caturaṅginiyā senāya punadeva rājagahaṃ paccāgañchi. Yena rājā māgadho seniyo bimbisāro tenupasaṅkami; upasaṅkamitvā rañño māgadhassa seniyassa bimbisārassa etamatthaṃ ārocesi.

297.“Very well, lord,” replied the general minister to King Seniya Bimbisāra of Magadha. Then, with the fourfold army, he set out for Bhaddiya. Gradually, he reached Bhaddiya and approached the householder Meṇḍaka. Upon arrival, he said to Meṇḍaka the householder: “Householder, I have been commanded by the king: ‘It is said, good sir, that in our realm, in the city of Bhaddiya, dwells the householder Meṇḍaka, who possesses such supernormal power—after he washes his head… his wife… his son… his daughter-in-law… his slave possesses such supernormal power, and when he plows with a single plow, seven furrows are made simultaneously.’ Go, good sir, and find out. As I have seen it myself, so you will see it too. Let us witness your supernormal power, householder.” Then Meṇḍaka the householder washed his head, had the granary swept clean, and sat outside the door. A shower of grain fell from the sky and filled the granary. “We have seen your supernormal power, householder. Now let us see your wife’s supernormal power.” Meṇḍaka then instructed his wife: “Well then, serve the fourfold army with food.” His wife sat down with a single āḷhaka-measure pot and a single pot of curry and relish, and served the fourfold army with food. It did not diminish until she rose from her seat. “We have seen your wife’s supernormal power, householder. Now let us see your son’s supernormal power.” Meṇḍaka instructed his son: “Well then, give the fourfold army six months’ wages.” His son took a single purse containing a thousand (coins) and gave the fourfold army six months’ wages. It did not diminish as long as it remained in his hand. “We have seen your son’s supernormal power, householder. Now let us see your daughter-in-law’s supernormal power.” Meṇḍaka instructed his daughter-in-law: “Well then, give the fourfold army six months’ rations.” His daughter-in-law sat down with a single four-doṇa basket and gave the fourfold army six months’ rations. It did not diminish until she rose from her seat. “We have seen your daughter-in-law’s supernormal power, householder. Now let us see your slave’s supernormal power.” “My lord, the slave’s supernormal power must be seen in the field.” “Enough, householder, we have seen your slave’s supernormal power too.” Then the general minister returned to Rājagaha with the fourfold army. He approached King Seniya Bimbisāra of Magadha and reported the matter to him.

298. Atha kho bhagavā vesāliyaṃ yathābhirantaṃ viharitvā yena bhaddiyaṃ tena cārikaṃ pakkāmi mahatā bhikkhusaṅghena saddhiṃ aḍḍhatelasehi bhikkhusatehi. Atha kho bhagavā anupubbena cārikaṃ caramāno yena bhaddiyaṃ tadavasari. Tatra sudaṃ bhagavā bhaddiye viharati jātiyā vane. Assosi kho meṇḍako gahapati – ‘‘samaṇo khalu bho gotamo sakyaputto sakyakulā pabbajito bhaddiyaṃ anuppatto bhaddiye viharati jātiyā vane. Taṃ kho pana bhagavantaṃ gotamaṃ evaṃ kalyāṇo kittisaddo abbhuggato – ‘itipi so bhagavā arahaṃ sammāsambuddho vijjācaraṇasampanno sugato lokavidū anuttaro purisadammasārathi satthā devamanussānaṃ buddho bhagavā’ [bhagavāti (ka.)]. So imaṃ lokaṃ sadevakaṃ samārakaṃ sabrahmakaṃ sassamaṇabrāhmaṇiṃ pajaṃ sadevamanussaṃ sayaṃ abhiññā sacchikatvā pavedeti. So dhammaṃ deseti ādikalyāṇaṃ majjhekalyāṇaṃ pariyosānakalyāṇaṃ sātthaṃ sabyañjanaṃ kevalaparipuṇṇaṃ parisuddhaṃ brahmacariyaṃ pakāseti. Sādhu kho pana tathārūpānaṃ arahataṃ dassanaṃ hotī’’ti. Atha kho meṇḍako gahapati bhadrāni bhadrāni yānāni yojāpetvā bhadraṃ bhadraṃ yānaṃ abhiruhitvā bhadrehi bhadrehi yānehi bhaddiyā niyyāsi bhagavantaṃ dassanāya. Addasaṃsu kho sambahulā titthiyā meṇḍakaṃ gahapatiṃ dūratova āgacchantaṃ, disvāna meṇḍakaṃ gahapatiṃ etadavocuṃ – ‘‘kahaṃ tvaṃ, gahapati, gacchasī’’ti? ‘‘Gacchāmahaṃ, bhante, bhagavantaṃ [idaṃ padaṃ sī. syā. potthakesu natthi] samaṇaṃ gotamaṃ dassanāyā’’ti. ‘‘Kiṃ pana tvaṃ, gahapati, kiriyavādo samāno akiriyavādaṃ samaṇaṃ gotamaṃ dassanāya upasaṅkamissasi? Samaṇo hi, gahapati, gotamo akiriyavādo akiriyāya dhammaṃ deseti, tena ca sāvake vinetī’’ti. Atha kho meṇḍakassa gahapatissa etadahosi – ‘‘nissaṃsayaṃ, kho so bhagavā arahaṃ sammāsambuddho bhavissati, yathayime titthiyā usūyantī’’ti. Yāvatikā yānassa bhūmi, yānena gantvā yānā paccorohitvā pattikova yena bhagavā tenupasaṅkami, upasaṅkamitvā bhagavantaṃ abhivādetvā ekamantaṃ nisīdi. Ekamantaṃ nisinnassa kho meṇḍakassa gahapatissa bhagavā anupubbiṃ kathaṃ kathesi, seyyathidaṃ – dānakathaṃ…pe… aparappaccayo satthusāsane bhagavantaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘abhikkantaṃ, bhante…pe… upāsakaṃ maṃ bhagavā dhāretu ajjatagge pāṇupetaṃ saraṇaṃ gataṃ. Adhivāsetu ca me, bhante, bhagavā svātanāya bhattaṃ saddhiṃ bhikkhusaṅghenā’’ti. Adhivāsesi bhagavā tuṇhībhāvena. Atha kho meṇḍako gahapati bhagavato adhivāsanaṃ viditvā uṭṭhāyāsanā bhagavantaṃ abhivādetvā padakkhiṇaṃ katvā pakkāmi.

298.Then the Blessed One, having stayed in Vesālī as long as he pleased, set out on a journey to Bhaddiya with a large company of bhikkhus, numbering twelve hundred and fifty. Traveling in stages, the Blessed One eventually arrived at Bhaddiya. There he stayed in the Jātiyā Grove. The householder Meṇḍaka heard: "Indeed, the ascetic Gotama, the Sakyan son who has gone forth from the Sakyan clan, has arrived at Bhaddiya and is staying in the Jātiyā Grove. About that Blessed One Gotama, such a glorious report has spread: 'For he is the Blessed One, the Arahant, the Perfectly Self-Enlightened One, accomplished in true knowledge and conduct, the Fortunate One, knower of the world, the unsurpassed leader of persons to be tamed, teacher of gods and humans, the Enlightened One, the Blessed One.' He has realized with direct knowledge this world with its gods, Māras, and Brahmās, this generation with its ascetics and brahmins, its devas and humans, and he makes it known to others. He teaches the Dhamma that is good in the beginning, good in the middle, and good in the end, with its meaning and phrasing; and he reveals the perfectly complete and pure holy life. It is indeed good to see such Arahants." Then the householder Meṇḍaka had fine carriages harnessed, mounted a fine carriage, and with his fine carriages, he set out from Bhaddiya to see the Blessed One. Several ascetics from other sects saw Meṇḍaka the householder coming from a distance and said to him: "Where are you going, householder?" "I am going, sirs, to see the ascetic Gotama." "But householder, why would you, a proponent of action, go to see the ascetic Gotama, who teaches non-action? The ascetic Gotama teaches the doctrine of non-action and trains his disciples accordingly." Then it occurred to Meṇḍaka the householder: "Surely, the Blessed One must be an Arahant, a Perfectly Self-Enlightened One, since these ascetics are envious of him." He went as far as the carriage could go, then dismounted from the carriage and approached the Blessed One on foot. Having approached, he paid homage to the Blessed One and sat down to one side. The Blessed One gave him a progressive talk—on generosity, on virtue, on the heavens, on the danger, vanity, and defilement of sensual pleasures, and on the benefits of renunciation. When the Blessed One knew that Meṇḍaka’s mind was ready, pliable, free from hindrances, joyful, and confident, he then revealed the teaching unique to the Buddhas: suffering, its origin, its cessation, and the path. Just as a clean cloth would take dye evenly, so too, while Meṇḍaka the householder sat there, the dust-free, stainless vision of the Dhamma arose in him: "All that is subject to arising is subject to cessation." Having seen the Dhamma, attained the Dhamma, understood the Dhamma, penetrated the Dhamma, overcome doubt, dispelled uncertainty, gained confidence, and become independent of others in the Teacher’s dispensation, he said to the Blessed One: "Excellent, venerable sir!... From today, may the Blessed One remember me as a lay follower who has gone for refuge for life. And, venerable sir, may the Blessed One accept tomorrow’s meal from me together with the Sangha of bhikkhus." The Blessed One consented by silence. Then Meṇḍaka the householder, understanding the Blessed One’s consent, rose from his seat, paid homage to the Blessed One, circumambulated him, and departed.

Atha kho meṇḍako gahapati tassā rattiyā accayena paṇītaṃ khādanīyaṃ bhojanīyaṃ paṭiyādāpetvā bhagavato kālaṃ ārocāpesi – ‘‘kālo, bhante, niṭṭhitaṃ bhatta’’nti. Atha kho bhagavā pubbaṇhasamayaṃ nivāsetvā pattacīvaramādāya yena meṇḍakassa gahapatissa nivesanaṃ tenupasaṅkami; upasaṅkamitvā paññatte āsane nisīdi saddhiṃ bhikkhusaṅghena. Atha kho meṇḍakassa gahapatissa bhariyā ca putto ca suṇisā ca dāso ca yena bhagavā tenupasaṅkamiṃsu, upasaṅkamitvā bhagavantaṃ abhivādetvā ekamantaṃ nisīdiṃsu. Tesaṃ bhagavā anupubbiṃ kathaṃ kathesi, seyyathidaṃ – dānakathaṃ…pe… aparappaccayā satthusāsane bhagavantaṃ etadavocuṃ – ‘‘abhikkantaṃ, bhante…pe… ete mayaṃ, bhante, bhagavantaṃ saraṇaṃ gacchāma dhammañca bhikkhusaṅghañca. Upāsake no bhagavā dhāretu ajjatagge pāṇupete saraṇaṃ gate’’ti. Atha kho meṇḍako gahapati buddhappamukhaṃ bhikkhusaṅghaṃ paṇītena khādanīyena bhojanīyena sahatthā santappetvā sampavāretvā bhagavantaṃ bhuttāviṃ onītapattapāṇiṃ ekamantaṃ nisīdi. Ekamantaṃ nisinno kho meṇḍako gahapati bhagavantaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘yāva, bhante, bhagavā bhaddiye viharati tāva ahaṃ buddhappamukhassa bhikkhusaṅghassa dhuvabhattenā’’ti. Atha kho bhagavā meṇḍakaṃ gahapatiṃ dhammiyā kathāya sandassetvā samādapetvā samuttejetvā sampahaṃsetvā uṭṭhāyāsanā pakkāmi.

Then, when the night had passed, the householder Meṇḍaka had fine food prepared and announced the time to the Blessed One: "It is time, venerable sir, the meal is ready." Then the Blessed One, having dressed in the morning, took his bowl and robe and went to the residence of the householder Meṇḍaka. Having arrived, he sat down on the prepared seat together with the community of monks. Then the wife, son, daughter-in-law, and servant of the householder Meṇḍaka approached the Blessed One. Having approached, they paid homage to the Blessed One and sat down to one side. The Blessed One gave them a progressive talk, that is, on generosity... having become independent of others in the Teacher's dispensation, they said to the Blessed One: "Excellent, venerable sir... We go for refuge to the Blessed One, to the Dhamma, and to the Sangha of monks. May the Blessed One remember us as lay followers who have gone for refuge from this day forward, for as long as life lasts." Then the householder Meṇḍaka personally served and satisfied the community of monks headed by the Buddha with fine food. When the Blessed One had finished eating and had put away his bowl, the householder Meṇḍaka sat down to one side. Sitting to one side, the householder Meṇḍaka said to the Blessed One: "Venerable sir, as long as the Blessed One remains in Bhaddiya, I will provide a constant meal for the community of monks headed by the Buddha." Then the Blessed One, having instructed, inspired, encouraged, and gladdened the householder Meṇḍaka with a Dhamma talk, rose from his seat and departed.

Meṇḍakagahapativattha niṭṭhitaṃ.

The story of the householder Meṇḍaka is concluded.

### 181. Pañcagorasādianujānanā ^22

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv6-brahmali-pali#^22|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch5|BMC Chapter 5]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-MV6.22" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


181.The Allowance of the Five Kinds of Milk Products

299. Atha kho bhagavā bhaddiye yathābhirantaṃ viharitvā meṇḍakaṃ gahapatiṃ anāpucchā yena aṅguttarāpo tena cārikaṃ pakkāmi mahatā bhikkhusaṅghena saddhiṃ aḍḍhatelasehi bhikkhusatehi. Assosi kho meṇḍako gahapati – ‘‘bhagavā kira yena aṅguttarāpo tena cārikaṃ pakkanto mahatā bhikkhusaṅghena saddhiṃ aḍḍhatelasehi bhikkhusatehī’’ti. Atha kho meṇḍako gahapati dāse ca kammakare ca āṇāpesi – ‘‘tena hi, bhaṇe, bahuṃ loṇampi, telampi, taṇḍulampi, khādanīyampi sakaṭesu āropetvā āgacchatha, aḍḍhatelasāni ca gopālakasatāni aḍḍhatelasāni ca dhenusatāni ādāya āgacchantu, yattha bhagavantaṃ passissāma tattha taruṇena [dhāruṇhena (sī. syā.)] khīrena bhojessāmā’’ti. Atha kho meṇḍako gahapati bhagavantaṃ antarāmagge kantāre sambhāvesi. Atha kho meṇḍako gahapati yena bhagavā tenupasaṅkami; upasaṅkamitvā bhagavantaṃ abhivādetvā ekamantaṃ aṭṭhāsi. Ekamantaṃ ṭhito kho meṇḍako gahapati bhagavantaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘adhivāsetu me, bhante, bhagavā svātanāya bhattaṃ saddhiṃ bhikkhusaṅghenā’’ti. Adhivāsesi bhagavā tuṇhībhāvena. Atha kho meṇḍako gahapati bhagavato adhivāsanaṃ viditvā bhagavantaṃ abhivādetvā padakkhiṇaṃ katvā pakkāmi.

299.Then the Blessed One, having stayed at Bhaddiya as long as he pleased, set out for Anguttarāpa without taking leave of the householder Meṇḍaka, accompanied by a large Sangha of monks, one thousand two hundred and fifty in number. The householder Meṇḍaka heard: "The Blessed One, it seems, has set out for Anguttarāpa accompanied by a large Sangha of monks, one thousand two hundred and fifty in number." Then the householder Meṇḍaka ordered his male and female slaves and workers: "Come now, good sirs, load much salt, oil, rice, and foodstuffs onto carts and come. And let one thousand two hundred and fifty cowherds and one thousand two hundred and fifty milch cows come, taking them with you. Wherever we see the Blessed One, there we will offer a meal with fresh milk." Then the householder Meṇḍaka encountered the Blessed One along the road in a desolate area. Then the householder Meṇḍaka approached the Blessed One, paid homage to him, and stood to one side. Standing to one side, the householder Meṇḍaka said to the Blessed One: "Venerable sir, may the Blessed One together with the Sangha of monks accept my meal for tomorrow." The Blessed One consented by remaining silent. Then the householder Meṇḍaka, knowing of the Blessed One's consent, paid homage to him, circumambulated him, and departed.

Atha kho meṇḍako gahapati tassā rattiyā accayena paṇītaṃ khādanīyaṃ bhojanīyaṃ paṭiyādāpetvā bhagavato kālaṃ ārocāpesi – ‘‘kālo, bhante, niṭṭhitaṃ bhatta’’nti. Atha kho bhagavā pubbaṇhasamayaṃ nivāsetvā pattacīvaramādāya yena meṇḍakassa gahapatissa parivesanā tenupasaṅkami; upasaṅkamitvā paññatte āsane nisīdi saddhiṃ bhikkhusaṅghena. Atha kho meṇḍako gahapati aḍḍhatelasāni gopālakasatāni āṇāpesi – ‘‘tenahi, bhaṇe, ekamekaṃ dhenuṃ gahetvā ekamekassa bhikkhuno upatiṭṭhatha taruṇena khīrena bhojessāmā’’ti. Atha kho meṇḍako gahapati buddhappamukhaṃ bhikkhusaṅghaṃ paṇītena khādanīyena bhojanīyena sahatthā santappesi sampavāresi, taruṇena ca khīrena. Bhikkhū kukkuccāyantā khīraṃ na paṭiggaṇhanti. Paṭiggaṇhatha, bhikkhave, paribhuñjathāti. Atha kho meṇḍako gahapati buddhappamukhaṃ bhikkhusaṅghaṃ paṇītena khādanīyena bhojanīyena sahatthā santappetvā sampavāretvā taruṇena ca khīrena bhagavantaṃ bhuttāviṃ onītapattapāṇiṃ ekamantaṃ nisīdi. Ekamantaṃ nisinno kho meṇḍako gahapati bhagavantaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘santi, bhante, maggā kantārā, appodakā appabhakkhā, na sukarā apātheyyena gantuṃ. Sādhu, bhante, bhagavā bhikkhūnaṃ pātheyyaṃ anujānātū’’ti. Atha kho bhagavā meṇḍakaṃ gahapatiṃ dhammiyā kathāya sandassetvā samādapetvā samuttejetvā sampahaṃsetvā uṭṭhāyāsanā pakkāmi. Atha kho bhagavā etasmiṃ nidāne etasmiṃ pakaraṇe dhammiṃ kathaṃ katvā bhikkhū āmantesi – ‘‘anujānāmi, bhikkhave, pañca gorase – khīraṃ, dadhiṃ, takkaṃ, navanītaṃ, sappiṃ. Santi, bhikkhave, maggā kantārā appodakā appabhakkhā, na sukarā apātheyyena gantuṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, pātheyyaṃ pariyesituṃ taṇḍulo taṇḍulatthikena, muggo muggatthikena, māso māsatthikena, loṇaṃ loṇatthikena, guḷo guḷatthikena, telaṃ telatthikena, sappi sappitthikena. Santi, bhikkhave, manussā, saddhā pasannā, te kappiyakārakānaṃ hatthe hiraññaṃ upanikkhipanti – ‘iminā ayyassa yaṃ kappiyaṃ taṃ dethā’ti. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, yaṃ tato kappiyaṃ taṃ sādituṃ; na tvevāhaṃ, bhikkhave, kenaci pariyāyena jātarūparajataṃ sāditabbaṃ pariyesitabbanti vadāmī’’ti.

Then, when the night had passed, the householder Meṇḍaka had fine food, both hard and soft, prepared and announced the time to the Blessed One: “It is time, Venerable Sir, the meal is ready.” Then, in the morning, the Blessed One dressed, took his bowl and robe, and went to the place where the meal was being served at the householder Meṇḍaka’s residence. Having arrived, he sat down on the prepared seat together with the community of monks. Then the householder Meṇḍaka instructed twelve hundred and fifty cowherds: “Come now, lads, take one cow each and attend to each monk with fresh milk—we shall serve them.” Then the householder Meṇḍaka personally served and satisfied the community of monks headed by the Buddha with fine food, both hard and soft, and fresh milk. The monks, being scrupulous, did not accept the milk. [The Blessed One said:] “Accept it, monks, and consume it.” Then, after serving and satisfying the community of monks headed by the Buddha with fine food, both hard and soft, and fresh milk, and when the Blessed One had finished his meal and withdrawn his hand from the bowl, the householder Meṇḍaka sat down to one side. Sitting to one side, he said to the Blessed One: “Venerable Sir, there are roads through wildernesses with little water and little food, where it is not easy to travel without provisions. It would be good, Venerable Sir, if the Blessed One would allow provisions for the monks.” Then the Blessed One instructed, encouraged, inspired, and gladdened the householder Meṇḍaka with a Dhamma talk, after which he rose from his seat and departed. Then, on this occasion, the Blessed One gave a Dhamma talk and addressed the monks: “Monks, I allow five products of the cow: milk, curd, buttermilk, butter, and ghee. There are, monks, roads through wildernesses with little water and little food, where it is not easy to travel without provisions. I allow you to seek provisions: rice for one who needs rice, mung beans for one who needs mung beans, beans for one who needs beans, salt for one who needs salt, sugar for one who needs sugar, oil for one who needs oil, and ghee for one who needs ghee. There are, monks, faithful and devoted people who place money in the hands of those who are suitable to handle it, saying, ‘With this, give the venerable what is allowable.’ I allow you, monks, to make use of what is allowable from that. However, I do not say that gold or silver should be sought or accepted in any way.”

Pañcagorasādianujānanā niṭṭhitā.

The allowance regarding the five products of the cow is completed.

### 182. Keṇiyajaṭilavatthu ^23

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv6-brahmali-pali#^23|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch5|BMC Chapter 5]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-MV6.23" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


182.The Story of the Ascetic Keṇiya with Matted Hair

300. [ma. ni. 2.396 ādayo; su. ni. selasuttampi passitabbaṃ] Atha kho bhagavā anupubbena cārikaṃ caramāno yena āpaṇaṃ tadavasari. Assosi kho keṇiyo jaṭilo – ‘‘samaṇo khalu bho gotamo sakyaputto sakyakulā pabbajito āpaṇaṃ anuppatto, taṃ kho pana bhavantaṃ gotamaṃ evaṃ kalyāṇo kittisaddo abbhuggato…pe… sādhu kho pana tathārūpānaṃ arahataṃ dassanaṃ hotī’’ti. Atha kho keṇiyassa jaṭilassa etadahosi – ‘‘kiṃ nu kho ahaṃ samaṇassa gotamassa harāpeyya’’nti. Atha kho keṇiyassa jaṭilassa etadahosi – ‘‘yepi kho te brāhmaṇānaṃ [ayaṃ pāṭho dī. ni. 1.285, 526, 536; ma. ni. 2.427; a. ni. 5.191-192 ādayo] pubbakā isayo mantānaṃ kattāro mantānaṃ pavattāro, yesamidaṃ etarahi brāhmaṇā porāṇaṃ mantapadaṃ gītaṃ pavuttaṃ samihitaṃ, tadanugāyanti tadanubhāsanti, bhāsitamanubhāsanti, vācitamanuvācenti, seyyathidaṃ – aṭṭhako vāmako vāmadevo vessāmitto yamataggi [yamadaggi (ka.)] aṅgīraso bhāradvājo vāseṭṭho kassapo bhagu [ayaṃ pāṭho dī. ni. 1.285, 526, 536; ma. ni. 2.427; a. ni. 5.191-192 ādayo], rattūparatā viratā vikālabhojanā, te evarūpāni pānāni sādiyiṃsu. Samaṇopi gotamo rattūparato virato vikālabhojanā, arahati samaṇopi gotamo evarūpāni pānāni sādiyitu’’nti pahūtaṃ pānaṃ paṭiyādāpetvā kājehi gāhāpetvā yena bhagavā tenupasaṅkami; upasaṅkamitvā bhagavatā saddhiṃ sammodi; sammodanīyaṃ kathaṃ sāraṇīyaṃ vītisāretvā ekamantaṃ aṭṭhāsi. Ekamantaṃ ṭhito kho keṇiyo jaṭilo bhagavantaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘paṭiggaṇhātu me bhavaṃ gotamo pāna’’nti. Tena hi, keṇiya, bhikkhūnaṃ dehīti. Atha kho keṇiyo jaṭilo bhikkhūnaṃ deti. Bhikkhū kukkuccāyantā na paṭiggaṇhanti. Paṭiggaṇhatha, bhikkhave, paribhuñjathāti. Atha kho keṇiyo jaṭilo buddhappamukhaṃ bhikkhusaṅghaṃ pahūtehi pānehi sahatthā santappetvā sampavāretvā bhagavantaṃ dhotahatthaṃ onītapattapāṇiṃ ekamantaṃ nisīdi. Ekamantaṃ nisinnaṃ kho keṇiyaṃ jaṭilaṃ bhagavā dhammiyā kathāya sandassesi samādapesi samuttejesi sampahaṃsesi. Atha kho keṇiyo jaṭilo bhagavatā dhammiyā kathāya sandassito samādapito samuttejito sampahaṃsito bhagavantaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘adhivāsetu me bhavaṃ gotamo svātanāya bhattaṃ saddhiṃ bhikkhusaṅghenā’’ti. Mahā kho, keṇiya, bhikkhusaṅgho aḍḍhatelasāni bhikkhusatāni, tvañca brāhmaṇesu abhippasannoti. Dutiyampi kho keṇiyo jaṭilo bhagavantaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘kiñcāpi kho, bho gotama, mahā bhikkhusaṅgho aḍḍhatelasāni bhikkhusatāni, ahañca brāhmaṇesu abhippasanno, adhivāsetu me bhavaṃ gotamo svātanāya bhattaṃ saddhiṃ bhikkhusaṅghenā’’ti. Mahā kho, keṇiya, bhikkhusaṅgho aḍḍhatelasāni bhikkhusatāni, tvañca brāhmaṇesu abhippasannoti. Tatiyampi kho keṇiyo jaṭilo bhagavantaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘kiñcāpi kho, bho gotama, mahā bhikkhusaṅgho aḍḍhatelasāni bhikkhusatāni, ahañca brāhmaṇesu abhippasanno, adhivāsetu bhavaṃ gotamo svātanāya bhattaṃ saddhiṃ bhikkhusaṅghenā’’ti. Adhivāsesi bhagavā tuṇhībhāvena. Atha kho keṇiyo jaṭilo bhagavato adhivāsanaṃ viditvā uṭṭhāyāsanā pakkāmi. Atha kho bhagavā etasmiṃ nidāne etasmiṃ pakaraṇe dhammiṃ kathaṃ katvā bhikkhū āmantesi – ‘‘anujānāmi, bhikkhave, aṭṭha pānāni – ambapānaṃ jambupānaṃ cocapānaṃ mocapānaṃ madhūkapānaṃ [madhupānaṃ (sī. syā.)] muddikapānaṃ sālūkapānaṃ phārusakapānaṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, sabbaṃ phalarasaṃ ṭhapetvā dhaññaphalarasaṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, sabbaṃ pattarasaṃ ṭhapetvā ḍākarasaṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, sabbaṃ puppharasaṃ ṭhapetvā madhūkapuppharasaṃ. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, ucchurasa’’nti.

300.Then the Blessed One, traveling by stages, arrived at Āpaṇa. The matted-hair ascetic Keṇiya heard: “Indeed, the ascetic Gotama, the son of the Sakyans, who has gone forth from the Sakyan clan, has arrived at Āpaṇa. A good report about Master Gotama has spread thus: ‘That Blessed One is perfected, a fully awakened Buddha, accomplished in knowledge and conduct, holy, knower of the world, supreme guide for those who wish to train, teacher of gods and humans, awakened, blessed.’ It is good to see such perfected ones.” Then the matted-hair ascetic Keṇiya thought: “What should I offer to the ascetic Gotama?” Then the matted-hair ascetic Keṇiya thought: “Those ancient seers among the brahmins, the makers of mantras, the expounders of mantras, whose ancient mantras are now chanted, pronounced, and collected by the brahmins—such as Aṭṭhaka, Vāmaka, Vāmadeva, Vessāmitta, Yamataggi, Aṅgīrasa, Bhāradvāja, Vāseṭṭha, Kassapa, and Bhagu—they abstained from food at night, refrained from eating at improper times, and they enjoyed such drinks. The ascetic Gotama also abstains from food at night, refrains from eating at improper times. The ascetic Gotama is worthy to enjoy such drinks.” Having prepared abundant drinks and, having had them taken in pots, he approached the Blessed One. Having approached, he exchanged greetings with the Blessed One, and when the courteous and amiable talk was finished, he stood to one side. Standing to one side, the matted-hair ascetic Keṇiya said to the Blessed One: “May Master Gotama accept this drink.” [The Blessed One said:] “Then, Keṇiya, give it to the monks.” So the matted-hair ascetic Keṇiya gave it to the monks. The monks, being scrupulous, did not accept it. [The Blessed One said:] “Accept it, monks, and consume it.” Then the matted-hair ascetic Keṇiya personally served and satisfied the community of monks headed by the Buddha with abundant drinks. When the Blessed One had washed his hands and put aside his bowl, he sat down to one side. Sitting to one side, the Blessed One instructed, encouraged, inspired, and gladdened the matted-hair ascetic Keṇiya with a Dhamma talk. Then the matted-hair ascetic Keṇiya, having been instructed, encouraged, inspired, and gladdened by the Blessed One’s Dhamma talk, said to him: “May Master Gotama together with the community of monks accept tomorrow’s meal from me.” [The Blessed One said:] “The community of monks is large, Keṇiya, consisting of twelve hundred and fifty monks, and you are devoted to the brahmins.” A second time, the matted-hair ascetic Keṇiya said to the Blessed One: “Even though, Master Gotama, the community of monks is large, consisting of twelve hundred and fifty monks, and I am devoted to the brahmins, may Master Gotama together with the community of monks accept tomorrow’s meal from me.” [The Blessed One said:] “The community of monks is large, Keṇiya, consisting of twelve hundred and fifty monks, and you are devoted to the brahmins.” A third time, the matted-hair ascetic Keṇiya said to the Blessed One: “Even though, Master Gotama, the community of monks is large, consisting of twelve hundred and fifty monks, and I am devoted to the brahmins, may Master Gotama together with the community of monks accept tomorrow’s meal from me.” The Blessed One consented by silence. Then the matted-hair ascetic Keṇiya, understanding the Blessed One’s consent, rose from his seat and left. Then the Blessed One, on this occasion, having given a Dhamma talk, addressed the monks: “Monks, I allow eight kinds of drinks: mango drink, rose-apple drink, banana drink, plantain drink, Madhuka drink, grape drink, lotus-stalk drink, and phārusaka drink. I allow all fruit juices except grain-based juices. I allow all leaf juices except ḍāka juice. I allow all flower juices except Madhuka flower juice. I allow sugarcane juice.”

Atha kho keṇiyo jaṭilo tassā rattiyā accayena sake assame paṇītaṃ khādanīyaṃ bhojanīyaṃ paṭiyādāpetvā bhagavato kālaṃ ārocāpesi – ‘‘kālo, bho gotama, niṭṭhitaṃ bhatta’’nti. Atha kho bhagavā pubbaṇhasamayaṃ nivāsetvā pattacīvaramādāya yena keṇiyassa jaṭilassa assamo tenupasaṅkami; upasaṅkamitvā paññatte āsane nisīdi saddhiṃ bhikkhusaṅghena. Atha kho keṇiyo jaṭilo buddhappamukhaṃ bhikkhusaṅghaṃ paṇītena khādanīyena bhojanīyena sahatthā santappetvā sampavāretvā bhagavantaṃ bhuttāviṃ onītapattapāṇiṃ ekamantaṃ nisīdi. Ekamantaṃ nisinnaṃ kho keṇiyaṃ jaṭilaṃ bhagavā imāhi gāthāhi anumodi –

Then, when the night had passed, the matted-hair ascetic Keṇiya had fine food, both hard and soft, prepared in his own hermitage and announced the time to the Blessed One: “It is time, Venerable Gotama, the meal is ready.” Then the Blessed One, having dressed in the morning, took his bowl and robe and went to the hermitage of the matted-hair ascetic Keṇiya. Having arrived, he sat down on the prepared seat together with the community of monks. Then the matted-hair ascetic Keṇiya personally served and satisfied the community of monks headed by the Buddha with fine food, both hard and soft. When the Blessed One had finished eating and had set aside his bowl, Keṇiya sat down to one side. Sitting to one side, the Blessed One expressed his appreciation to the matted-hair ascetic Keṇiya with these verses:

‘‘Aggihuttamukhā yaññā, sāvittī chandaso mukhaṃ;Rājā mukhaṃ manussānaṃ, nadīnaṃ sāgaro mukhaṃ.

“The fire offering is the chief of sacrifices, the Sāvitrī is the chief of meters; the king is the chief of men, the ocean is the chief of rivers.

‘‘Nakkhattānaṃ mukhaṃ cando, ādicco tapataṃ mukhaṃ;Puññaṃ ākaṅkhamānānaṃ saṅgho, ve yajataṃ mukha’’nti.

The moon is the foremost of the stars, the sun is the foremost of those that heat; for those desiring merit, the community is the foremost of sacrificers.”

Atha kho bhagavā keṇiyaṃ jaṭilaṃ imāhi gāthāhi anumoditvā uṭṭhāyāsanā pakkāmi.

Then the Blessed One, having expressed his appreciation to the matted-hair ascetic Keṇiya with these verses, rose from his seat and departed.

Keṇiyajaṭilavatthu niṭṭhitaṃ.

The account of the ascetic Keṇiya with matted hair is concluded.

### 183. Rojamallavatthu ^24

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv6-brahmali-pali#^24|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch5|BMC Chapter 5]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-MV6.24" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


183.The account of Roja the Malla.

301. Atha kho bhagavā āpaṇe yathābhirantaṃ viharitvā yena kusinārā tena cārikaṃ pakkāmi mahatā bhikkhusaṅghena saddhiṃ aḍḍhatelasehi bhikkhusatehi. Assosuṃ kho kosinārakā mallā – ‘‘bhagavā kira kusināraṃ āgacchati mahatā bhikkhusaṅghena saddhiṃ aḍḍhatelasehi bhikkhusatehī’’ti. Te saṅgaraṃ [saṅkaraṃ (ka.)] akaṃsu – ‘‘yo bhagavato paccuggamanaṃ na karissati, pañcasatānissa daṇḍo’’ti. Tena kho pana samayena rojo mallo āyasmato ānandassa sahāyo hoti. Atha kho bhagavā anupubbena cārikaṃ caramāno yena kusinārā tadavasari. Atha kho kosinārakā mallā bhagavato paccuggamanaṃ akaṃsu. Atha kho rojo mallo bhagavato paccuggamanaṃ karitvā yenāyasmā ānando tenupasaṅkami, upasaṅkamitvā āyasmantaṃ ānandaṃ abhivādetvā ekamantaṃ aṭṭhāsi. Ekamantaṃ ṭhitaṃ kho rojaṃ mallaṃ āyasmā ānando etadavoca – ‘‘uḷāraṃ kho te idaṃ, āvuso roja, yaṃ tvaṃ bhagavato paccuggamanaṃ akāsī’’ti. ‘‘Nāhaṃ, bhante ānanda, bahukato buddhe vā dhamme vā saṅghe vā; api ca ñātīhi saṅgaro kato – ‘yo bhagavato paccuggamanaṃ na karissati, pañcasatānissa daṇḍo’’’ti; so kho ahaṃ, bhante ānanda, ñātīnaṃ daṇḍabhayā evāhaṃ bhagavato paccuggamanaṃ akāsinti. Atha kho āyasmā ānando anattamano ahosi’ kathañhi nāma rojo mallo evaṃ vakkhatī’ti? Atha kho āyasmā ānando yena bhagavā tenupasaṅkami, upasaṅkamitvā bhagavantaṃ abhivādetvā ekamantaṃ nisīdi. Ekamantaṃ nisinno kho āyasmā ānando bhagavantaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘ayaṃ, bhante, rojo mallo abhiññāto ñātamanusso. Mahatthiko kho pana evarūpānaṃ ñātamanussānaṃ imasmiṃ dhammavinaye pasādo. Sādhu, bhante, bhagavā tathā karotu, yathā rojo mallo imasmiṃ dhammavinaye pasīdeyyā’’ti. ‘‘Na kho taṃ, ānanda, dukkaraṃ tathāgatena, yathā rojo mallo imasmiṃ dhammavinaye pasīdeyyā’’ti.

301.Then the Blessed One, having stayed at Āpaṇa as long as he pleased, set out on a journey to Kusinārā with a large company of bhikkhus, with one thousand two hundred and fifty bhikkhus. The Mallas of Kusinārā heard: “The Blessed One is coming to Kusinārā with a large company of bhikkhus, with one thousand two hundred and fifty bhikkhus.” They made a proclamation: “Whoever does not go out to meet the Blessed One will be fined five hundred kahāpaṇas.” Now at that time, Roja the Mallan was a friend of the Venerable Ānanda. Then the Blessed One, traveling by stages, arrived at Kusinārā. Then the Mallas of Kusinārā went out to meet the Blessed One. Then Roja the Mallan, having gone out to meet the Blessed One, approached the Venerable Ānanda, paid homage to him, and stood to one side. Standing to one side, the Venerable Ānanda said to Roja the Mallan: “It is a great thing indeed, friend Roja, that you went out to meet the Blessed One.” “I, Venerable Ānanda, am not one who is greatly devoted to the Buddha, the Dhamma, or the Saṅgha. But my relatives made a proclamation: ‘Whoever does not go out to meet the Blessed One will be fined five hundred kahāpaṇas.’ So, Venerable Ānanda, out of fear of the fine from my relatives, I went out to meet the Blessed One.” Then the Venerable Ānanda was displeased, thinking: “How could Roja the Mallan say such a thing?” Then the Venerable Ānanda approached the Blessed One, paid homage to him, and sat down to one side. Sitting to one side, the Venerable Ānanda said to the Blessed One: “This Roja the Mallan, Bhante, is a well-known kinsman. It is of great importance that such well-known kinsmen gain confidence in this Dhamma and Discipline. It would be good, Bhante, if the Blessed One would act in such a way that Roja the Mallan might gain confidence in this Dhamma and Discipline.” “It is not difficult, Ānanda, for the Tathāgata to act in such a way that Roja the Mallan might gain confidence in this Dhamma and Discipline.”

Atha kho bhagavā rojaṃ mallaṃ mettena cittena pharitvā uṭṭhāyāsanā vihāraṃ pāvisi. Atha kho rojo mallo bhagavato mettena cittena phuṭṭho, seyyathāpi nāma gāviṃ taruṇavaccho, evameva, vihārena vihāraṃ pariveṇena pariveṇaṃ upasaṅkamitvā bhikkhū pucchati – ‘‘kahaṃ nu kho, bhante, etarahi so bhagavā viharati arahaṃ sammāsambuddho, dassanakāmā hi mayaṃ taṃ bhagavantaṃ arahantaṃ sammāsambuddha’’nti. ‘‘Esāvuso roja, vihāro saṃvutadvāro, tena appasaddo upasaṅkamitvā ataramāno āḷindaṃ pavisitvā ukkāsitvā aggaḷaṃ ākoṭehi, vivarissati te bhagavā dvāra’’nti. Atha kho rojo mallo yena so vihāro saṃvutadvāro, tena appasaddo upasaṅkamitvā ataramāno āḷindaṃ pavisitvā ukkāsitvā aggaḷaṃ ākoṭesi. Vivari bhagavā dvāraṃ. Atha kho rojo mallo vihāraṃ pavisitvā bhagavantaṃ abhivādetvā ekamantaṃ nisīdi. Ekamantaṃ nisinnassa kho rojassa mallassa bhagavā anupubbiṃ kathaṃ kathesi, seyyathidaṃ – dānakathaṃ…pe… aparappaccayo satthusāsane bhagavantaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘sādhu, bhante, ayyā mamaññeva paṭiggaṇheyyuṃ cīvarapiṇḍapātasenāsanagilānappaccayabhesajjaparikkhāraṃ, no aññesa’’nti. ‘‘Yesaṃ kho, roja, sekkhena ñāṇena sekkhena dassanena dhammo diṭṭho seyyathāpi tayā, tesampi evaṃ hoti – ‘aho nūna ayyā amhākaññeva paṭiggaṇheyyuṃ cīvarapiṇḍapātasenāsanagilānappaccayabhesajjaparikkhāraṃ, no aññesa’nti. Tena hi, roja, tava ceva paṭiggahissanti aññesañcā’’ti.

Then the Blessed One, having suffused Roja the Malla with a mind of loving-kindness, rose from his seat and entered his dwelling. Then Roja the Malla, touched by the Blessed One’s mind of loving-kindness, just as a young calf [follows its mother cow,] so too he went from dwelling to dwelling, from enclosure to enclosure, asking the monks: “Venerable sirs, where is the Blessed One, the Arahant, the Perfectly Enlightened One, staying now? For I wish to see that Blessed One, Arahant, Perfectly Enlightened One.” “That, friend Roja, is the dwelling with the door closed. Approach it quietly, without haste. Enter the verandah, clear your throat, and knock on the latch. The Blessed One will open the door for you.” Then Roja the Malla approached that closed-door dwelling quietly, without haste. He entered the verandah, cleared his throat, and knocked on the latch. The Blessed One opened the door. Then Roja the Mallan entered the dwelling, paid homage to the Blessed One, and sat down to one side. As he sat to one side, the Blessed One gave Roja the Malla a progressive talk, that is, a talk on generosity, on morality, on the heavens, on the drawbacks, degradation, and defilement of sensual pleasures, and on the benefits of renunciation. When the Blessed One knew that Roja the Malla’s mind was ready, pliable, free from hindrances, uplifted, and confident, he then expounded to him the Dhamma-talk special to the Buddhas: suffering, its origin, its cessation, and the path. Just as a clean cloth, free of stains, would readily absorb dye, so too, as Roja the Malla sat there, the dust-free, stainless Eye of Dhamma arose in him: “Whatever is subject to origination is subject to cessation.” Then Roja the Malla, having seen the Dhamma, attained the Dhamma, understood the Dhamma, penetrated the Dhamma, having overcome doubt, having dispelled uncertainty, having gained full confidence in the Teacher’s instruction, without relying on others, said to the Blessed One: “Excellent, venerable sir! May the venerable ones accept robes, almsfood, lodging, and medicinal requisites only from me, and not from others.” “Roja, those who have seen the Dhamma with the trainee's knowledge and the trainee's vision—as you have—also think thus: ‘If only the venerable ones would accept robes, almsfood, lodging, and medicinal requisites only from us, and not from others.’ Therefore, Roja, they will accept from you as well as from others.”

302. Tena kho pana samayena kusinārāyaṃ paṇītānaṃ bhattānaṃ bhattapaṭipāṭi aṭṭhitā hoti. Atha kho rojassa mallassa paṭipāṭiṃ alabhantassa etadahosi – ‘‘yaṃnūnāhaṃ bhattaggaṃ olokeyyaṃ, yaṃ bhattagge nāssa, taṃ paṭiyādeyya’’nti. Atha kho rojo mallo bhattaggaṃ olokento dve nāddasa – ḍākañca piṭṭhakhādanīyañca. Atha kho rojo mallo yenāyasmā ānando tenupasaṅkami; upasaṅkamitvā āyasmantaṃ ānandaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘idha me, bhante ānanda, paṭipāṭiṃ alabhantassa etadahosi – ‘yaṃnūnāhaṃ bhattaggaṃ olokeyyaṃ, yaṃ bhattagge nāssa, taṃ paṭiyādeyya’nti. So kho ahaṃ, bhante ānanda, bhattaggaṃ olokento dve nāddasaṃ – ḍākañca piṭṭhakhādanīyañca. Sacāhaṃ, bhante ānanda, paṭiyādeyyaṃ ḍākañca piṭṭhakhādanīyañca, paṭiggaṇheyya me bhagavā’’ti? ‘‘Tena hi, roja, bhagavantaṃ paṭipucchissāmī’’ti. Atha kho āyasmā ānando bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesi. ‘‘Tena hānanda, paṭiyādetū’’ti. ‘‘Tena hi, roja, paṭiyādehī’’ti. Atha kho rojo mallo tassā rattiyā accayena pahūtaṃ ḍākañca piṭṭhakhādanīyañca paṭiyādāpetvā bhagavato upanāmesi ‘‘paṭiggaṇhātu me, bhante, bhagavā ḍākañca piṭṭhakhādanīyañcā’’ti. ‘‘Tena hi, roja, bhikkhūnaṃ dehī’’ti. Atha kho rojo mallo bhikkhūnaṃ deti. Bhikkhū kukkuccāyantā na paṭiggaṇhanti. ‘‘Paṭiggaṇhatha, bhikkhave, paribhuñjathā’’ti. Atha kho rojo mallo buddhappamukhaṃ bhikkhusaṅghaṃ pahūtehi ḍākehi ca piṭṭhakhādanīyehi ca sahatthā santappetvā sampavāretvā bhagavantaṃ dhotahatthaṃ onītapattapāṇiṃ ekamantaṃ nisīdi. Ekamantaṃ nisinnaṃ kho rojaṃ mallaṃ bhagavā dhammiyā kathāya sandassetvā samādapetvā samuttejetvā sampahaṃsetvā uṭṭhāyāsanā pakkāmi. Atha kho bhagavā etasmiṃ nidāne etasmiṃ pakaraṇe dhammiṃ kathaṃ katvā bhikkhū āmantesi – ‘‘anujānāmi, bhikkhave, sabbañca ḍākaṃ sabbañca piṭṭhakhādanīya’’nti.

302.Now at that time in Kusinārā there was a regular distribution of excellent food. Then the Malla named Roja, not receiving his turn, thought: “Why don't I inspect the refectory? Whatever is lacking there, I will prepare.” Then the Malla Roja, inspecting the refectory, did not see two things: ḍāka and flour-based foods. Then the Malla Roja approached the Venerable Ānanda and said: “Venerable Ānanda, not receiving my turn, I thought: ‘Why don't I inspect the refectory? Whatever is lacking there, I will prepare.’ Venerable Ānanda, inspecting the refectory, I did not see two things: ḍāka and flour-based foods. If I were to prepare ḍāka and flour-based foods, would the Blessed One accept it from me?” “Well then, Roja, I will ask the Blessed One.” Then the Venerable Ānanda informed the Blessed One of the matter. “Well then, Ānanda, let him prepare it.” “Well then, Roja, prepare it.” Then the Malla Roja, after the night had passed, had a large quantity of ḍāka and flour-based foods prepared and offered it to the Blessed One, saying: “Venerable sir, may the Blessed One accept ḍāka and flour-based foods from me.” “Well then, Roja, give it to the monks.” Then the Malla Roja gave it to the monks. The monks, being scrupulous, did not accept it. “Accept, monks, and eat.” Then the Malla Roja, having personally served and satisfied the Saṅgha of monks headed by the Buddha with abundant ḍāka and flour-based foods, sat down to one side while the Blessed One washed his hands and put away his bowl. Sitting to one side, the Blessed One instructed, encouraged, inspired, and gladdened the Malla Roja with a Dhamma talk, then rose from his seat and departed. Then the Blessed One, on this occasion, having given a Dhamma talk, addressed the monks: “Monks, I allow all ḍāka and all flour-based foods.”

Rojamallavatthu niṭṭhitaṃ.

The story of Roja the Malla is concluded.

### 184. Vuḍḍhapabbajitavatthu ^25

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv6-brahmali-pali#^25|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch5|BMC Chapter 5]] and the following cites:
>

> "VIN-MV6.25" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


184.The Story of the Elder Renunciant

303. Atha kho bhagavā kusinārāyaṃ yathābhirantaṃ viharitvā yena ātumā tena cārikaṃ pakkāmi mahatā bhikkhusaṅghena saddhiṃ aḍḍhatelasehi bhikkhusatehi. Tena kho pana samayena aññataro vuḍḍhapabbajito ātumāyaṃ paṭivasati nahāpitapubbo. Tassa dve dārakā honti, mañjukā paṭibhāneyyakā, dakkhā pariyodātasippā sake ācariyake nahāpitakamme. Assosi kho so vuḍḍhapabbajito – ‘‘bhagavā kira ātumaṃ āgacchati mahatā bhikkhusaṅghena saddhiṃ aḍḍhatelasehi bhikkhusatehī’’ti. Atha kho so vuḍḍhapabbajito te dārake etadavoca – ‘‘bhagavā kira, tātā, ātumaṃ āgacchati mahatā bhikkhusaṅghena saddhiṃ aḍḍhatelasehi bhikkhusatehi. Gacchatha tumhe, tātā, khurabhaṇḍaṃ ādāya nāḷiyāvāpakena anugharakaṃ anugharakaṃ āhiṇḍatha, loṇampi, telampi, taṇḍulampi, khādanīyampi saṃharatha, bhagavato āgatassa yāgupānaṃ karissāmā’’ti. ‘‘Evaṃ, tātā’’ti kho te dārakā tassa vuḍḍhapabbajitassa paṭissuṇitvā khurabhaṇḍaṃ ādāya nāḷiyāvāpakena anugharakaṃ anugharakaṃ āhiṇḍanti, loṇampi, telampi, taṇḍulampi, khādanīyampi saṃharantā. Manussā te dārake mañjuke paṭibhāneyyake passitvā yepi na kārāpetukāmā tepi kārāpenti, kārāpetvāpi bahuṃ denti. Atha kho te dārakā bahuṃ loṇampi, telampi, taṇḍulampi, khādanīyampi saṃhariṃsu.

303.Then the Blessed One, having stayed at Kusinārā as long as he pleased, set out on a tour towards Ātumā with a large Sangha of bhikkhus, numbering twelve hundred and fifty. Now at that time, a certain elder renunciant, formerly a barber, was residing in Ātumā. He had two sons, sweet-voiced and ingenious, skillful and with perfected craft in their own master's barbering. That elder renunciant heard: “The Blessed One, it is said, is coming to Ātumā with a large Sangha of bhikkhus, numbering twelve hundred and fifty.” Then that elder renunciant said to those boys: “Dear sons, the Blessed One, it is said, is coming to Ātumā with a large Sangha of bhikkhus, numbering twelve hundred and fifty. Go, dear sons, take your barber’s tools and a collection container, and wander from house to house, collecting salt, oil, rice, and edibles. We will prepare gruel and drink for the Blessed One when he arrives.” “Yes, father,” replied the boys to that elder renunciant. Taking their barber’s tools and a collection container, they wandered from house to house, collecting salt, oil, rice, and edibles. People, seeing those sweet-voiced and ingenious boys, even those who did not wish to have their services done, had them done, and after having them done, gave them much. Thus, the boys gathered a great deal of salt, oil, rice, and edibles.

Atha kho bhagavā anupubbena cārikaṃ caramāno yena ātumā tadavasari. Tatra sudaṃ bhagavā ātumāyaṃ viharati bhusāgāre. Atha kho so vuḍḍhapabbajito tassā rattiyā accayena pahūtaṃ yāguṃ paṭiyādāpetvā bhagavato upanāmesi – ‘‘paṭiggaṇhātu me, bhante, bhagavā yāgu’’nti. Jānantāpi tathāgatā pucchanti…pe… sāvakānaṃ vā sikkhāpadaṃ paññapessāmāti. Atha kho bhagavā taṃ vuḍḍhapabbajitaṃ etadavoca – ‘‘kutāyaṃ, bhikkhu yāgū’’ti? Atha kho so vuḍḍhapabbajito bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesi. Vigarahi buddho bhagavā, ‘‘ananucchavikaṃ, moghapurisa, ananulomikaṃ appatirūpaṃ assāmaṇakaṃ akappiyaṃ akaraṇīyaṃ. Kathañhi nāma tvaṃ, moghapurisa, pabbajito akappiye samādapessasi [samādapesi (ka.)]. Netaṃ, moghapurisa, appasannānaṃ vā pasādāya…pe… vigarahitvā dhammiṃ kathaṃ katvā bhikkhū āmantesi ‘na, bhikkhave, pabbajitena akappiye samādapetabbaṃ, yo samādapeyya, āpatti dukkaṭassa. Na ca, bhikkhave, nahāpitapubbena khurabhaṇḍaṃ pariharitabbaṃ. Yo parihareyya, āpatti dukkaṭassā’’’ti.

Then the Blessed One, traveling by stages, arrived at Ātumā. There the Blessed One stayed at the threshing hall in Ātumā. Now, that elder renunciant, after the night had passed, had a large quantity of gruel prepared and offered it to the Blessed One, saying, “Venerable sir, may the Blessed One accept this gruel from me.” Even though the Tathāgatas know, they ask…or they will lay down a training rule for the disciples. Then the Blessed One said to that elder renunciant, “Monk, where did this gruel come from?” Then that elder renunciant told the Blessed One the matter. The Blessed One rebuked him: “It is unseemly, foolish man, unsuitable, inappropriate, unbecoming for a recluse, impermissible, not to be done. How could you, foolish man, as one gone forth, encourage what is impermissible? This is not, foolish man, for inspiring confidence in those without it…” Having rebuked him and given a Dhamma talk, the Blessed One addressed the bhikkhus: “Monks, one who has gone forth should not encourage what is impermissible. Whoever encourages it commits an offense of wrong-doing. And, monks, one who formerly was a barber should not carry barber’s tools. Whoever carries them commits an offense of wrong-doing.”

Atha kho bhagavā ātumāyaṃ yathābhirantaṃ viharitvā yena sāvatthi tena cārikaṃ pakkāmi. Anupubbena cārikaṃ caramāno yena sāvatthi tadavasari. Tatra sudaṃ bhagavā sāvatthiyaṃ viharati jetavane anāthapiṇḍikassa ārāme. Tena kho pana samayena sāvatthiyaṃ bahuṃ phalakhādanīyaṃ uppannaṃ hoti. Atha kho bhikkhūnaṃ etadahosi – ‘‘kiṃ nu kho bhagavatā phalakhādanīyaṃ anuññātaṃ, kiṃ ananuññāta’’nti? Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. ‘‘Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, sabbaṃ phalakhādanīya’’nti.

Then the Blessed One, having stayed at Ātumā as long as he pleased, set out on a tour towards Sāvatthī. Traveling by stages, he arrived at Sāvatthī. There the Blessed One stayed in Jeta’s Grove, Anāthapiṇḍika’s Park. Now at that time in Sāvatthī, much fruit and edibles had arisen. Then the bhikkhus thought: “What fruit and edibles has the Blessed One allowed, and what has he not allowed?” They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “I allow, bhikkhus, all fruit and edibles.”

304. Tena kho pana samayena saṅghikāni bījāni puggalikāya bhūmiyā ropiyanti, puggalikāni bījāni saṅghikāya bhūmiyā ropiyanti. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. Saṅghikāni, bhikkhave, bījāni puggalikāya bhūmiyā ropitāni bhāgaṃ datvā paribhuñjitabbāni. Puggalikāni bījāni saṅghikāya bhūmiyā ropitāni bhāgaṃ datvā paribhuñjitabbānīti.

304.Now at that time, communal seeds were being planted in private fields, and private seeds were being planted in communal fields. They reported this matter to the Blessed One. “Monks, communal seeds planted in private fields are to be consumed after giving a share. Private seeds planted in communal fields are to be consumed after giving a share.”

Vuḍḍhapabbajitavatthu niṭṭhitaṃ.

The Story of the Elder Renunciant is concluded.

### 185. Catumahāpadesakathā ^26

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv6-brahmali-pali#^26|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch5|BMC Chapter 5]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-MV6.26" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


185.The Discourse on the Four Great References

305. Tena kho pana samayena bhikkhūnaṃ kismiñci kismiñci ṭhāne kukkuccaṃ uppajjati – ‘‘kiṃ nu kho bhagavatā anuññātaṃ, kiṃ ananuññāta’’nti? Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. ‘‘Yaṃ, bhikkhave, mayā ‘idaṃ na kappatī’ti appaṭikkhittaṃ tañce akappiyaṃ anulometi, kappiyaṃ paṭibāhati, taṃ vo na kappati. Yaṃ, bhikkhave, mayā ‘idaṃ na kappatī’ti appaṭikkhittaṃ tañce kappiyaṃ anulometi, akappiyaṃ paṭibāhati, taṃ vo kappati. Yaṃ, bhikkhave, mayā ‘idaṃ kappatī’ti ananuññātaṃ tañce akappiyaṃ anulometi, kappiyaṃ paṭibāhati, taṃ vo na kappati. Yaṃ, bhikkhave, mayā ‘idaṃ kappatī’ti ananuññātaṃ, tañce kappiyaṃ anulometi, akappiyaṃ paṭibāhati, taṃ vo kappatī’’ti.

305.Now at that time, doubts arose in the monks in various places, wondering: "What has the Blessed One allowed? What has he not allowed?" They reported this matter to the Blessed One. [He replied:] "Monks, whatever I have not forbidden by saying, 'This is not allowable,' if it accords with what is unallowable and opposes what is allowable, that is not allowable for you. Monks, whatever I have not forbidden by saying, 'This is not allowable,' if it accords with what is allowable and opposes what is unallowable, that is allowable for you. Monks, whatever I have not allowed by saying, 'This is allowable,' if it accords with what is unallowable and opposes what is allowable, that is not allowable for you. Monks, whatever I have not allowed by saying, 'This is allowable,' if it accords with what is allowable and opposes what is unallowable, that is allowable for you."

Atha kho bhikkhūnaṃ etadahosi – ‘‘kappati nu kho yāvakālikena yāmakālikaṃ, na nu kho kappati? Kappati nu kho yāvakālikena sattāhakālikaṃ, na nu kho kappati? Kappati nu kho yāvakālikena yāvajīvikaṃ, na nu kho kappati? Kappati nu kho yāmakālikena sattāhakālikaṃ, na nu kho kappati? Kappati nu kho yāmakālikena yāvajīvikaṃ, na nu kho kappati? Kappati nu kho sattāhakālikena yāvajīvikaṃ, na nu kho kappatī’’ti? Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. ‘‘Yāvakālikena, bhikkhave, yāmakālikaṃ, tadahu paṭiggahitaṃ kāle kappati, vikāle na kappati. Yāvakālikena, bhikkhave, sattāhakālikaṃ, tadahu paṭiggahitaṃ kāle kappati, vikāle na kappati. Yāvakālikena, bhikkhave, yāvajīvikaṃ, tadahu paṭiggahitaṃ kāle kappati, vikāle na kappati. Yāmakālikena, bhikkhave, sattāhakālikaṃ, tadahu paṭiggahitaṃ yāme kappati, yāmātikkante na kappati. Yāmakālikena, bhikkhave, yāvajīvikaṃ, tadahu paṭiggahitaṃ yāme kappati, yāmātikkante na kappati. Sattāhakālikena, bhikkhave, yāvajīvikaṃ paṭiggahitaṃ, sattāhaṃ kappati, sattāhātikkante na kappatī’’ti.

Then the monks thought: "Is it allowable to use what is allowable for a limited time for what is allowable for a watch, or is it not allowable? Is it allowable to use what is allowable for a limited time for what is allowable for a week, or is it not allowable? Is it allowable to use what is allowable for a limited time for what is allowable for life, or is it not allowable? Is it allowable to use what is allowable for a watch for what is allowable for a week, or is it not allowable? Is it allowable to use what is allowable for a watch for what is allowable for life, or is it not allowable? Is it allowable to use what is allowable for a week for what is allowable for life, or is it not allowable?" They reported this matter to the Blessed One. "Monks, when what is allowable for a limited time is used for what is allowable for a watch, if it is received on that day, it is allowable at the (proper) time but not at the improper time. Monks, when what is allowable for a limited time is used for what is allowable for a week, if it is received on that day, it is allowable at the (proper) time but not at the improper time. Monks, when what is allowable for a limited time is used for what is allowable for life, if it is received on that day, it is allowable at the (proper) time but not at the improper time. Monks, when what is allowable for a watch is used for what is allowable for a week, if it is received on that day, it is allowable during the watch but not after the watch has passed. Monks, when what is allowable for a watch is used for what is allowable for life, if it is received on that day, it is allowable during the watch but not after the watch has passed. Monks, when what is allowable for a week is received for what is allowable for life, it is allowable for seven days but not after the seven days have passed."

Catumahāpadesakathā niṭṭhitā.

The discourse on the four great references is concluded.

Bhesajjakkhandhako chaṭṭho.

The sixth chapter is the Bhesajjakkhandhaka.

### 186. Tassuddānaṃ ^27

> [!TIP]- Links to [[mv6-brahmali-pali#^27|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch5|BMC Chapter 5]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-MV6.27" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


186.Its summary.

Sāradike vikālepi, vasaṃ mūle piṭṭhehi ca;Kasāvehi paṇṇaṃ phalaṃ, jatu loṇaṃ chakaṇañca.

Autumnal, even at the improper time; fat, root, and with flour; with astringents, leaves, fruit, lac, salt, and cow dung.

Cuṇṇaṃ cālini maṃsañca, añjanaṃ upapisanī [upapiṃ sanī (sī.), upapiṃ sanaṃ (syā.)];Añjanī uccāpārutā, salākā salākaṭhāniṃ [salākodhanī (sī. syā.)].

Powder, sieve, and flesh; collyrium, whetstone; collyrium pot uncovered; probe, probe holder.

Thavikaṃsabaddhakaṃ suttaṃ, muddhanitelanatthu ca;Natthukaraṇī dhūmañca, nettañcāpidhanatthavi.

Bag, binding, thread; oil for the head, and snuff; snuff-tube, and smoke; eye-covering and bag.

Telapākesu majjañca, atikkhittaṃ abbhañjanaṃ;Tumbaṃ sedaṃ sambhārañca, mahā bhaṅgodakaṃ tathā.

In oil preparations, and intoxicants; excessive anointing; gourd, sweat, and provisions; and also great bhang-water.

Dakakoṭṭhaṃ lohitañca, visāṇaṃ pādabbhañjanaṃ;Pajjaṃ satthaṃ kasāvañca, tilakakkaṃ kabaḷikaṃ.

Water container, and blood; horn, foot-anointing; foot-water, knife, and astringent; sesame-cake, morsel.

Coḷaṃ sāsapakuṭṭañca, dhūma sakkharikāya ca;Vaṇatelaṃ vikāsikaṃ, vikaṭañca paṭiggahaṃ.

Cloth, and mustard powder; smoke, and with sugar; wound oil, eruption; and deformed acceptance.

Gūthaṃ karonto loḷiñca, khāraṃ muttaharītakaṃ;Gandhā virecanañceva, acchākaṭaṃ kaṭākaṭaṃ.

Feces, doing, and agitation; alkali, urine-haritaki; odors, and purgatives; fresh-cut, cut-cut.

Paṭicchādani pabbhārā, ārāma sattāhena ca;Guḷaṃ muggaṃ sovīrañca, sāmaṃpākā punāpace.

Covering, cave; monastery, and for seven days; jaggery, green gram, and sour gruel; self-cooked, again and again.

Punānuññāsi dubbhikkhe, phalañca tilakhādanī;Purebhattaṃ kāyaḍāho, nibbattañca bhagandalaṃ.

Again allowed in famine; and fruit, sesame-eating; before meal, body burning; and arisen fistula.

Vatthikammañca suppiñca, manussamaṃsameva ca;Hatthiassā sunakho ca, ahi sīhañca dīpikaṃ [hatthiassasunakhāhi, sīhabyagghañca dīpikaṃ (sī.)].

Enema, and winnowing basket; and indeed human flesh; elephant, horse, and dog; snake, and lion, leopard.

Acchataracchamaṃsañca, paṭipāṭi ca yāgu ca;Taruṇaṃ aññatra guḷaṃ, sunidhāvasathāgāraṃ.

Bear and hyena flesh; and in order, and gruel; tender, except jaggery; well-provided lodging house.

Gaṅgā koṭisaccakathā, ambapālī ca licchavī;Uddissa kataṃ subhikkhaṃ, punadeva paṭikkhipi.

Ganges, discourse on a crore of truths; and Ambapālī, Licchavis; made with reference to abundance; again indeed forbidden.

Megho yaso meṇḍako, ca gorasaṃ pātheyyakena ca;Keṇi ambo jambu coca, mocamadhumuddikasālukaṃ.

Cloud, fame, ram, and; cow's milk, and with provisions for the journey; Keṇi, mango, rose apple, plantain; plantain, honey, grapes, lotus root.

Phārusakā ḍākapiṭṭhaṃ, ātumāyaṃ nahāpito;Sāvatthiyaṃ phalaṃ bījaṃ, kismiṃ ṭhāne ca kāliketi.

Phārusaka fruit, ḍāka-cake; in Ātumā, bathed; in Sāvatthī, fruit, seed; and in what place, and timely.

Imamhi khandhake vatthū ekasataṃ chavatthu.

In this chapter, there are one hundred and six subjects.

Bhesajjakkhandhako niṭṭhito.

The Chapter on Medicines is finished.
